Stray Camel Captured by Enemy: Ownership Transfer
Ruling on a stray animal captured by enemy

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that an owned animal straying into enemy territory and captured becomes the property of the captors, and explain the basis for ownership transfer.

Core Idea
If an owned animal strays into enemy territory and is captured, the enemy becomes its owner.

In the context of war and interactions with enemy territory, questions of ownership arise. This lesson clarifies a specific ruling: when a camel (or any owned animal) wanders off into the land of the enemy and they capture it, the enemy gains ownership. This contrasts with slaves who have a right to freedom; regular property follows capture.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act
The act is a camel straying (nad) into enemy territory (dar al-harb).
2
Identify the captors
The captors are the enemy (ahl al-harb) who take possession of the camel.
3
State the ruling
The enemy becomes the owner (maliku) upon capture. The ruling is straightforward: ownership transfers.
4
Note the contrast
This ruling is for regular property (like camels). It differs from slaves with impending freedom, whose status is protected.

Death in Dar al-Harb Before Division of Spoils: The Hanafi Ruling on Ihraz
Ruling on a fighter who dies before spoils transfer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on a fighter who dies before spoils are brought to Dar al-Islam, explain the role of ihraz in establishing ownership, and distinguish the Hanafi position from the Shafi'i view.

Core Idea
Ownership of spoils requires ihraz (secure possession) in Dar al-Islam; death before that forfeits the share.

This lesson examines the ruling on a fighter who dies before the spoils of war are transferred to Muslim territory. The Hanafi school denies a share, while the Shafi'i school grants it. We will explore the reasoning behind each view, focusing on the concept of ihraz and the practical difference (thamarah al-khilaf) between the two madhhabs.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario and Hanafi ruling
Read the passage to understand the exact situation: a fighter dies in Dar al-Harb before the spoils are brought to Dar al-Islam. According to Imam Abu Hanifa, he has no right to a share.
The ruling applies whether death occurs during battle or after battle but before transport.
2
Locate the key condition: ihraz
Identify that the Hanafi position hinges on the concept of ihraz (secure possession). Ownership of spoils is established only after the spoils are brought into Dar al-Islam. This is the condition for entitlement.
Hanafi: ihraz = transport to Dar al-Islam. Shafi'i: ihraz = end of battle.
3
Examine the Hanafi proof (dalil aqli)
The Hanafi argument uses analogy (qiyas) to a martyr killed during battle: such a martyr gets no share. Similarly, a fighter who dies before ihraz is like a martyr—he does not live to see the spoils collected, so no entitlement arises.
The underlying principle: right to spoils accrues only after the property is collected in Dar al-Islam.
4
Contrast the Shafi'i position
Imam al-Shafi'i holds that fighters become owners of the spoils as soon as the battle ends. Therefore, death after battle but before transport does not forfeit the share; his heirs inherit it.
Shafi'i: end of battle = instant ownership, regardless of location of spoils.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf (practical consequence)
The practical difference: if a fighter dies after battle but before spoils are moved to Dar al-Islam, Hanafi says his heirs get nothing; Shafi'i says they inherit his share. This affects estate distribution and the division of spoils.
The ikhtilaf is legitimate; the text follows the Hanafi view.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
[۳۰۲۷ (۴۸) ومـن مـات من الغانيمن في در الحرب فلا حق له في القسمة] ۳۰۲۷ (۴۸) مجاہد میں سے کوئی دار الحرب میں مرجائے تو تقسیم میں اس کا کوئی حق نہیں ہے۔ اگر جنگ کے درمیان کوئی شہید ہو گیا تو ان کو بالاتفاق حصہ نہیں ملے گا۔ اور اگر جنگ ختم ہونے کے بعد لیکن غنیمت کو دارالاسلام لانے سے پہلے کوئی انتقال کر گیا تو امام ابو حنیفہ کے نزدیک اس کو بھی غنیمت میں حصہ نہیں ملے گا۔ امام ابو حنیفہ کا مسلک یہ ہے کہ دارالاسلام میں احراز کے بعد مجاہد نقیمت کا مالک ہوتا ہے۔ اس لئے اس سے پہلے جو انتقال کر جائے اس کو مال غنیمت میں حصہ نہیں ملے گا۔ جس طرح جنگ کے دوران کوئی شہید ہو جائے اس کو حصہ نہیں ملتا ہے۔ اصول یہ مسئلہ اس اصول پر ہے کہ دارالاسلام میں مال جمع ہونے کے بعد مجاہد کا حق ہوتا ہے۔ امام شافعی فرماتے ہیں کہ جنگ ختم ہونے کے بعد جو مجاہد انتقال ہوئے ہیں ان کو بھی غنیمت میں حصہ ملے گا چاہے وہ دارالحرب میں ہی کیوں نہ ہو۔ اور دار الاسلام میں مال لانے سے پہلے کیوں نہ ہو۔ ان کا قاعدہ یہ ہے کہ جنگ ختم ہو جانے کے بعد مجاہدین غنیمت کے مالک ہو جاتے ہیں۔ ان کے یہاں جنگ ختم ہوتے ہی احراز ہو جاتا ہے۔
And whoever among the warriors dies in the abode of war has no right to a share in the division.
Source pages p. 282

Commentary
This passage presents a ruling from the Hanafi school on the distribution of spoils when a fighter dies. It states that if a fighter dies in Dar al-Harb (enemy territory) before the spoils are brought to Dar al-Islam, he has no share. The commentator explains that this applies whether he is martyred during battle or dies after the battle but before the spoils are transported. Imam Abu Hanifa's position is that ownership of spoils is established only after ihraz (secure possession) in Dar al-Islam. Before that, the fighter has no right. He draws an analogy to a martyr who dies during battle—no share. This is based on the principle that the right to spoils accrues only after the property is collected in Dar al-Islam. Imam Shafi'i disagrees, holding that fighters become owners as soon as the battle ends, regardless of location. Thus, according to Shafi'i, a fighter who dies after the battle has a right to a share, and his heirs inherit it. This ikhtilaf is noted but the text adheres to the Hanafi view.

Key Terms
غنيمت (ghanimah): Spoils of war taken from the enemy.
احراز (ihraz): Secure possession, i.e., bringing the spoils into Dar al-Islam.
دار الحرب (dar al-harb): Territory under non-Muslim control where hostilities are permitted.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Imam Abu Hanifa, when does a fighter become entitled to a share of the spoils?
A) As soon as the battle ends.
B) After the spoils are brought to Dar al-Islam.
C) After the spoils are distributed.
D) Only if he is alive at the time of division.

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, ownership of spoils requires physical transfer to Dar al-Islam; a fighter who dies before that point has no share.

Inheritance of Spoils After Death in Dar al-Islam
Ruling on a fighter who dies after spoils are brought to Dar al-Islam

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on a fighter who dies after spoils are brought to Dar al-Islam and explain the legal concept of ihraz that determines the share.

Core Idea
If a fighter dies after the spoils reach Dar al-Islam, his share is fixed and passes to his heirs.

In this lesson, we examine a specific scene in the law of ghanimah (spoils of war). The Hanafi school distinguishes between death before and after the spoils have been brought to Dar al-Islam (the abode of Islam), based on the concept of ihraz (secure possession). The passage clarifies that once the spoils are in Dar al-Islam, the fighters' ownership is established; therefore, a fighter who dies after that moment has a vested right that goes to his heirs.

Guided Path
1
State the ruling
Identify the explicit ruling: the share of a warrior who dies after the spoils are brought to Dar al-Islam is given to his heirs.
2
Identify the critical condition
Note that the timing of death relative to ihraz is decisive. Ihraz occurs when the spoils are brought into Dar al-Islam, establishing the fighters' ownership.
3
Explain the legal basis
The basis is that tamlik (ownership) is established at the moment of ihraz. Thus, the fighter's right becomes a property right that can be inherited.
4
Distinguish from the opposite case
If death occurs before ihraz (e.g., in the battlefield or during transport), no share is established; hence nothing passes to heirs.
This contrast highlights the importance of the condition.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
[۳۰۲۸] (۴۹) ومن مات من الغانمين بعد اخراجها الى دار الاسلام فنصيبه لورثته [۳۰۲۸] (۴۹) اور مجاہدین میں سے کوئی دار الاسلام تک مال لانے کے بعد انتقال کر جائے تو اس کا حصہ اس کے ورثہ کے لئے ہوگا۔ دار الاسلام میں مال غنیمت جمع کیا اس کے بعد کسی مجاہد کا انتقال ہوا تو اس کو غنیمت میں حصہ ملے گا۔ اور یہ حصہ اس کے ورثہ کو دے دیا جائے گا۔ دار الاسلام تک آنے کے بعد احراز ہو گیا یعنی مال غنیمت محفوظ ہو گیا اور مجاہدین کا اس میں حق ہو گیا۔ اس لئے جو اس کے بعد انتقال کیا وہ اس کا حصہ دار بن گیا۔ اور چونکہ وہ انتقال کر چکا ہے اس لئے اس کا حصہ اس کے ورثہ کو دے دیا جائے گا۔
And whoever among the warriors dies after taking them out to the abode of Islam, his share is for his heirs.
Source pages p. 282

Commentary
This passage states a clear ruling: if a fighter dies after the spoils have been brought to Dar al-Islam, he is entitled to a share, and that share is given to his heirs. The commentator explains that bringing the spoils to Dar al-Islam constitutes ihraz (secure possession), which establishes the fighters' ownership rights. Since the fighter dies after ownership is established, his right passes to his successors. This is the opposite of the previous ruling: before ihraz, no share; after ihraz, share goes to heirs.

Key Terms
ورثہ (warathah): Heirs, those entitled to inherit according to Islamic law.
احراز (ihraz): Secure possession; bringing spoils into Dar al-Islam, establishing ownership for the fighters.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a fighter dies after the spoils have been brought to Dar al-Islam, what happens to his share?
A) It is lost.
B) It is returned to the treasury.
C) It is given to his heirs.
D) It is divided among the remaining fighters.

Key Takeaway
A fighter's share in spoils becomes inheritable only after the spoils are securely possessed in Dar al-Islam (ihraz).

Imam's Permission to Offer Nafl During Battle
Ruling on imam offering extra reward during battle

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the permissibility of nafl during battle and identify its basis in the Sunnah.

Core Idea
An imam can promise a slain enemy's belongings to his killer as a special incentive during battle.

The imam is allowed to encourage fighters by promising extra rewards (nafl) beyond the regular spoils. This passage explains that such a promise is permissible, citing the example of the Prophet at Badr who declared that the killer gets the slain's personal effects.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling
The passage states: 'There is no harm if the imam gives extra reward (nafl) during battle and encourages by extra reward.' The ruling is that offering nafl is permissible (mubah) for the imam.
2
Locate the dalil naqli
Two proofs are cited: (1) Quran 8:65 commanding the Prophet to urge the believers to fight, and (2) a hadith from Abu Qatada that the Prophet said at Badr: 'Whoever kills a slain man with clear proof, his belongings are for him.'
The hadith is recorded in Abu Dawud, Tirmidhi, Muslim, and Bukhari.
3
Analyze the wajh al-dalalah
The key phrase 'فله سلبه' directly grants the killer the slain's personal belongings. This shows that the imam can promise such a reward to motivate fighters.
The phrase is zanni al-dalala but sufficient for permissibility.
4
Note the practical application
The nafl is a discretionary reward, not an automatic right. The imam decides when and how much to offer. The salab (weapons, armor) is a specific form of nafl.
This is beyond the regular five shares of booty.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
[۳۰۲۹ (۵۰) ولا بأس بان ينفل الامام فى حال القتال ويحرّض بالنفل على القتال فيقول من قتل قتيلا فله سلبه] [ص 283 continuation] اس کی ترغیب ہے ۔ یا ایها النبی حرض المؤمنين على القتال (الف) ( آیت ۶۵ سورۃ الانفال (۸) اس آیت میں ہے کہ اے نبی ایمان والوں کو قتال پر ابھارئیے (۲) حدیث میں ہے کہ جنگ بدر کے موقع پر آپ نے یہ کہہ کر ابھارا تھا کہ جو جس کو قتل کرے گا اس کا ساز و سامان اس کے لئے ہے۔ حدیث یہ ہے۔ عن ابی قتادة قال قال رسول الله له من قتل قتيلا له عليه بينة فله سلبه (ب) (ترندی شریف، باب ما جاء فیمن قتل قتیلا فله سلبه، ص ۲۵۸، نمبر ۱۵۶۲ را بود او دشریف، باب فی النفل ، ج ۲ ص ۱۹، نمبر ۲۷۳۸ مسلم شریف ، باب استحقاق القاتل سلب التقتيل ، ج ۲ ص ۸۶ نمبر ۷۵ ار بخاری شریف ، باب من لم شمس الاسلاب ،ص ۲۴۴، نمبر ۳۱۴۲ کتاب فرض الخمس ) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ مزید انعام کا وعدہ کرنا جائز ہے۔ ات حرض : قال پر ابھارنا، نفل : مزید انعام، سلب : چھینا ہوا مال ، سلب سے مشتق ہے چھینا۔
And there is no harm if the imam gives extra reward (nafl) during battle and encourages by extra reward, saying: Whoever kills a slain man, his belongings are for him.
Source pages p. 282

Commentary
This passage permits the imam to promise extra rewards (nafl) to fighters during battle to motivate them. Specifically, he can say that whoever kills an enemy will get the slain's personal effects (salab). The commentator supports this with Quranic verse 8:65 (encouragement to fight) and a hadith from the Battle of Badr where the Prophet ﷺ declared that the belongings of the slain go to his killer. This is a special incentive beyond the regular share of spoils. The key terms are explained: nafl (extra grant) and salab (stripped belongings).

Key Terms
نفل (nafl): Extra reward given to fighters beyond the regular share of spoils.
سلب (salab): The personal belongings of a slain enemy, including weapons and armor.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
An imam may promise extra rewards (nafl) like the slain's belongings to motivate fighters, based on the Prophet's example at Badr.

Imam's Discretionary Nafl for Raiding Parties After Khums
Ruling on imam promising spoils after khums

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the imam's permission to promise a portion of spoils after khums to a raiding party, cite the hadith proof, and apply the condition that the promise is after khums.

Core Idea
The imam may promise a portion of spoils after khums as a discretionary incentive.

In this lesson, we examine the ruling on the imam's authority to encourage a raiding party by promising them an extra share of the spoils. The passage clarifies that such a promise is valid only after the mandatory khums has been deducted. This practice is based on a hadith of the Prophet (sallallahu alayhi wa sallam) and demonstrates the flexibility of the imam in managing war incentives.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is the imam promising a predetermined portion (e.g., quarter) of the spoils to a sariyyah (raiding party) after the khums is taken. The ruling is mubah (permissible) as a discretionary nafl (additional reward).
This is not obligatory; it is a motivational tool.
2
Locate the dalil
The proof is a hadith from Habib ibn Salamah that the Prophet used to grant a quarter after khums and a third after khums when returning. This is a hadith ahad with zanni thubut.
The hadith is reported by Abu Dawud and Tirmidhi.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The phrase 'yanfilu al-rub' ba'da al-khumus' directly indicates that the promised share is taken after the khums has been set aside. The word 'ba'da' (after) is the key operative term.
This shows the condition that the promise applies to the remaining four-fifths.
4
Apply to a concrete example
If 20 camels are captured, the khums (1/5) is 4 camels, leaving 16. If the imam promised a quarter, then 4 camels are given as nafl, and the remaining 12 are distributed to the entire army as regular spoils.
The promised share is not taken from the khums or the total before khums.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
[۱۳۰۳۰ (۵۱) او يقول السرية قد جعلت لكم الربع بعد الخمس] [ص 283] یا کہے دستہ سے کہ میں نے تمہارے لئے چوتھائی کی شمس نکالنے کے بعد ۔ بڑے لشکر کے اندر سے کوئی چھوٹا لشکر جس کو دستہ کہتے ہیں وہ کسی جگہ جنگ کے لئے جارہا ہے اس کی ہمت بڑھانے کے لئے امام کہے کہ جتنا مال غنیمت میں لاؤ گے اس میں سے شمس نکالنے کے بعد جو بچے گا اس میں سے چوتھائی تم لوگوں کو انعام دیں گے ۔ اس کے بعد اس کو مال غنیمت کے طور پر لشکر میں تقسیم کریں گے۔ مثلا ہیں اونٹ غنیمت میں لایا اس میں سے پانچواں حصہ شمس نکالا جو چار اونٹ ہونگے۔ باقی سولہ اونٹ میں سے چوتھائی یعنی چار اونٹ انعام میں دیئے جائیں گے اور باقی بارہ اونٹ تمام مجاہدین پر بطور مال غنیمت تقسیم کریں گے۔ حدیث میں اس کا ثبوت ہے۔ عن حبیب بن سلمة ان رسول الله الله الله كان ينفل الربع بعد الخمس والثلث بعد الخمس اذا قفل (ج) (ابوداؤد شریف ، باب فیمن قال النمس قبل النفل میں ۲۱ نمبر ۲۷۴۹ ترمذی شریف، باب فی النفل ص ۲۸۴ ، نمبر ۱۵۶۱) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ موقع محل کے اعتبار سے امام انعام کا اعلان کر سکتا ہے۔ السرية : چھوٹا لشکر، دسته
Or he says to the detachment: I have made for you a quarter after the fifth.
Source pages p. 283

Commentary
This passage explains that the imam can promise a raiding party (sariyyah) a specific fraction of the spoils after the khums (one-fifth) is taken out. He might promise them one-quarter or one-third of the remaining spoils. The commentator gives an example: if 20 camels are captured, 4 go to khums, leaving 16. If the imam promised a quarter, an additional 4 camels are given as extra reward (nafl), and the remaining 12 are distributed among the entire army. This is supported by a hadith of Habib ibn Salamah that the Prophet used to grant nafl of a quarter after khums when commencing a raid, and a third after khums when returning. This shows the imam's discretion based on circumstances.

Key Terms
سرية (sariyyah): A detachment or raiding party sent from the main army.
خمس (khums): One-fifth of the spoils set aside for the public treasury.
نفل (nafl): Extra reward or bonus given to some fighters beyond their regular share.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) From the khums (fifth).
B) From the remaining four-fifths after khums.
C) From the total spoils before any deduction.
D) From the personal belongings of the enemy.

Key Takeaway
The imam may grant extra spoils to a raiding party from the four-fifths remaining after khums, a practice established by the Prophet's sunnah.

Prohibition of Nafl After Secure Possession Except from Khums
Ruling restricting extra rewards after spoils are secured

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling on giving extra rewards from spoils after ihraz and identify the only permissible source.

Core Idea
After spoils are secured, extra rewards are only from the khums — never from the fighters' shares.

This lesson addresses a specific rule in the law of spoils of war (ghanima). Once the spoils have been brought under secure control in Dar al-Islam (ihraz), the imam loses the discretion to give additional rewards from the general spoils. The ruling ensures that the fighters' shares are not diminished arbitrarily. The only exception is the khums (one-fifth) set aside for the public treasury.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What is the act being ruled? Giving nafl (extra reward) from spoils. The ruling is: prohibited after ihraz.
2
Identify the temporal condition
The condition that triggers the prohibition is after ihraz (secure possession). Before ihraz, the imam has discretion to give nafl from the general spoils.
3
Identify the exception
After ihraz, the only permissible source for nafl is the khums (the fifth portion set aside for public treasury).
4
Note the rationale
The rationale is to protect the shares of the fighters that have already been determined by the distribution rules after ihraz.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
[۳۰۳۱) (۵۲) ولا يُنفل بعد احراز الغنيمة الا من الخمس] [ص 283] اور انعام نہ دے غنیمت جمع کرنے کے بعد ممر خمس سے۔ جنگ ختم ہوگئی۔ لوگوں نے مال غنیمت بھی جمع کر لیا۔ اب اس میں سے کسی کو انعام دینا جائز نہیں ہے۔ اور اگر دینا ہی ہے تو پورے مال غنیمت میں سے پانچواں حصہ شمس نکالا ہے اس میں سے انعام دے۔
And no extra reward (nafl) is given after secure possession of the spoils except from the fifth (khums).
Source pages p. 283

Commentary
This passage establishes a restriction: once the spoils have been secured (ihraz) in Dar al-Islam, the imam cannot give any extra rewards (nafl) from the general spoils. The only permissible source for additional rewards after that point is the khums (one-fifth) that is set aside for public treasury. The commentator explains that after the battle is over and the spoils are collected, any special grants must be taken from the khums, not from the four-fifths belonging to the fighters. This ensures that the fighters' shares are not diminished after the distribution has been decided.

Key Terms
احراز (ihraz): Secure possession; bringing spoils into Dar al-Islam.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
After the spoils are secured in Dar al-Islam, from which portion can the imam give extra rewards?
A) From the fighters' shares.
B) From the total spoils.
C) Only from the khums (fifth).
D) He cannot give any extra rewards.

Key Takeaway
After spoils are secured (ihraz), extra rewards can only be given from the khums, not from the common spoils.

Ruling on Salb and Nafal from Ghanimah
Ruling on salb and nafal from spoils with proofs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the condition under which a fighter receives the slain enemy's equipment (salb) and explain why nafal is normally given only from the khums.

Core Idea
A fighter only gets the slain enemy's gear if the imam promised it; otherwise it is shared like all spoils.

This lesson examines the Hanafi ruling on the distribution of spoils, specifically regarding the salb (equipment) of a slain enemy and the additional reward known as nafal. Using proofs from the Sunnah and the practice of the Companions, we will see that the default rule is equality among all mujahideen, with two exceptions: a prior promise by the imam, or giving from the khums.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two categories of salb
Distinguish between salb that the imam designates for the killer (via a nafal announcement) and salb that is not designated. The ruling differs based on this.
2
Determine the default ruling for undesignated salb
If the imam does not announce nafal for the killer, the salb becomes part of the general ghanimah and is shared equally among all fighters.
This is the default, based on the hadith of the camel and the athar of Anas.
3
Recognize the exceptions for giving nafal
Nafal can be given from the general spoils only if the imam made a promise during battle. Alternatively, it can be given from the khums without a prior promise.
4
Analyze the proofs
Examine the hadith where the Prophet refused to take even a hair from spoils except the khums, and the athar of Anas insisting on nafal from khums.
5
Understand the procedure for nafal from the Hunayn incident
The imam must formally announce nafal and the killer must produce witnesses. Abu Bakr's refusal reinforces that without announcement, no nafal from general spoils.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب السير
[۳۰۳۲ (۵۳) واذا لم يجعل السلب للقاتل فهو من جملة الغنيمة والقاتل وغيره فيه
مال غنیمت جمع ہونے کے بعد سب مجاہدین کا حق لاحق ہو گیا ہے۔ اب اس میں سے کسی کو انعام دینا صحیح نہیں ہے۔ اس لئے اگر دینا ہی ہو تو خمس جو نکالا ہے اس میں سے کسی کو انعام دے۔ ہاں! حالت جنگ میں کسی کے لئے انعام کا وعدہ کیا تھا تو وہ پورے مال غنیمت میں سے دیگا (۲) اس حدیث میں اس کا اشارہ ہے۔ سمعت عمرو بن عبسة قال صلى بنا رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم الى بعير من المغنم فلما سلم اخذ وبرة من جنب البعير ثم قال ولا يحل لى من غنمائكم مثل هذا الا الخمس والخمس مردود فيكم (الف) (ابوداؤد شریف، باب الامام يستأثر بشى من الفى لنفسه ، ج ۲، ص ۲۳، نمبر ۲۷۵۵) اس حدیث میں جب حضور فرماتے ہیں کہ خمس کے علاوہ میں مال غنیمت کا مالک نہیں ہوں۔ تو جب مال غنیمت میں مجاہدین کا حق ثابت ہو گیا تو اب دوسرے کو انعام کیسے دے سکیں گے (۳) اثر میں ہے کہ حضرت انس کو حضرت عبید اللہ بن ابی بکرۃ مال غنیمت میں سے انعام دینا چاہتے تھے تو انہوں نے انکار فرمایا اور فرمایا کہ اگر دینا ہی ہو تو خمس جو نکالا ہے اس میں سے دو۔ اثریہ ہے۔ ان انس بن مالک کان مع عبيد الله بن ابى بكرة في غزاة غزاها فاصابوا سبيا فاراد عبيد الله ان يعطى انسا من السبى قبل ان يقسم فقال انس لا ولكن اقسم ثم اعطنى من الخمس قال فقال عبيد الله لا الا من جميع الغنائم فابى انس ان يقبل منه وابي عبيد الله ان يعطيه من الخمس شيئا (ب)(طحاوى شریف، باب النفل بعد الفراغ من قال العدو واحراز الغنيمة ، ج ثانی ص ۱۳۳ مصنف عبد الرزاق ، باب لا نفل الامن الخمس ولا نفل من الذهب والفضة ، ج خامس، ص۱۹۲، نمبر ۹۳۴۴) اس اثر میں ہے کہ خمس میں سے انعام دے۔
احراز : مال جمع کرنا۔
[۳۰۳۲ (۵۳) اگر سامان قاتل کے لئے نہیں کیا تو وہ غنیمت میں ہوگا اور اس میں قاتل اور غیر قاتل برابر ہوگا۔
اگر امام نے مزید انعام دینے کا اعلان کیا تب تو مقتول کا سازو سامان قاتل کے لئے ہوگا ۔ اور اگر یہ اعلان نہیں کیا تو مقتول کا ساز و سامان قاتل کے لئے نہیں ہوگا۔ اس کو مال غنیمت میں شامل کر دیا جائے گا۔ اور اس سامان میں قاتل اور غیر قاتل سب کا حصہ برابر ہوگا۔
جنگ حنین کے واقعہ سے معلوم ہوتا ہے کہ با ضابطہ امام انعام کا اعلان کرے اور قاتل قتل کرنے پر گواہ پیش کرے تب اس کو سلب اور انعام دیا جائے گا ورنہ نہیں۔ حدیث کا ٹکڑا یہ ہے۔ عن ابی قتادة قال خرجنا مع رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم عام حنين ... وجلس النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم فقال من قتل قتيلا له عليه بينة فله سلبه فقمت فقلت من يشهد لي؟ ثم جلست ثم قال من قتل قتيلا له عليه بينة فله سلبه فقمت فقلت من يشهد لي؟ (الف) ( بخاری شریف، باب من لم [؟] شمس الاسلاب ،ص ۴۴۴ نمبر ۳۱۴۲ر مسلم شریف، باب استحقاق القاتل سلب التقتیل ، ص ۸۶ نمبر ۱ ۱۷۵) اس حدیث کے انداز سے معلوم ہوا کہ امام انعام کا اعلان کرے گا تو مقتول کا سامان قاتل کو ملے گا ورنہ نہیں (۲) کیونکہ ابو بکر نے انعام دینے سے انکار فرمایا ۔ فقال ابو بكر لاها الله اذا لا يعمد الى اسد من اسد الله يقاتل عن الله ورسوله یعطیک سلبه (ب) ( بخاری شریف، نمبر ۱۳۱۴۲ مسلم شریف نمبر (۱۷۵) اس اثر میں ہے کہ حضرت ابو بکر نے عام حالات میں انعام دینے سے انکار فرمایا۔ جس سے معلوم ہوا کہ امام انعام دینے کا وعدہ کرے گا تو سلب دیا جائے گا ورنہ نہیں۔
حاشیه: (الف) عمر بن عبسہ فرماتے ہیں کہ ہم کو حضور نے مال غنیمت کے اونٹ کی طرف نماز پڑھائی۔ جب سلام پھیرا تو اونٹ کے پہلو سے بال پکڑا پھر فرمایا تمہاری غنیمت میں سے میرے لئے اتنا بھی حلال نہیں ہے سوائے خمس کے۔ اور خمس بھی تمہارے اوپر واپس کیا جاتا ہے (ب) انس بن مالک عبید اللہ بن بکرۃ کے ساتھ کسی غزوہ میں تھے ۔ انہوں نے قیدی پایا۔ عبید اللہ نے حضرت انس کو کچھ قیدی تقسیم سے پہلے دینا چاہا تو حضرت انس نے فرمایا نہیں۔ لیکن تقسیم کرو پھر پانچویں میں سے دو۔ تو عبید اللہ نے کہا نہیں۔ لیکن تمام مال سے تو حضرت انس نے اس کو قبول کرنے سے انکار کیا۔ اور عبید اللہ خمس میں سے کچھ دینا نہیں چاہتے تھے۔
Book of Siyar [3032 (53)] And if the salb is not designated for the killer, it is part of the general ghanimah, and the killer and others are equal in it. After the spoils are collected, the right of all mujahideen is established. Now it is not correct to give a gift (nafal) to anyone from it. Therefore, if one must give, then give a gift to someone from the khums that was taken out. Yes, if a promise of nafal was made to someone during the state of war, then it will be given from the entire spoils. (2) There is an indication of this in this hadith: I heard Amr ibn Abasah say: The Prophet (peace be upon him) led us in prayer facing a camel from the spoils. When he said the salam, he took a hair from the side of the camel, then said: 'It is not lawful for me from your spoils even this much except the khums, and the khums is returned to you.' (a) (Abu Dawud, Chapter: The Imam taking something for himself from the spoils, vol. 2, p. 23, no. 2755) In this hadith, when the Prophet says he is not the owner of any of the spoils except the khums, then once the right of the mujahideen is established in the spoils, how can they give a gift to another? (3) There is an athar that when Ubaydullah ibn Abi Bakrah wanted to give a gift to Anas from the spoils, Anas refused and said: 'If you must give, then give from the khums that was taken out.' The athar is: Anas ibn Malik was with Ubaydullah ibn Abi Bakrah in a battle they fought, and they captured some prisoners. Ubaydullah wanted to give Anas some of the prisoners before the division. Anas said: 'No, but divide first, then give me from the khums.' Ubaydullah said: 'No, only from the entire spoils.' Anas refused to accept from him, and Ubaydullah refused to give him anything from the khums. (b) (Tahawi, Chapter: Nafal after finishing, etc.; Musannaf Abd al-Razzaq, Chapter: No nafal except from khums, vol. 5, p. 192, no. 9344) This athar indicates to give from the khums. Ihtiraz: collecting the spoils. [3032 (53)] If the equipment is not designated for the killer, then it will be in the ghanimah and the killer and non-killer are equal in it. If the imam announced additional nafal, then the slain man's equipment will be for the killer. And if he did not announce, then the slain man's equipment will not be for the killer. It will be included in the general ghanimah, and in that equipment the killer and non-killer all share equally. From the incident of the Battle of Hunayn, it is understood that the imam must formally announce nafal and the killer must produce witnesses that he killed, then he will be given the salb and nafal; otherwise not. A portion of the hadith is: From Abu Qatadah: We went out with the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) in the year of Hunayn... The Prophet (peace be upon him) sat and said: 'Whoever kills a slain person and has clear proof of it, then his salb is for him.' I stood and said: 'Who will testify for me?' Then I sat. Then he said: 'Whoever kills a slain person and has clear proof of it, then his salb is for him.' I stood and said: 'Who will testify for me?' (a) (Bukhari, Chapter: ... no. 3142; Muslim, Chapter: Entitlement of the killer to the salb of the slain, p. 86, no. 175) From the manner of this hadith, it is understood that if the imam announces nafal, then the slain man's equipment goes to the killer; otherwise not. (2) Because Abu Bakr refused to give nafal. Abu Bakr said: 'No, by Allah, then would one go to a lion from the lions of Allah who fights for Allah and His Messenger and give you his salb?' (b) (Bukhari, no. 13142; Muslim, no. 175) In this athar, Abu Bakr refused to give nafal in general circumstances. From this it is understood that if the imam promises nafal, then salb is given; otherwise not. Footnotes: (a) Amr ibn Abasah says: The Prophet led us in prayer facing a camel from the spoils. When he said the salam, he took a hair from the side of the camel, then said: 'From your spoils, even this much is not lawful for me except the khums, and the khums is returned to you.' (b) Anas ibn Malik was with Ubaydullah ibn Bakrah in a battle. They captured prisoners. Ubaydullah wanted to give Anas some prisoners before division. Anas said: 'No, but divide, then give me from the khums.' Ubaydullah said: 'No, only from all the spoils.' Anas refused to accept, and Ubaydullah did not want to give anything from the khums.
Source pages p. 284

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof (dalil) regarding the distribution of spoils (ghanimah) and the additional reward (nafal) for killing an enemy. The matn states: if the imam does not designate the slain enemy's equipment (salb) for the killer, it becomes part of the general spoils and is shared equally among all fighters. The commentary explains that once the spoils are collected, all mujahideen have a right to them; no individual can be singled out for a gift (nafal) from the general spoils. However, if the imam had promised nafal during battle, he may fulfill that promise from the entire spoils. Alternatively, nafal can be given from the khums (one-fifth) which is set aside for the public treasury. The author then provides two proofs: (1) A hadith from Amr ibn Abasah where the Prophet (ﷺ) refused to take even a hair from the spoils except the khums, and (2) an athar from Anas ibn Malik who refused to accept any gift from the general spoils before division, insisting that nafal be given from the khums. The passage also discusses the procedure of nafal: the imam must formally announce that whoever kills someone will get his salb, and the killer must provide witnesses. This is based on the incident of Hunayn where the Prophet (ﷺ) repeatedly asked for witnesses. Finally, an athar from Abu Bakr shows that he refused to give nafal from the general spoils without a prior promise, emphasizing that nafal is only given when the imam announces it beforehand.

Key Terms
سلب (salab / salb): The equipment (clothes, weapons, mount) taken from a slain enemy warrior.
نفل (nafal): An additional reward or prize given to a fighter beyond his regular share of spoils.
خمس (khums): One-fifth of the spoils set aside for the public treasury and specific recipients (Allah, Prophet, relatives, orphans, poor, travelers).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the primary source from which nafal can be given if the imam did not make a prior promise?
A) General spoils
B) Khums
C) The killer's share
D) The imam's personal property

Key Takeaway
A fighter receives the slain enemy's salb only if the imam announced nafal beforehand; otherwise it is shared equally. Nafal from the general spoils is not permissible except from the khums.

Definition of Salb: Items Included in Spoils of a Slain Enemy
Defines salb and provides three hadith proofs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi definition of salb and identify the three categories of items included, with their hadith evidence.

Core Idea
Salb includes all items on the slain enemy's person: clothes, weapons, and mount — the imam must give all if he promised.

What exactly does the killer of an enemy in battle receive as his special reward (salab)? This passage from Al-Sharh al-Sameri defines 'salb' as the personal belongings of the slain: his clothes, weapons, and mount. Understanding this definition is crucial for applying the imam's offer of nafal correctly. The passage also provides hadith evidence for each component and clarifies that the imam must give the entire salb if he made such a promise.

Guided Path
1
Identify the definition of salb
The text defines salb as 'what is on the slain person of his clothes, weapons, and mount.' Recognize that this is a three-part definition.
Clothes include whatever the slain is wearing; weapons include swords, etc.; mount includes the horse or camel he rides.
2
Examine the proof for weapons
The hadith of Abdullah ibn Mas'ud: the Prophet gave him the sword of Abu Jahl as nafal. This shows that weapons are part of salb.
Hadith from Abu Dawud no. 272.
3
Examine the proof for the mount
The hadith of an expedition where the Prophet gave extra camels as nafal. This shows that the mount (riding animal) is included in salb.
Hadith from Abu Dawud no. 2745.
4
Examine the proof for clothes and accessories
The incident of Mutah: a soldier brought the slain Roman's horse, sword, saddle, bridle, belt, and gold-adorned weapons to Khalid ibn al-Walid, who gave most as nafal. This proves that all personal effects and riding gear are salb.
Hadith from Tahawi.
5
Understand the imam's promise
The salb is given only if the imam declares 'man qatala qatilan falahu salabuh'. Otherwise, the items go to general booty. This is supported by Abu Bakr's refusal to give nafal in general circumstances.
The imam's promise makes it wajib to give the entire salb.

رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم نقل القاتل سلب كله قال بلى ولكنى استكثرته (ه) ( طحاوی شریف، باب الرجل يقتل قتیلافی دار الحرب هل يكون له سلبهم لا ؟ ، ج حاشیہ : (الف) عمر بن عبسہ فرماتے ہیں کہ ہم کو حضور And the salb is what is on the slain person of his clothes, weapons, and mount... his salb. Then I stood and said: 'Who will testify for me?' (a) (Bukhari, Chapter: ... no. 3142; Muslim, Chapter: Entitlement of the killer to the salb of the slain, p. 86, no. 175) From the manner of this hadith, it is understood that if the imam announces nafal, then the slain man's equipment goes to the killer; otherwise not. (2) Because Abu Bakr refused to give nafal. Abu Bakr said: 'No, by Allah, then would one go to a lion from the lions of Allah who fights for Allah and His Messenger and give you his salb?' (b) (Bukhari, no. 13142; Muslim, no. 175) In this athar, Abu Bakr refused to give nafal in general circumstances. From this it is understood that if the imam promises nafal, then salb is given; otherwise not. [3033] (54) What is on the slain person of his clothes, weapons, and mount, that is the salb. What items are included in salb? They say: Whatever clothes are on the slain, or weapons on him, and the mount he is riding, all are included in the salb. When the imam says 'Whoever kills a slain person, his salb is for him', all these will be included in the salb, and it becomes incumbent upon the imam to give all of them. The evidence that weapons are included is this hadith: From Abdullah ibn Mas'ud: The Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) gave me as nafal on the day of Badr the sword of Abu Jahl, whom I had killed. (c) (Abu Dawud, Chapter: Permitting nafal from the spoils of the wounded, vol. 2, p. 17, no. 272) In this, the sword of Abu Jahl was given as nafal, so it is understood that weapons are included in salb. The evidence that the mount is included is this hadith: From Abdullah: The Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) sent us in a small expedition, and our shares reached twelve camels each, and the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) gave us an additional camel each as nafal. (d) (Abu Dawud, Chapter: Nafal for the expedition going out of the army, vol. 2, p. 20, no. 2745) In this hadith, camels were given as nafal, so it is understood that the mount is included in salb. Clothes, reins, saddles, etc. are also included in salb. The evidence is this hadith: Indeed, an auxiliary soldier accompanied them in the battle of Mutah. A Roman soldier was attacking the Muslims and inciting them. So that auxiliary soldier used a trick: he sat under a rock. When the Roman passed by, he hamstrung his horse, the Roman fell, and he struck him with his sword and killed him. Then he brought his horse, his sword, his saddle, his bridle, his belt, and his weapons, all adorned with gold and jewels, to Khalid ibn al-Walid. Khalid took a portion and gave him the rest as nafal. I said, 'O Khalid, what is this? Do you not know that the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) gave the entire salb of the slain to the killer?' He said, 'Yes, but I considered it too much.' (e) (Tahawi, Chapter: A man killing an enemy in dar al-harb; is his salb for him or not?) Footnotes: (a) Amr ibn Abasah says: The Prophet led us in prayer facing a camel from the spoils. When he said the salam, he took a hair from the side of the camel, then said: 'From your spoils, even this much is not lawful for me except the khums, and the khums is returned to you.' (b) Anas ibn Malik was with Ubaydullah ibn Bakrah in a battle. They captured prisoners. Ubaydullah wanted to give Anas some prisoners before division. Anas said: 'No, but divide, then give me from the khums.' Ubaydullah said: 'No, only from all the spoils.' Anas refused to accept, and Ubaydullah did not want to give anything from the khums.
Source pages p. 285

Commentary
This passage is a definition and ruling (definition_ruling) on what constitutes salb (the spoils taken from a slain enemy). The matn defines salb as the clothes, weapons, and mount of the slain. The commentary expands on each item: clothes include whatever the slain is wearing; weapons include swords, etc.; mount includes the horse or camel he rides. The author provides three hadith proofs: (1) The sword of Abu Jahl was given as nafal to Abdullah ibn Mas'ud, showing that weapons are part of salb. (2) The Prophet gave an additional camel as nafal in an expedition, proving that mounts are included. (3) The incident of Mutah where a soldier brought the entire equipment of a slain Roman (horse, sword, saddle, bridle, belt, and gold-adorned weapons) to Khalid ibn al-Walid, who gave most of it as nafal. This shows that all personal effects and riding gear of the slain are included in salb. The passage also clarifies that the imam is obligated to give the entire salb if he declared 'man qatala qatilan falahu salabuh'. The footnote discusses the permissibility of nafal from khums versus general spoils, consistent with the previous lesson.

Key Terms
سلب (salab / salb): All items on the person of the slain enemy: clothes, weapons, and his mount.
مركب (markab): The mount (horse, camel) that the slain enemy was riding.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the following items is NOT considered part of the salb of a slain enemy according to the passage?
A) The enemy's sword
B) The enemy's coat
C) The enemy's horse
D) The enemy's wallet

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi definition of salb includes three categories: clothes, weapons, and mount (with its equipment), and the imam must give all if he promised nafal.

Definition and Conditions of Salab (Spoils of the Slain)
Defines salab and its components with supporting hadith

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define salab as per Hanafi fiqh, list its three components, and apply the condition that the imam must announce a reward for the killer to be entitled.

Core Idea
Salab is the slain enemy's attire, weapons, and mount; entitlement depends on the imam's prior promise.

This passage from the commentary defines salab – the spoils taken from a slain enemy warrior. It specifies exactly which items are included: clothing, weapons, and mount. More importantly, it establishes a key condition: the imam must have announced a reward for the kill. Without such an announcement, the killer does not receive the salab; it becomes part of the general booty. We will examine the textual evidence from hadith and the practice of Abu Bakr.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and its condition
The passage rules that salab belongs to the killer only if the imam announces a reward. State this as the core Hanafi position.
This condition is derived from the context of the Hunayn hadith and Abu Bakr's refusal.
2
Define salab and list its components
The text explicitly lists three components: the slain's clothing, weapon, and mount. Note that cash, gold, and silver are excluded – they belong to the general booty (ghanimah).
The Urdu commentary mentions that saddle, reins, belt, etc. are also included as part of the mount's equipment.
3
Examine the primary proof
The hadith from Hunayn: 'Whoever kills a slain and has proof, for him is his salab.' The phrase 'for him is his salab' indicates entitlement, but the context (the imam's announcement) makes it conditional.
The hadith is ahad (zanni al-thubut) and zanni al-dalala, so it does not create certainty.
4
Consider the practice of Abu Bakr
Abu Bakr refused to give salab to a warrior who had killed without a prior promise, saying 'No, by Allah, would he go to a lion from the lions of Allah... and then you give him his salab?' This confirms the condition.
This athar is cited as support for the Hanafi position.
5
Apply the ruling
In practice, the imam must explicitly declare a reward for specific kills. Only then does the killer get the salab. Otherwise, all spoils go to the general treasury and are distributed as ghanimah.
The killer does not even get extra share unless announced.

And the salab is what is on the slain from his clothes, his weapon, and his mount. So I stood and said: Who will testify for me? (Bukhari, Muslim) From the style of this hadith it is understood that if the imam announces a reward, then the slain's belongings go to the killer; otherwise not. (2) Because Abu Bakr refused to give a reward. He said: No, by Allah, would he go to a lion from the lions of Allah who fights for Allah and His Messenger and then you give him his salab? (Bukhari, Muslim) In this athar, Abu Bakr refused to give a reward in general circumstances, from which it is understood that if the imam promises to give a reward, then salab is given; otherwise not. [3033] (54) Whatever clothes, weapon, and mount are on the slain are the salab. The scholars say: whatever clothes is on the slain, or weapon is on the slain, or mount the slain is riding, all are included in the salab. When the imam says 'Whoever kills a slain person, for him is his salab,' all these are included in the salab, and it is obligatory upon the imam to give all of them. The weapon is included; its proof is the hadith of Ibn Mas'ud: The Messenger of Allah gave me the sword of Abu Jahl on the day of Badr because I killed him. (Abu Dawud) Thus the sword was given as nafal, showing that the weapon is included in salab. The mount is included; its proof is the hadith of Ibn Mas'ud: The Messenger of Allah sent us on a raid, our shares reached twelve camels each, and he gave us an extra camel each. (Abu Dawud) Thus the camel was given as nafal, showing that the mount is included. Clothing, reins, saddle, etc., are also included; its proof is the hadith of al-Madadi who accompanied them in the battle of Mu'tah, and a Roman was attacking the Muslims. So al-Madadi tricked him, cut the horse's leg, killed him, and brought his horse, sword, saddle, reins, belt, and weapons, all adorned with gold and jewels, to Khalid ibn al-Walid. Khalid took a portion and gave the remainder as nafal. I said: O Khalid, do you not know that the Messenger of Allah gave the killer the entire salab? He said: Yes, but I considered it too much. (Tahawi) Hashiya: (a) We went out with the Messenger of Allah for the battle of Hunayn... (b) Abu Bakr said... (c) Ibn Mas'ud... (d) Ibn Mas'ud... (e) al-Madadi story: They went to Khalid; all were adorned with gold and jewels, so Khalid took some and gave the rest as nafal. I asked: O Khalid, do you not know that the Messenger of Allah gave the killer the entire salab? He said: Yes, but I considered it too much.
Source pages p. 285

Commentary
This passage from the commentary explains the definition of salab (the spoils taken from a slain enemy warrior) and its components. The Arabic matn states that salab consists of the slain's clothing, weapons, and mount. The Urdu commentary elaborates with several hadith proofs. A key condition is that the imam must explicitly announce a reward for the kill; otherwise, the killer is not entitled to the salab. The passage also distinguishes that cash, gold, and silver are not part of salab but belong to the general booty (ghanimah) subject to khums and distribution. The hadith evidence is provided for each component: the sword (weapon), the camel (mount), and the story of al-Madadi showing that all items including saddle, reins, belt, etc., are included. The ruling is that the imam is obliged to give the salab when he has promised it. The commentary follows the Hanafi school's position on this matter.

Key Terms
السلب (al-salab): The spoils taken from a slain enemy warrior, consisting of his clothing, weapons, and mount.
النفل (al-nafal): Extra spoils given to a warrior beyond his regular share, often as a reward for bravery.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to this passage, what is required for a killer to receive the salab of his slain enemy?
A) He must bring witnesses to confirm the kill.
B) The imam must have announced a reward for the kill.
C) The slain must be a leader of the enemy.
D) The killer must be a close companion of the Prophet.

Key Takeaway
Salab consists of the slain's clothing, weapons, and mount; the killer is entitled to it only if the imam has promised a reward.

Prohibition of Using Ghanimah After Leaving Dar al-Harb
Rules on using booty provisions after departing enemy territory

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on using booty after leaving enemy territory and apply the rule that leftover provisions must be returned for collective distribution.

Core Idea
Once outside Dar al-Harb, all booty must be pooled; personal use is haram until distribution.

The rules of ghanimah do not end when the battle is over. This passage clarifies a critical boundary: the moment the Muslim army crosses into friendly territory, the booty becomes a collective right of all mujahideen. Any provisions still in hand must be returned to the common pool for fair distribution. The ruling is supported by the Prophet's practice at Khaybar and a companion's permission to consume only until reaching home.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
State exactly what the passage prohibits: using food or fodder from booty after leaving Dar al-Harb. The ruling is haram.
The prohibition applies to both eating (for humans) and feeding (for animals).
2
Locate the primary dalil
Find the hadith of Mu'adh from Abu Dawud: the Prophet distributed only a portion at Khaybar and kept the rest for formal distribution.
The hadith is zanni al-thubut but accepted in Hanafi fiqh as a proof.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The Prophet's action of setting aside leftovers for the general booty indicates that after the campaign, all booty must be pooled. The leftover portion is not for personal retention.
The rule distinguishes between immediate need (permissible in dar al-harb) and post-departure (must return).
4
Consider the athar of Ibn Abbas
Ibn Abbas allowed eating from booty in enemy territory until entering one's home (Dar al-Islam). This supports the boundary: after reaching Dar al-Islam, leftovers must be returned.
The athar is a companion opinion, not a direct proof, but it reinforces the Hanafi position.
5
Note the practical hashia
Umar's letter permits eating and feeding while in enemy territory, but if items are sold, khums becomes due. This shows that commercial exchange does not exempt booty from collective rights.
The hashia reminds that even permissible use is limited to necessity, not ownership.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
واذا خرج المسلمون من دار الحرب لم يجز ان يعلقوا من الغنيمة ولا يأكلوا منها شيئا ومن فضل معه علف او طعام ردّه الى الغنيمة. جب تک دار الحرب میں رہا مال غنیمت کا کھانا وغیرہ استعمال کر سکتا تھا۔ لیکن جب دار الحرب سے باہر چلے گئے تو اب اس میں سے استعمال نہیں کر سکتے۔ اب جو باقی بچا ہے اس کو بھی مال غنیمت میں شامل کرے اور امام کے تقسیم کرنے کے بعد اپنے اپنے حصے میں کھائے اور چارہ کھلائے۔ دار الحرب سے نکلنے کے بعد یہ مال سب مجاہدین کا ہو گیا اس لئے مجاہدین میں تقسیم کر کے اپنا اپنا حصہ استعمال کرے (۲) دارالحرب سے باہر جانے کے بعد غنیمت کو مجاہدین میں تقسیم کرنا ضروری ہے اس لئے اگر ہر ایک کے پاس کھانے پینے کی چیز رہ جائے گی تو مکمل طور پر تقسیم نہیں ہو سکے گی۔ اس لئے ان چیزوں کو غنیمت میں شامل کرنا ضروری ہے (۳) فقال معاذ غزونا مع رسول الله الله خيبر فاصبنا فيها غنما فقسم فينا رسول الله الله طائفة وجعل بقيتها فى المغنم (ابوداؤد شریف، باب فی بیع الطعام اذ افضل عن الناس في ارض العدو، ص ۱۳، نمبر ۲۷۰۷) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ ضرورت کے مطابق ہی استعمال کرے اور باقی مال غنیمت میں شامل کرے (۴) اثر ہے۔ ان عبد الله بن عباس لم ير بأسا ان يأكل الرجل طعاما في ارض الشرك حتى يدخل اهله (مصنف ابن ابی شیبة، ۲۹ امن قال يا كلون من الطعام ولا تحملون ومن رخص فیه، ج سادس، ص ۵۰۹، نمبر ۳۳۳۳۷) اس اثر سے معلوم ہوا کہ اہل یعنی دار الاسلام تک کھا سکتا ہے اس کے بعد واپس جمع کر دے۔ حاشیہ: (الف) حضرت عمر نے مجھ کو لکھا کہ لوگوں کو کھانے دو اور چارہ مال غنیمت میں کھلانے دو۔ ہاں! کچھ سونا یا چاندی کے بدلے بیچے تو اس میں سے خمس واجب ہے اور مسلمانوں کا حصہ ہے۔ (ب) حضرت معاذ فرماتے ہیں کہ ہم نے حضور کے ساتھ خیبر کا غزوہ کیا۔ ہم نے اس میں غنیمت حاصل کی تو حضور نے ایک ٹکڑا ہم میں تقسیم کیا اور باقی غنیمت میں حصہ دے دیا (ج) حضرت عبداللہ بن عباس اس بات میں کوئی حرج نہیں سمجھتے تھے کہ آدمی گھر آنے تک دارالحرب کی زمین میں غنیمت میں سے کھائے۔
And when the Muslims leave Dar al-Harb, it is not permissible for them to feed (their animals) from the booty nor to eat anything from it. And whatever fodder or food remains with him, he should return it to the booty. As long as he stayed in Dar al-Harb, he could use the food of the booty etc. But when he left Dar al-Harb, he cannot use it. Now what remains, he should include it in the booty, and after the imam distributes it, he may eat and feed from his own share. After leaving Dar al-Harb, this property becomes the right of all the mujahideen, so it must be distributed among them and each should use his own share. (2) After going outside Dar al-Harb, it is necessary to distribute the booty among the mujahideen; if each person keeps leftover food, the distribution cannot be complete. Therefore, it is necessary to include these items in the booty. (3) Mu'adh said: We fought with the Messenger of Allah at Khaybar and we obtained goats. The Messenger of Allah divided a portion among us and placed the remainder in the booty. (Abu Dawud) From this hadith, it is understood that one should use only as much as needed and return the rest to the booty. (4) There is an athar: Ibn Abbas saw no harm in a man eating food in the land of shirk until he enters his family (i.e., Dar al-Islam). (Musannaf Ibn Abi Shaybah) From this athar, it is understood that he can eat until he reaches Dar al-Islam, after that he must return it. Hashiya: (a) Umar wrote to me: Let the people eat and feed the animals from the booty. Yes, if someone sells something for gold or silver, then khums is obligatory on it, and it is the share of the Muslims. (b) Mu'adh says: We fought with the Messenger of Allah at Khaybar... (c) Ibn Abbas saw no harm...
Source pages p. 286

Commentary
This passage addresses the rules regarding the use of ghanimah (booty) after the Muslim army has left enemy territory. While still in dar al-harb, soldiers may use food and fodder from the booty for immediate needs. However, once they leave dar al-harb, such usage is prohibited because the booty must be collected and distributed fairly among all entitled mujahideen. Any leftover food or fodder must be returned to the general booty pool. The commentator supports this with the hadith of Mu'adh at Khaybar, where the Prophet distributed only a portion and kept the rest for formal distribution, and with the athar of Ibn Abbas allowing consumption until reaching home. The hashia adds that while in dar al-harb, eating and feeding are permitted, but if items are sold for gold or silver, khums becomes due, indicating that the sale is considered part of the booty. The overall rule is that after departure from enemy land, all booty must be subject to proper distribution.

Key Terms
دار الحرب (dar al-harb): Territory under non-Muslim rule where Muslims are in a state of war or where Islamic law is not applied.
الغنيمة (al-ghanimah): Booty taken from enemy combatants after a battle, subject to khums and distribution among mujahideen.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What must a soldier do with leftover food or fodder after the Muslim army leaves dar al-harb?
A) He may keep it for his own use.
B) He must return it to the general booty.
C) He must sell it and give the proceeds to the imam.
D) He may give it to his family.

Key Takeaway
Leaving Dar al-Harb triggers a duty to pool all booty; personal use becomes unlawful until distribution.

Shares for Horseman and Foot Soldier: Abu Hanifa vs. Sahibayn
Intra-Hanafi dispute on horseman's shares in spoils.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on shares for horsemen and foot soldiers, identify the Sahibayn's opposing view, and explain the dalil and thamarah al-khilaf.

Core Idea
A horseman gets 2 shares per Imam Abu Hanifa, but the Sahibayn say 3 — the Khaybar precedent is decisive.

This lesson examines an important intra-Hanafi dispute on the distribution of war spoils (ghanimah). The number of shares a horseman receives directly affects the allocation among soldiers. By examining the textual proofs, we see how different hadith lead to different rulings, and how the Hanafi school resolves the conflict.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the ruling attributed to Abu Hanifa: the horseman gets two shares (one for himself, one for his horse) and the foot soldier gets one share.
This is the mufta bihi (relied-upon) position.
2
Identify the opposing view
State the view of the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani): the horseman gets three shares (one for himself, two for his horse).
This is an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf, not an external madhhab dispute.
3
Examine the proofs
Read the two hadiths cited: the Khaybar hadith supporting Abu Hanifa, and the Ibn ‘Umar hadith supporting the Sahibayn. Note how each serves as a direct proof.
Both are ahadith, but one is specific to the Khaybar incident.
4
Analyse the Hanafi response
Understand why the Hanafi school prefers Abu Hanifa's view: the Khaybar incident is a specific, large-scale distribution that overrides the general hadith.
This is a form of tarjih based on specificity (takhsis).
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
Calculate the practical difference: under Abu Hanifa, a horseman receives 2 shares; under the Sahibayn, 3 shares. This changes the proportion of shares between horsemen and foot soldiers.
Affects the total number of shares in a given army.

حاشیہ : (الف) خیبر کی زمین حضور نے اہل حدیبیہ پر اٹھارہ حصوں میں تقسیم فرمائی اور لشکر ایک ہزار پندرہ سو تھے ۔ جن میں سے تین سو گھوڑے سوار تھے۔ پس گھوڑے سوار کو دو حصے دیئے اور پیدل کو ایک حصہ (ب) حضور نے پیدل والے کو ایک حصہ دیا اور گھوڑے سوار کو تین حصے ۔ ایک حصہ آدمی کا اور دو حصے گھوڑے کے
[3036] (57) For the horseman, two shares, and for the foot soldier, one share according to Abu Hanifa, may Allah have mercy on him. And they both said: forage: fodder. (Explanation: After the one-fifth part (khums) is extracted from the spoils, the distribution of wealth among the mujahideen will be as follows: The horseman will receive two shares—one share for the horse and one share for the rider. And the one fighting on foot will receive only one share, for himself. This is the view of Imam Abu Hanifa. There is proof in the hadith: The Prophet divided Khaybar into 36 shares, half for the Muslims' affairs and half (1800 shares) for the mujahideen. The mujahideen were 1500, among them 300 horsemen—so they were doubled to become 600, so 1200 foot soldiers and 600 horsemen made 1800. And the horseman was given two shares. The hadith is: He said, 'Khaibar was divided among the people of Hudaybiyyah, and the Messenger of Allah divided it into eighteen shares. The army was one thousand five hundred, among them three hundred horsemen. So he gave the horseman two shares and the foot soldier one share.' (Abu Dawood, chapter on the ruling of Khaibar land, page 68 number 3015; Dar Qutni, Kitab al-Siyar, volume 4, page 61 number 4138). This hadith shows that the horseman gets only two shares and the foot soldier one share. The Sahibayn say that the horseman has three shares. There is proof in the hadith: 'From Ibn ‘Umar that the Messenger of Allah gave a man and his horse three shares: one share for him and two shares for his horse.' (Abu Dawood, chapter on the shares of horses, page 19 number 2733; Tirmidhi, chapter on the share of the horse, page 283 number 1554; Dar Qutni, Kitab al-Siyar, volume 4, page 58 number 4122). This hadith shows that two shares are for the horse and one for the rider, total three shares. Footnote (a): the Prophet divided the land of Khaibar among the people of Hudaybiyyah into 18 shares, and the army was 1500, among them 300 horsemen, so he gave two shares to each horseman and one share to each foot soldier. Footnote (b): the Prophet gave the foot soldier one share and the horseman three shares—one share for the man and two for the horse.
Source pages p. 287

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the number of shares a horseman receives in the distribution of spoils (after khums). The ruling is stated: according to Abu Hanifa, the horseman gets two shares (one for himself and one for his horse) and the foot soldier gets one share. The Sahibayn—Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani—hold that the horseman gets three shares (one for himself and two for his horse). Both views are supported by hadith. Abu Hanifa relies on the practice at Khaybar where the Prophet gave two shares to a horseman. The Sahibayn use the general hadith from Ibn ‘Umar stating that the Prophet gave three shares: one for the man and two for the horse. The author does not explicitly resolve the dispute here, but the text favors Abu Hanifa's view by noting the Khaybar incident. In the Hanafi school, the mufta bihi (relied-upon) position is that of Imam Abu Hanifa, as the Khaybar incident is specific and more directly relevant. The term 'faris' is derived from 'faras' (horse), and 'sahm' means share.

Key Terms
فارس (faris): Horseman; a fighter mounted on a horse during battle.
راجل (rajil): Foot soldier; a fighter on foot.
سهم (sahm): Share or portion of the spoils.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Abu Hanifa gives 2 shares to a horseman; Sahibayn give 3.
B) Abu Hanifa gives 1 share to a foot soldier; Sahibayn give 2.
C) Abu Hanifa gives no share to the horse; Sahibayn give one.
D) Both agree on 2 shares for the horseman.

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, a horseman receives two shares based on the precedent of Khaybar, despite the Sahibayn's view of three shares.

Only One Horse Gets a Share per Person
Ruling that only one horse per person receives a share in war spoils

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the number of horses eligible for a share in spoils and cite the key proof from the Sunnah.

Core Idea
Only one horse per fighter gets a share in spoils, regardless of how many he brings.

In the distribution of war spoils (ghanimah), the Hanafi school has a specific ruling regarding horses. While a fighter himself receives a full share, he also receives a share for his horse. However, if a fighter brings multiple horses, he is only compensated for one. This lesson examines the reasoning and the proof from the Sunnah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is the distribution of shares for horses in war spoils. The ruling is that a fighter receives a share for only one horse, regardless of how many he had.
2
Locate the dalil
The author cites the hadith of al-Zubayr from Dar Qutni, where the Prophet gave Zubayr four shares: one for himself, one for his relative, and two for his horse (the horse's share is two shares). Despite Zubayr having two horses, only one horse received a share.
The hadith is zanni al-thubut but qati' al-dalala for this ruling.
3
Understand the reasoning (ta'lil)
The passage gives three reasons: (1) a fighter can ride only one horse at a time, (2) giving shares for multiple horses would wrong other fighters, and (3) the precedent of al-Zubayr. These reinforce the ruling.
4
Confirm the absence of ikhtilaf
The ruling is mutually agreed upon (muttafaq alayh) among the schools; no significant dispute.
5
Apply the ruling to a scenario
If a fighter brings three horses into battle, he receives only one horse's share in the spoils. The extra horses do not entitle him to additional shares.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
[٣٠٣٧] (٥٨) ولا يسهم الا لفرس واحد.
آدمی دو یا تین گھوڑے لیکر جہاد میں گیا ہو پھر بھی صرف ایک گھوڑے کا حصہ ملے گا باقی گھوڑوں کو حصہ نہیں ملے گا۔
ایک آدمی بیک وقت ایک ہی گھوڑے پر سوار ہو کر جہاد کر سکتا ہے۔ اس لئے ایک ہی گھوڑے کا حصہ ملے گا (٢) کئی گھوڑوں کے حصے دیئے جائیں تو دوسرے مجاہدین کی حق تلفی ہوگی اس لئے ایک ہی گھوڑے کا حصہ دیا جائے گا (٣) حضرت زبیر جنگ خیبر میں دو گھوڑے لیکر شریک ہوئے تھے اس کے باوجو دان کو ایک گھوڑے کا حصہ دیا گیا۔ عن عبد الله بن الزبير عن جده انه يقول ضرب رسول الله لال عام خيبر للزبير بن العوام باربعة اسهم سهما له وسهما لذى القربي لصفية بنت عبد المطلب وسهمين لفرسه (ج) ( دارقطنی، کتاب السیر ، ج رابع ، ص ٦٢ نمبر ٤١٤٣) اس میں دیکھئے ایک ہی گھوڑے کا حصہ ملا ہے۔
[3037] (58) And only one horse receives a share. (Explanation:) Even if a person goes to jihad with two or three horses, he will only receive a share for one horse; the remaining horses will not get a share. The reason is that a person can ride only one horse at a time during battle. Therefore, only one horse's share is given. Secondly, if shares were given for multiple horses, it would wrong other mujahideen. Thirdly, al-Zubayr participated in the battle of Khaybar with two horses, yet he was given a share for only one horse. It is narrated from ‘Abdullah ibn al-Zubayr from his grandfather that he said: 'The Messenger of Allah on the day of Khaybar allotted al-Zubayr ibn al-‘Awwam four shares: one share for himself, one share for the relative (Safiyyah bint ‘Abd al-Muttalib), and two shares for his horse.' (Dar Qutni, Kitab al-Siyar, volume 4, page 62 number 4143). In this, we see he received a share for only one horse.
Source pages p. 288

Commentary
This is a supplementary ruling limiting the number of horses eligible for shares in spoils. The rule is clear: regardless of how many horses a fighter brings, he receives a share for only one horse. The author provides three reasons: (1) A fighter can only ride one horse at a time; (2) granting shares for multiple horses would unjustly reduce shares for other fighters; (3) the precedent of al-Zubayr at Khaybar, who brought two horses but received a share for only one. The hadith of Zubayr also illustrates that the share for the horse is given as two shares (the horse's share), but only for one horse. This ruling is consistent with the principle of avoiding harm to others and is based on the practice of the Prophet.

Key Terms
فرس (faras): A horse used in battle; the subject of a share in spoils.

Key Terms from Source Passage

D) Only caliphs could receive horse shares.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school rules that only one horse per fighter receives a share in spoils, based on the hadith of al-Zubayr and the reasoning of practicality and justice.

Understanding the Mention of Allah in the Khums Verse
Definitional ruling on the interpretation of the khums verse

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the mention of Allah in the khums verse (8:41) is for blessing and state the Hanafi position on the division of khums.

Core Idea
Allah's mention in the khums verse is for blessing; the actual shares are four, not five.

This lesson unpacks the Hanafi interpretation of Surah al-Anfal 8:41, where Allah is listed as a recipient of one-fifth of war booty. The author clarifies that this mention is not a literal allocation but a verbal blessing (tabarruk). Understanding this helps clarify the actual distribution of khums among the remaining recipients: the Prophet (later his treasury), relatives, orphans, needy, and travelers.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Verse and Its Literal Recipients
Read the full verse (8:41) and list the six categories mentioned: Allah, the Messenger, relatives, orphans, the needy, and the wayfarer. Note the apparent implication that Allah receives a share.
2
Recognize the Hanafi Principle: Tabarruk
Understand that the Hanafi school interprets the mention of Allah as 'li-iftitah al-kalam tabarrukan bi-ismihi'—opening the speech with His name for blessing, not as a real entitlement.
This is a hermeneutic principle based on the athar of Hasan ibn Muhammad.
3
Apply the Principle to the Verse
Since all things belong to Allah, allocating a separate share to Him is meaningless. Therefore, the verse's mention of Allah is a divine opening, and the effective shares are for the other five categories (with the Prophet's share later being allocated to the state).
4
Support with the Athar
Consider the narration from Hasan ibn Muhammad: 'This is a key to speech; Allah owns everything in the heavens and earth.' This confirms that the mention is not for allocation but for blessing.
5
Derive the Practical Division
Conclude that the khums is divided into five shares: for the Prophet (now for the state), his relatives, orphans, the needy, and travelers. Allah's mention does not create an extra sixth share.
In later Hanafi fiqh, the Prophet's share is dropped after his death, some say goes to the caliph.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وما ماذكر الله تعالى في الخمس فانما هو لافتتاح الكلام تبركا باسمه [۳۰۴۴ (۶۵) خمس کے بارے میں اللہ کا جو ذکر ہے وہ اس کے نام کے ساتھ کلام کی برکت کے لئے ہے۔ شمس کو پانچ حصوں میں تقسیم کرتے تھے۔ حالانکہ قرآن میں واعلموا انما غنمتم من شيء فان لله خمسه وللرسول الخ ہے۔ اس آیت میں اللہ کے لئے بھی شمس میں حصے کا تذکرہ ہے تو اس کے بارے میں فرمایا کہ اللہ تعالی کے لئے پوری دینا ہے اس لئے اس کا کوئی حصہ نہیں ہے۔ اللہ کا نام صرف برکت کے طور پر ہے۔ او پر اثر میں گزر چکا ہے۔ سألت الحسن بن محمد عن قول الله تعالى واعلموا انما غنمتم من شيء فان لله خمسه وللرسول (آیت ۴۱ سورة الانفال (۸) فقال هذا مفتاح كلام لله ما في الدنيا والآخرة (الف) (مستدرك للحاكم، كتاب قسم الفی ، ج ثانی، ص ۱۴۰، نمبر ۲۵۸۵ / مصنف عبدالرزاق، باب ذکر ائمس و سهم ذی القربی، ج خامس،ص ۲۳۸، نمبر ۹۴۸۲) اس اثر میں ہے کہ اللہ کا ذکر برکت کے لئے ہے۔
And what Allah mentioned regarding khums is only for opening the speech with blessing of His name. (Urdu: The mention of Allah in khums is for blessing; they used to divide khums into five parts, although the verse says '...that for Allah is a fifth of it and for the Messenger...' In this verse, a share for Allah is mentioned, so it is said that all of the world belongs to Allah, so there is no share for Him. Allah's name is only for blessing. It has passed in the athar. I asked al-Hasan ibn Muhammad about the saying of Allah: '...and know that whatever you take as spoils of war, indeed for Allah is a fifth of it and for the Messenger...' (8:41), and he said: This is a key to speech; for Allah is whatever is in the heavens and the earth. (al-Mustadrak, etc.) In this athar, the mention of Allah is for blessing.)
Source pages p. 293

Commentary
This passage is a definitional ruling explaining the legal interpretation of the verse on khums. The author clarifies that the mention of Allah in the khums verse (Surah al-Anfal 8:41) is not meant to allocate a literal share to Allah, as everything belongs to Him. Rather, it is a form of opening the speech with blessing (tabarruk). This is supported by the athar from Hasan ibn Muhammad who said, 'This is a key to speech; Allah owns everything in the heavens and earth.' Thus, the five shares of khums are actually four: for the Prophet (later dropped), his relatives, orphans, needy, and travelers. This passage introduces the concept that the Prophet's share and the relatives' share are subject to change after his death.

Key Terms
الخمس (al-khums): The one-fifth share of war booty (ghanimah) set aside for Allah, the Prophet, his relatives, orphans, needy, and travelers.
لافتتاح الكلام تبركا باسمه (li-iftitah al-kalam tabarrukan bi-ismihi): Opening the speech (verse) with the name of Allah for blessing, not to indicate a real share.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) To indicate that Allah owns the universe and deserves a share
B) For blessing when opening the speech
C) To show that the khums is divided into six shares
D) To emphasize that the Prophet's share is also for Allah

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school interprets the mention of Allah in the khums verse as a blessed opening, not a literal share; thus khums is divided among the other specified recipients.

The Prophet's Share in Khums Ceases After His Death
Ruling with proof from hadith

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the Prophet's share in khums after his death and explain the proof from the hadith of safi.

Core Idea
The Prophet's exclusive rights in khums ended with his prophethood; they do not transfer to the caliph.

This lesson addresses a unique aspect of khums distribution: the Prophet's personal right to select any item before the five-fold division. The Hanafi school holds that this right, along with the Prophet's general share, is dropped upon his death. The proof lies in a hadith that ties the right to prophethood itself. Understanding this ruling clarifies the boundaries of leadership privilege in war spoils.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling
What exactly is dropped after the Prophet's death? The passage states that both the Prophet's share (sahm an-nabi) and his special selection right (safi) are dropped.
The Urdu text says 'حضور کا حصہ ساقط ہو گیا'.
2
Locate the proof
Which hadith is cited? The proof is from 'Amir al-Sha'bi: the Prophet had a share called safi; he could choose any item before the khums division.
The hadith is from Abu Dawud and Bukhari.
3
Examine the basis
Why does the author say the right was attached to prophethood? The hadith uses 'kana li-n-nabi' (it was for the Prophet), indicating the right belonged to him due to his prophethood.
Thus, it ceases when prophethood ends.
4
Extend the ruling
How is the same reasoning applied to the Prophet's share mentioned in the Quran? The verse says 'li-r-Rasul'; since there is no Messenger after him, that share is also dropped.
This is by analogy (qiyas) on the safi ruling.
5
Note the practical consequence
What does this mean for the caliph or commander today? The caliph does not inherit any special right; he receives only the regular share of a soldier if he fights.
No personal privilege from spoils for the ruler.

وسهم النبى عليه السلام سقط بموته كما سقط الصفی [۳۰۴۵(۶۶) حضور کا حصہ ساقط ہو گیا آپ کے پردہ فرمانے سے جیسے صفی ساقط ہو گیا۔ اوپر گزر چکا ہے کہ حضور کا حصہ ان کے انتقال کے بعد ساقط ہو گیا، حضور موحق تھا کہ مال غنیمت جمع ہو تو اس میں سے جو آپ کو پسند ہو وہ لے لیں ۔ لیکن آپ کے انتقال کے بعد یہ حق خلیفہ کے لئے ساقط ہو گیا۔ اب خلیفہ یا امیر المومنین کو یہ حق نہیں ہے کہ مال غنیمت میں سے جو پسند ہو وہ لے لے۔ بلکہ مال غنیمت میں عام مجاہد کو جو حصہ ملے گا وہی حصہ امیر المومنین قتال میں شرکت کریں گے تو ملے گا۔ صفی کی دلیل یہ حدیث ہے۔ عن عامر الشعبي قال كان للنبي سهم يدعى الصفى ان شاء عبدا وان شاء امة وان شاء فرسا یختاره قبل الخمس (ب) (ابوداؤد شریف، باب ماجاء فی تھم الصلی ص ۶۴ نمبر ۲۹۹۱ / بخاری شریف ، باب غزوۃ خیبر ص ۶۰۳ نمبر (۴۲) اس حدیث سے دو باتیں معلوم ہوئیں۔ ایک تو یہ کہ حضور گو صفی کا حق تھا۔ اور کان للنبی سے معلوم ہوا کہ منتخب کرنے کا حق نبوت کی وجہ سے تھا اس لئے اب نبوت نہیں رہی تو یہ حق بھی خلیفہ کے لئے ساقط ہو گیا۔ اور اسی نبوت پر قیاس کر کے نمس میں خلیفہ کا حق بھی ساقط ہو گیا۔ کیونکہ آیت میں الرسول کا لفظ ہے۔ جب بعد میں رسول نہیں رہے تو ان کا حصہ بھی ساقط ہو جائے گا۔
The share of the Prophet (peace be upon him) is dropped with his death, just as the safi was dropped. (Urdu: The Prophet's share was dropped after his departure; he had the right to choose from the booty before division. After his death, this right is also dropped for the caliph. Now the caliph or commander of the faithful does not have this right to take whatever he likes from the spoils. Rather, the share that a common soldier gets will be the same share the commander gets if he participates in battle. The proof for safi is this hadith: From 'Amir al-Sha'bi said: The Prophet had a share called safi; if he wished, he could choose a slave, or a slave-girl, or a horse before the khums. (Abu Dawud, Bukhari) Two things are known from this hadith: first, that the Prophet had the right of safi, and 'kana li-n-nabi' indicates that the right to choose was due to prophethood, so now that prophethood is no more, this right is also dropped for the caliph. And by analogy on prophethood, the share of the caliph in khums is also dropped because the verse uses 'li-r-Rasul'; since there is no Messenger, his share is also dropped.)
Source pages p. 293

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof regarding the Prophet's share in khums. It states that the Prophet's exclusive share (sahm an-Nabi) and his right to select any item before division (safi) both cease upon his death. This is based on the hadith from Amir ash-Sha'bi that the Prophet had a share called safi which he could choose before the khums. The author argues that since this right was attached to prophethood, it does not transfer to the caliph. The ruling is also extended to the Prophet's share mentioned in the verse (li-Dhi al-Qurba), which is also dropped. The proof is that the verse uses 'li-r-Rasul' (for the Messenger); after the Messenger's death, his share is no longer applicable.

Key Terms
الصفي (as-safi): The special share of the Prophet from the booty from which he could choose any item he liked before the division of khums.
سهم النبي (sahm an-nabi): The Prophet's share from khums, which is also dropped after his death.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the basis for the Hanafi ruling that the Prophet's safi right drops after his death?
A) The caliph's authority
B) The right was attached to prophethood
C) The ummah's consensus
D) The hadith is weak

Key Takeaway
The Prophet's special rights in khums are not inherited; they cease with his death, affirming that leadership does not confer personal privileges from public war booty.
