Share of Prophet's Relatives in Khums Ceases After His Death
Ruling that the share for relatives ceases after the Prophet's death, except for poverty.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the share of the Prophet's relatives in khums after his death, identify the basis (support vs poverty), and cite the hadith proof.

Core Idea
Relatives' share in khums ceased after the Prophet's death because it was based on support, not lineage.

This lesson examines the fate of the share of the Prophet's relatives (sahm dhawil qurba) in war booty after his death. The Hanafi school holds that this share is no longer given on the basis of relationship alone; rather, it is dropped except for the poor among them. The ruling is supported by a hadith and the consensus of the Companions. Understanding this helps clarify how Khums is distributed today.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Ruling
Read the passage and determine the Hanafi position on the share of the Prophet's relatives after his death. The share is dropped, but poor relatives can still receive from khums due to poverty.
The share is not given on the basis of relationship, only need.
2
Understand the Basis During the Prophet's Lifetime
The text states that during the Prophet's life, relatives deserved the share because of their support (nusrah) for him. This is the key difference.
Support was active because the Prophet needed help in battles and spread of Islam.
3
Analyze the Dalil
Examine the hadith of Jubayr bin Mut'im. The Prophet allocated the share to Banu Hashim and Banu al-Muttalib due to their continuous support in Jahiliyyah and Islam, excluding others. This shows the basis was support, not mere kinship.
The Prophet interlinked his fingers to show unity with Banu al-Muttalib.
4
Note the Exception
After the Prophet's death, if a relative is poor (orphan, needy, traveler), they may receive from khums on that basis, but with priority due to kinship.
The poverty condition replaces the support condition.
5
Confirm with Ijma
The text mentions that the Companions agreed, during Abu Bakr and Umar's caliphates, to drop the two shares (Prophet's and relatives') and spend them on horses and equipment for jihad. This ijma strengthens the ruling.
The consensus is recorded in al-Mustadrak and Musannaf Abd al-Razzaq.

[۳۰۴۶) (۶۷) رشتہ داروں کا حصہ حضور کے زمانے میں مستحق ہوتے تھے مدد کی وجہ سے اور آپ کے بعد فقر کی وجہ سے۔ حضور کے زمانے میں آپ کے رشتہ ساروں کوشس میں سے ایک حصہ اس لئے دیا جاتا تھا کہ وہ آپ کی ہر وقت مددفرماتے تھے لیکن حاشیہ : (الف) میں نے حضرت حسن بن محمد کو اللہ تعالی کے قول و اعلموا انما عمتم من شی و فان اللہ خمسہ والرسول کے بارے میں پوچھا تو فرمایا کہ للہ کا نام اور اس کا حصہ بات شروع کرنے کے لئے ہے۔ اللہ کی تو دنیا اور آخرت بھی ہیں (ب) حضرت عامر فرماتے ہیں کہ حضور کا جو حصہ تھا اس کا نام صفی تھا۔ چاہے وہ غلام منتخب کرے چاہے باندی چاہے گھوڑا شمس نکالنے سے پہلے پسند فرمالے۔ آپ کی وفات کے بعد مدد کا سلسلہ ختم ہو گیا اس لئے رشتہ داروں کا حصہ بھی ختم ہو گیا۔ اب رشتہ داری کی بنا پر نہیں دیا جائے گا۔ البتہ ان میں سے کوئی یتیم یا مسکین یا مسافر ہو تو یتیم ہونے یا مسکین ہونے یا مسافر ہونے کی بنا پر دیا جائے گا۔ البتہ ان کو پہلے دیا جائے گا کیونکہ یہ حضور کے رشتہ دار ہیں ۔ اور اب تو وہ بھی نہیں رہے۔ تعاون کی دلیل یہ حدیث ہے۔ اخبرنی جبیر بن مطعم قال لما كان يوم خيبر وضع رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم سهم ذي القربي فی بنی هاشم و بنی المطلب و ترک بنی نوفل و بن عبد شمس، فانطلقت انا وعثمان بن عفان حتى اتينا النبي فقلنا یا رسول الله ! هؤلاء بنو هاشم لا ننكر فضلهم للمواضع الذى وضعك الله به منهم، فما بال اخواننا بنی المطلب اعطيتهم وتركتنا وقرابتنا واحدة؟ فقال رسول الله انا وبنو المطلب لا نفترق في جاهلية ولا اسلام وانما نحن وهم شيء واحد و شبک بین اصابعه (الف) (ابوداؤد شریف، باب فی مواضع قسم المس دهم ذی القربی ، ج ۲، ص ۶۰ نمبر ۲۹۸) اس حدیث میں آپ نے اشارہ فرمایا کہ زمانہ جاہلیت اور زمانہ اسلام دونوں میں بنو مطلب نے ہماری مدد کی ہے جس کی وجہ سے اس کے لئے شمس میں ایک حصہ ہے۔ اور آپ کی وفات کے بعد مدد کی ضرورت نہیں ہے اس لئے ان کا حصہ ساقط ہو جائے گا (۲) او پر مستدرک للحاکم کا بھی اثر گزرا جس میں تھا کہ اب آپ کے رشتہ داروں کے حصے ساقط ہونے پر صحابہ کا اتفاق ہو گیا۔ عبارت یہ تھی فاجتمع رأيهم على ان يجعلوا هذين السهمين في الخيل والعدة في سبيل الله فكانا علي ذالك في خلافة ابي بكر وعمر (متدرك للحاكم، كتاب قسم الفني ، ج ثانی، ص ۱۴۰، نمبر ۲۵۸۵ / مصنف عبدالرزاق، باب ذکر ائمس و سهم ذی القربي ، ج خامس، ص ۲۳۸، نمبر ۹۴۸۲)
And the share of relatives: they used to deserve it in the Prophet's time due to support (nusrah) and after him due to poverty. (Urdu: The relatives' share in the Prophet's time was given because they supported him always, but after his death, since the support is no longer needed, their share is dropped. Now it will not be given on the basis of relationship. However, if any of them is orphan, needy, or wayfarer, it will be given on that basis, but they will be given priority because they are relatives of the Prophet. But now even that is no more. The proof for support is this hadith: Jubayr bin Mut'im informed me: On the day of Khaybar, the Messenger of Allah placed the share of relatives among Banu Hashim and Banu al-Muttalib, leaving out Banu Nawfal and Banu Abd Shams. So I and Uthman bin Affan went to the Prophet and said: O Messenger of Allah, we do not deny the virtue of Banu Hashim because of the position Allah has placed you among them, but what about our brothers Banu al-Muttalib; you gave them and left us, though our relationship is the same? The Prophet said: We and Banu al-Muttalib do not separate in Jahiliyyah or Islam; we and they are one thing, and he interlinked his fingers. (Abu Dawud) In this hadith, the Prophet indicated that Banu al-Muttalib supported us in both Jahiliyyah and Islam, so they have a share in khums. After his death, support is not needed, so their share drops. Also, there is an athar from al-Mustadrak that the companions agreed to drop these two shares and spend them on horses and equipment in the path of Allah, and they followed that during the caliphates of Abu Bakr and Umar.)
Source pages p. 293

Commentary
This passage provides the ruling on the share of the Prophet's relatives (dhawil qurba) in khums. During the Prophet's lifetime, they received it because of their support for him. After his death, this share is dropped, except that if they are poor (orphans, needy, travelers), they may still receive from the khums on that basis, with priority due to their relationship. The proof is the hadith of Jubayr ibn Mut'im where the Prophet allocated the share to Bani Hashim and Bani al-Muttalib due to their support, excluding Bani Nawfal and Bani Abd Shams. The Prophet intertwined his fingers to show unity with Bani al-Muttalib in both Jahiliyyah and Islam. This shows the basis was support (nusrah). After his death, support is no longer needed, so the share drops. This consensus is reported from the companions during the caliphates of Abu Bakr and Umar, as recorded in al-Mustadrak and Musannaf Abd al-Razzaq.

Key Terms
سهم ذوي القربى (sahm dhawil qurba): The share of the Prophet's relatives in the khums of war booty.
النصرة (an-nusrah): Support given by the relatives to the Prophet, which was the basis for receiving the share during his lifetime.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) Their poverty
C) Their support for the Prophet
D) Their wealth

Key Takeaway
The share of the Prophet's relatives from khums is dropped after his death, but poor relatives may receive due to poverty, per Hanafi school.

No Khums on Booty from Unauthorized Small Raid
Ruling on booty from unauthorized small-scale raid

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on booty taken by one or two individuals without the imam's permission and explain why khums is not levied.

Core Idea
Booty from an unauthorized small raid is not ghanimah but stolen property; no khums applies.

In this lesson, we examine a specific exception to the general rule that war booty (ghanimah) requires khums. The Hanafi school distinguishes between legitimate raids authorized by the imam and unauthorized incursions by a small group. This distinction has significant implications for the distribution of spoils.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario
The passage describes one or two Muslims entering Dar al-Harb as raiders (mugheerin) without the imam's permission. This is a small-scale, unauthorized operation.
The number is specified as one or two; larger groups may fall under different rules.
2
Determine the legal status of the booty
The text states that the property taken is not considered war booty (ghanimah). Instead, it is classified as stolen property (sariqah), even though it is taken from enemy combatants.
Hanafi law treats unauthorized taking as theft, which is forbidden.
3
State the outcome
Because it is not ghanimah, the one-fifth khums is not levied. The imam has no claim to a share.
4
Understand the rationale
The reasoning is that theft is abhorrent (mubghad) even if the property belongs to enemies. Thus, the act is not a legitimate means of acquisition.
This reflects the principle that ends do not justify illegal means.
5
Note the evidence
The author alludes to a hadith from Ibn Umar (incomplete) indicating that theft is prohibited. The hadith serves as a proof that such unauthorized taking is not sanctioned.
The complete hadith may have been: 'Indeed, Allah has cursed the thief...'

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
واذا دخل الواحد والاثنان الى دار الحرب مغيرين بغير اذن الامام [۳۰۴۷ (۲۸) اگر ایک یا دو آدمی دار الحرب میں لوٹ مار کرتے ہوئے داخل ہو جا ئیں بغیر امام کی اجازت کے اور وہ کچھ لے لیں تو خمس نہیں لیا جائیگا۔ بغیر امام کی اجازت کے ایک دو آدمی لوٹ مار کرتے ہوئے داخل ہو جائیں اور تربیوں کا کچھ مال لوٹ لائیں تو اس میں سے امام شمس نہیں لے گا۔ یہ مال غنیمت کا نہیں ہے بلکہ اس طرح کرنا چوری کا مال شمار کیا جائے گا۔ اور چوری کے مال میں شمس نہیں ہے۔ کیونکہ چوری بہر حال مبغوض ہے چاہے حربیوں کے مال کی چوری کیوں نہ ہو (۲) حدیث میں اس کا اشارہ ہے۔ عن ابن عمر ان رسول الله الله قال ان کا اللہ [hadith cut off] ]
And if one or two persons enter Dar al-Harb as raiders without the imam's permission... (Urdu: If one or two men enter Dar al-Harb raiding without the imam's permission and take something, khums is not taken. The imam will not take khums from it. This is not war booty but is considered stolen property. There is no khums on stolen goods because theft is abhorrent even if it is the property of combatants. The hadith indicates this: from Ibn Umar that the Messenger of Allah said: ... [incomplete])
Source pages p. 294

Commentary
This passage presents the ruling for a specific scenario: a small number of Muslims (one or two) enter enemy territory (Dar al-Harb) without the imam's permission to raid. If they bring back booty, it is not treated as ghanimah (war booty) but as stolen property (sariqah). Consequently, no khums is taken from it. The reasoning is that such unauthorized action is akin to theft, even from enemies, as theft is generally prohibited. The author alludes to a hadith from Ibn Umar indicating that theft is not permitted, but the exact text is not fully quoted. This ruling is limited to small numbers; larger organized expeditions require imam's permission.

Key Terms
مغيرين (mugheerin): Raiders or plunderers entering enemy territory to take booty.
دار الحرب (dar al-harb): Territory under non-Muslim rule where hostilities are permitted.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) Because they are too few to fight
B) Because it is considered stolen property
C) Because the imam did not authorize it, so it is invalid
D) Because the booty is negligible

Key Takeaway
Booty from unauthorized small raids is not ghanimah and no khums is levied because it is considered stolen property.

Khums on Spoils from a Group Acting with Implied Permission
Ruling with proof on khums for a powerful group entering Dar al-Harb without permission

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on khums when a powerful group enters Dar al-Harb without explicit Imam permission, and explain the proof from the hadith of Salamah ibn Akwa'.

Core Idea
Imam's implied permission suffices for khums on spoils taken by a powerful mujahideen group.

This passage clarifies a key distinction in Hanafi siyar: not all spoils taken without the Imam's explicit permission are considered theft. When a powerful group of mujahideen, acting on the Imam's underlying intent to weaken the enemy, brings back booty, khums is wajib. The proof comes from the well-known hadith of Salamah ibn Akwa', who fought without explicit permission yet was rewarded by the Prophet with a share of the spoils, indicating implied approval and thus the application of khums.

Guided Path
1
Distinguish the two scenarios
Contrast the case of one or two individuals breaking a covenant (treachery, no khums) with a powerful group entering enemy territory. Identify which scenario matches the passage's ruling.
The 'powerful group' (jama'atun lahum man'ah) is a detachment of mujahideen, not a raiding band.
2
Identify the core legal concept
Understand the Hanafi concept of 'isharah al-idhn (implied permission). Why does the Imam's general desire to defeat the enemy create implied permission even without an explicit order?
The Imam's intent is considered: he wishes the enemy to be weakened, so an action achieving that is deemed permissible.
3
Examine the dalil from the hadith
Read the hadith of Salamah ibn Akwa'. Note that he acted without the Prophet's explicit command, yet the Prophet awarded him a share of the horseman and foot soldier. What does this indicate about the status of the spoils?
The Prophet's positive response implies approval and that the spoils were legitimate ghanimah, subject to khums.
4
Confirm the ruling and its rationale
State the Hanafi ruling: khums is levied on such spoils. Explain that the spoils are not theft because the group acted with implied permission; they are ghanimah.
The athar of Hasan al-Basri supports that if they depart without explicit permission, they are like the army (i.e., their share is as per the army, and khums is taken).
5
Note the cross-madhhab difference
Other schools (e.g., Shafi'i) may require explicit permission for khums. The Hanafi reliance on implied permission is a distinguishing feature.
The practical consequence: in the Hanafi school, the khums obligation is broader.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فاخذوا شيئا لم يخمس [۳۰۴۸ (۶۹) وان دخل جماعة لهم منعة فاخذوا شيئا حُمّسَ الغادر ينصب له لواء يوم القيامة فيقال هذه غدرة فلان بن فلان (الف) ( ابوداؤد شریف، باب فی الوفاء بالعهد ، ص ۲۳، نمبر ۲۷۵۶ / بخاری شریف، باب اثم الغادر للبر والفاجر ، ص ۴۵۲، نمبر ۳۱۸۶) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ عہد کو پورا کرنا چاہئے ۔ اور ایک دو آدمیوں نے گویا کہ چوری کر کے عہد کو توڑا اس لئے اس میں خمس نہیں لیا جائے گا۔
ات مغیرین : اغار سے مشتق ہے رات کو دھاوا بولنا، غارت گیری کرنا۔ [۳۰۴۸) (۶۹) اور اگر قوت والی جماعت داخل ہوئی اور انہوں نے کوئی چیز لی تو ٹس لیا جائے گا چاہے امام نے ان کو اجازت نہ دی ہو۔ ر قوت والی جماعت سے مراد مجاہدین کا دستہ ہے غارت گیری کرنے والی جماعت نہیں ہے۔ پس اگر مجاہدین کا دستہ امام کی اجازت کے بغیر دارالحرب چلی جائے اور جہاد کر کے مال غنیمت لے آئے تو اس میں خمس ہے۔
یہ غارت گیری نہیں ہے بلکہ جہاد ہی ہے۔ صرف اتنی بات ہے کہ امام کی اجازت کے بغیر ہے۔ کیونکہ یہ دستہ ان لوگوں سے نقیمت حاصل کیا ہے جو حربی ہیں اور جن سے جنگ جاری ہے (۲) اگر چہ امام کی جانب سے ظاہری اجازت نہیں ہے لیکن اندرونی طور پر اجازت ہے کیونکہ ایسے حالات میں امام تو چاہتے ہی ہیں کہ حربیوں کو شکست ہو اور جانی اور مالی نقصان ہو۔ اور اس دستے نے وہ کر دیا اس لئے اشارۃ اجازت موجود ہے اس لئے اس سے شمس لیا جائے گا (۳) حدیث میں حضرت سلمہ بن اکوع کی لمبی حدیث ہے جس میں انہوں نے اہل مکہ سے حضور کی اجازت کے بغیر جنگ کی ہے۔ اور حضور کے اونٹ کو بھی چھڑایا اور اہل مکہ کے سامان کو بھی مال غنیمت میں حاصل کیا۔ پھر حضور نے ان کو گھوڑ سوار اور پیدل دونوں کا حصہ عنایت فرمایا۔ جس سے معلوم ہوا کہ امام کی مراد سمجھ کر اس کی اجازت کے بغیر کوئی جماعت مال غنیمت لے آئے تو اس میں ٹمس لیا جائے گا۔ کیونکہ وہ غنیمت کا مال ہے چوری کا مال نہیں ہے۔ حدیث کا ٹکڑا یہ ہے۔ حدثنی ایاس بن سلمة عن ابيه قال اغار عبد الرحمن ابن عيينة على ابل رسول الله الا الله ... فاذا نبي الله في خمس مائة فاعطاني سهم الفارس والراجل (ب) ( ابوداؤد شریف ، باب السریة ترد علی اہل العسکر ، ص ۲۲، نمبر ۲۷۵۲ / مسلم شریف ، باب غزوة ذی قرد و غیرها، ج ۲ ص ۱۱۳ نمبر ۱۸۰۷) اس حدیث میں حضور کی اجازت کے بغیر موقع کا جہاد کیا۔ آپ نے اس سے شمس بھی لیا ہوگا۔ اور صحابی کو پیدل اور گھوڑ سوار کے حصے عنایت فرمائے ۔ اثر میں اس کا ثبوت ہے۔ عن الحسن قال اذا رحلوا باذن الامام اخذ الخمس وكان لهم ما بقى واذا رحلوا بغير اذن الامام فهو اسوة الجيش (ج) (مصنف ابن ابی هیته ۱۲ افی السرية تخرج بغیر اذن الامام تنغنم ، ج سادس ص ۴۹۹، نمبر ۳۳۲۳۱) اس اثر میں ہے کہ جیش کے برابر ہوگا یعنی نمس لیا جائے گا۔
حاشیہ : (الف) آپ نے فرمایا دھو کے دینے والے کے لئے قیامت کے دن جھنڈا نصب کیا جائے گا اور کہا جائے گا یہ فلاں کو دھوکا دینے والا ہے ( ب ) ایاس بن مسلمہ کے باپ فرماتے ہیں کہ عبد الرحمن بن عیینہ نے حضور کے اونٹ پر دھاوا بولا حضور کے سامنے پانچ سو اونٹ تھے تو مجھے گھوڑ سوار اور پیدل کا حصہ دیا (ج) حضرت حسن نے فرمایا اگر امام کی اجازت سے کوچ کرے تو شمس لیا جائے گا اور باچھی لشکر کا ہوگا۔ اور امام کی اجازت کے بغیر کوچ کرے تو سب لشکر کو جتنا ملے گا اس کو بھی اس میں سے اتنا ہی ملے گا۔
They took something, it was not made khums. [3048 (69)] And if a group with power entered and took something, khums is levied. The treacherous one will have a banner set up for him on the Day of Resurrection, and it will be said: 'This is the treachery of so-and-so, son of so-and-so.' (a) (Abu Dawud, Book of Fulfilling Covenant, p.23, no.2756 / Bukhari, Book of Sin of Treachery for Righteous and Wicked, p.452, no.3186) From this hadith it is understood that the covenant must be fulfilled. And one or two people broke the covenant as if by theft, therefore khums will not be taken from it.
Al-Mughirun: derived from aghara, meaning to raid at night, to plunder. [3048) (69) And if a powerful group entered and they took something, khums will be taken from it even if the Imam did not permit them. The meaning of 'powerful group' is a detachment of mujahideen, not a raiding band. So if a detachment of mujahideen goes to Dar al-Harb without the Imam's permission and fights and brings back booty, then khums is due on it.
This is not plunder; rather it is jihad. The only thing is that it was without the Imam's permission. Because this detachment obtained booty from those who are harbi (enemy combatants) and with whom war is ongoing. (2) Even though there is no apparent permission from the Imam, internally there is permission, because in such situations the Imam certainly wishes that the harbis be defeated and suffer loss of life and property. And this detachment did that, so implied permission exists; therefore khums will be taken from it. (3) In the hadith there is the long hadith of Hazrat Salamah bin Akwa' in which he fought the people of Makkah without the Prophet's permission. He rescued the Prophet's camel and also obtained the belongings of the people of Makkah as booty. Then the Prophet gave him the share of both the horseman and the foot soldier. From this it is understood that if a group, understanding the Imam's intent, brings booty without his permission, khums will be taken from it. Because that is booty, not stolen property. The portion of the hadith is: Haddathani Iyas bin Salamah from his father, he said: 'Abdur Rahman bin 'Uyaynah raided the camels of the Messenger of Allah... then I saw the Prophet of Allah among five hundred, and he gave me the share of the horseman and the foot soldier.' (b) (Abu Dawud, Book of the Detachment Returning to the Army, p.22, no.2752 / Muslim, Book of the Expedition of Dhi Qarad and Others, vol.2, p.113, no.1807) In this hadith, jihad was performed on the spot without the Prophet's permission. He must have taken khums from it. And the Companion was given the shares of foot soldier and horseman. There is evidence for this in the athar: From al-Hasan, he said: 'If they depart with the Imam's permission, khums is taken and the rest is for them. If they depart without the Imam's permission, then they are like the army [in sharing].' (c) (Musannaf Ibn Abi Shaybah, vol.6, p.499, no.33231) In this athar it is that they will be equal to the army, i.e., khums will be taken.
Footnote: (a) He said: For the one who deceives, a banner will be set up on the Day of Resurrection and it will be said: 'This is the one who deceived so-and-so.' (b) Iyas bin Salamah's father said: 'Abdur Rahman bin 'Uyaynah raided the Prophet's camels, the Prophet had five hundred camels, then he gave me the share of horseman and foot soldier. (c) Hazrat Hasan said: If they depart with the Imam's permission, khums will be taken and the rest is for the army. And if they depart without the Imam's permission, then whatever the whole army gets, he will also get the same amount from it.
Source pages p. 295

Commentary
This passage presents a ruling from the chapter of Siyar (military expeditions) regarding the application of khums (one-fifth share) on spoils obtained by a group of Muslims who enter enemy territory without the explicit permission of the Imam but with implied intent. The author distinguishes between a small number of individuals acting treacherously (for which no khums is due, as it is considered theft) and a powerful group of mujahideen whose actions align with the Imam's underlying desire to weaken the enemy. The key proof is the incident of Salamah ibn Akwa', who fought the Quraysh without the Prophet's explicit order but was nevertheless awarded a share of the spoils, indicating that the Prophet approved and thus khums applied. The authority weight is from Zahir al-Riwayah, as the ruling is established through well-known hadith and athar. The operative ruling (mufta bihi) is that if a group enters with implied permission, khums is levied; if they enter with the Imam's explicit permission, khums is also levied; if they enter as unauthorized plunderers, the spoils are not subject to khums and are considered stolen. The Hanafi position emphasizes the concept of 'isharah al-idhn (implied permission) based on the Imam's underlying intent. The footnote clarifies the prohibition of treachery and the distribution of shares.

Key Terms
جماعة لهم منعة (jama'atun lahum man'ah): A group with power or strength, specifically a detachment of mujahideen who can defend themselves and act effectively in enemy territory.
اشارة الاذن (isharat al-idhn): Implied permission from the Imam based on his general desire to defeat the enemy, even without explicit authorization.
خمس (khums): The one-fifth share of spoils of war that is to be distributed to the categories mentioned in the Quran (8:41).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to this passage, what is the ruling on khums when a powerful group of mujahideen enters Dar al-Harb without the Imam's explicit permission and brings back spoils?
A) No khums is taken; the spoils belong entirely to the group.
B) The spoils are considered stolen and must be returned.
C) Khums is taken because the group acted with the Imam's implied permission.
D) The ruling depends on the size of the group; if less than ten, no khums.

Key Takeaway
Khums is wajib on spoils taken by a powerful mujahideen group even without explicit Imam permission, because the group acts on the Imam's implied intent.

Ruling on a Harbi Becoming a Dhimmi and Conditions of Stay
Ruling with proof on harbi becoming dhimmi

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on when a harbi becomes a dhimmi and identify the applicable taxes and residence restrictions based on the proofs cited.

Core Idea
A harbi who stays in dar al-Islam for one year becomes a dhimmi, must pay jizya, and cannot return to dar al-harb.

This passage from the Book of Siyar clarifies the legal transition of a harbi (non-Muslim from enemy territory) who enters dar al-Islam. The Hanafi school uses the duration of stay to determine whether he remains a harbi or becomes a dhimmi, with significant implications for taxation and permanent residence. The proofs include athar from Umar and the hadith of Mu'adh.

Guided Path
1
Identify the minimum stay restriction in Hijaz
Recall that Christians and Magians may not stay in the Hijaz for more than three nights, based on an athar. This is a separate rule but part of the conditions of stay.
This applies regardless of dhimmi status.
2
Determine the harbi's status based on duration
A harbi staying less than six months: no trade tax; between six months and one year: pays ushr (one-tenth) but remains a harbi; after one full year: becomes a dhimmi, paying jizya and half-ushr (one-twentieth) on trade goods.
The athar from Umar via Ziyad ibn Hudayr provides these thresholds.
3
Identify the evidence for jizya
The hadith of Mu'adh commands taking a dinar from every adult male dhimmi, establishing the obligation of jizya.
This hadith is ahad but accepted in Hanafi fiqh; the command indicates wujub.
4
Understand the permanent residence obligation
Once a harbi becomes a dhimmi, he must live permanently in dar al-Islam and cannot return to dar al-harb.
This is part of the dhimma contract, protecting the state and ensuring compliance.
5
Note the cross-madhhab ikhtilaf
The Shafi'i school limits jizya to People of the Book (Ahl al-Kitab), while the Hanafi school extends dhimmi status and jizya to all non-Muslims who accept the contract.
This difference affects who qualifies as a dhimmi.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
أخذت منه الجزية وصار ذميًّا ولم يترك ان يرجع الى دار الحرب ولا يقيم احد منهم فوق ثلاث ليال (الف) (سنن للبیہقی ، باب الذى يمر بالحجاز مارالا یتقیم بلد منها اکثر من ثلاث ليال، ج تاسع ، ص ۱۳۵۳، نمبر ۱۸۷۶۲) اس اثر میں ہے کہ نصاری اور مجوس تین دن سے زیادہ نہ ٹھہرے (۳) اور سال ٹھہبر نے پر ذمی بنالیا جائے گا اس کی دلیل یہ اثر ہے۔ عن زياد بن حـديـر قـال كتبت الى عمر في أناس من اهل العرب يدخلون ارضنا ارض الاسلام فيقيمون قال فكتب الى عمر ان اقاموا ستة اشهر فخذ منهم العشر وان اقاموا سنة فخذ منهم نصف العشر (ب) (سن للبیہقی ، باب ما یؤ خذ من الذمی اذا اتجر فی غیر بلده والحربی از ادخل بلاد الاسلام بامان ، ج تاسع ،ص ۱۳۵۴ نمبر ۱۸۷۷) اس اثر میں ہے کہ اگر حربی سال بھر ٹھہر جائے تو اس پر نصف عشر یعنی بیسواں حصہ لازم کرو۔ اور بیسواں ذمی سے لیا جاتا ہے۔ اور دسواں حصہ حربی سے لیا جاتا ہے۔ اس لئے سال بھر ٹھہرنے سے بیسواں حصہ اور چھ ماہ ٹھہرنے سے دسواں حصہ لینے کا مطلب یہ ہوا کہ چھ مہینے تک میں حربی رہے گا اور سال بھر رہنے میں ذمی بن جائے گا۔ اور جو ذمی بن جاتا ہے اس کو ہمیشہ دار الاسلام میں رہنا پڑتا ہے۔ دار الحرب جانے کی اجازت نہیں ہوتی۔ نوں جو زمی ہوتا ہے اس کے سر پر جزیہ لازم ہوتا ہے جو ہر سال میں ایک دینار ہے۔ اور اس کی تجارت کے مال میں بیسواں حصہ خراج لازم ہوگا۔ اور مسلمانوں کی تجارت کے مال میں چالیسواں حصہ زکوۃ لازم ہوتی ہے۔ ذمی پر جزیہ لازم کرنے کی دلیل یہ حدیث ہے۔ عن معاذ ان النبي عل الله لما وجهه الى اليمن امره ان ياخذ من كل حالم يعنى محتلما دينارا او عدله من المعافري ثياب تكون باليمن (ج) (ابوداؤد شریف، باب فی اخذ الجزیۃ، ص۷۴، نمبر ۳۰۳۸ ر بخاری شریف، باب الجزية والموادعة مع اهل الذمة والحرب، ص ۴۴۶، نمبر ۳۱۵۷) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ ذمی کے سر پر جزیہ لازم کیا جائے گا۔
Jizya was taken from him and he became a dhimmi, and he was not permitted to return to the abode of war, and none of them may stay more than three nights. (alif) [Reference] In this athar it is that Christians and Magians do not stay more than three days. And if one stays a year, he will be made a dhimmi. Its evidence is this athar: From Ziyad ibn Hudayr: I wrote to Umar about some people from the people of war who enter our land, the land of Islam, and stay. He said: Umar wrote to me: If they stay six months, take from them the tenth; and if they stay a year, take from them half of the tenth. (ba) [Reference] In this athar it is that if a harbi stays a full year, then impose on him half-tenth, i.e., one-twentieth. The twentieth is taken from a dhimmi, and the tenth is taken from a harbi. So the meaning of taking one-twentieth for a year and one-tenth for six months is that he remains a harbi for six months, and if he stays a full year he becomes a dhimmi. And whoever becomes a dhimmi must always remain in dar al-Islam; he is not permitted to go to dar al-harb. Now, the dhimmi is obligated to pay jizya on his head, which is one dinar every year. And on his trade goods, one-twentieth (khiraj) is obligatory. And on Muslims' trade goods, one-fortieth (zakat) is obligatory. The evidence for imposing jizya on the dhimmi is this hadith: From Mu'adh that the Prophet, when he sent him to Yemen, commanded him to take from every mature person (meaning adult) a dinar or its equivalent from the Ma'afiri garments that are in Yemen. (jim) [Reference] From this hadith it is known that jizya will be imposed on the head of the dhimmi.
Source pages p. 298

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof from the Book of Siyar. It addresses the situation of a harbi (non-Muslim from dar al-harb) who enters dar al-Islam. The author explains that when such a person is taken as a dhimmi, he must pay jizya and cannot return to dar al-harb. There is a restriction that such people may not stay in the Hijaz for more than three nights, based on an athar from Umar. The duration of stay determines the tax: if a harbi stays six months, he pays one-tenth (ushr); if a full year, he becomes a dhimmi and pays one-twentieth (half-ushr) on trade goods. This is derived from the correspondence of Ziyad ibn Hudayr with Umar. The author then notes that a dhimmi must remain permanently in dar al-Islam and cannot go back to dar al-harb. The jizya on his head is one dinar annually, and the tax on his trade is one-twentieth, whereas Muslims pay one-fortieth as zakat. The primary proof for jizya is the hadith of Mu'adh ibn Jabal when he was sent to Yemen, where the Prophet instructed him to take a dinar or its equivalent from every adult dhimmi. This establishes the obligation of jizya on dhimmis.

Key Terms
ذمي (dhimmi): A non-Muslim subject of an Islamic state who pays jizya in return for protection and is bound by the conditions of the dhimma contract.
حربي (harbi): A non-Muslim who is not under a peace treaty and resides in dar al-harb; his life and property are not protected in dar al-Islam unless he enters with aman.
جزية (jizya): A per capita tax imposed on adult male dhimmis in the Islamic state as a condition of their protection and exemption from military service.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what happens to a harbi who stays in dar al-Islam for one year?
A) He must leave immediately.
B) He becomes a dhimmi and pays jizya.
C) He pays one-tenth on trade.
D) He is exempt from all taxes.

Key Takeaway
A harbi who stays a full year in dar al-Islam becomes a dhimmi, liable for jizya and half-ushr, and must reside permanently; stay less than a year but over six months incurs ushr only.

Consequences of a Dhimmi Returning to Dar al-Harb: Loss of Protection and Permissibility of Blood
Ruling with evidence from Khaybar hadith

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on a dhimmi who returns to dar al-harb and analyze the evidence from the Khaybar hadith.

Core Idea
Breaking the dhimma covenant by returning to dar al-harb makes the dhimmi a harbi and his blood mubah.

A dhimmi enjoys protection (dhimma) in exchange for jizya and adherence to Islamic law, but this contract is conditional. This lesson explores the consequence when a dhimmi violates that condition by returning to dar al-harb. Understanding this ruling clarifies the sanctity of treaties in Islamic law and the limits of aman (protection).

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Determine what action is being ruled upon (the dhimmi's return to dar al-harb) and what the legal consequence is (he becomes a harbi, his blood becomes mubah).
The ruling is about the change in status, not a specific act of worship.
2
Locate the dalil (evidence)
Find the primary evidence cited: the hadith of Khaybar where the Jews concealed property and were punished. Identify the specific clause that proves the principle.
The hadith is from Sunan Abi Dawud, and an athar from Musannaf Abd al-Razzaq is also referenced.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah (legal link)
Explain how the hadith's clause 'fa in fa'alu fa la dhimma lahum wa la 'ahd' (if they do, then no protection and no covenant) directly supports that violation of a condition nullifies the dhimma, and the subsequent killing proves the blood becomes mubah.
The analogy is: just as the Khaybar Jews violated the treaty by hiding property, a dhimmi violates by returning to dar al-harb.
4
Note the ikhtilaf (scholarly disagreement)
Identify that some non-Hanafi scholars hold that return alone does not make blood mubah unless the dhimmi actually fights. The Hanafi position considers the return itself as breach of contract.
This is a legitimate ikhtilaf based on differing interpretations of what constitutes violation.
5
Determine the tarjih (preferred view)
The relied-upon (mufta bihi) Hanafi position is that the dhimmi becomes a harbi immediately upon return, making his blood and property permissible. This is from Zahir al-Riwayah.
The evidence from the Khaybar hadith is considered strong enough.

[۳۰۵۱) (۷۲) اگر دار الحرب لوٹ گیا اور مسلمان یا ذمی کے پاس امانت چھوڑ گیا یا ان کے ذمہ قرض چوڑ گیا تو واپس جانے کی وجہ سے اس کا خون مباح ہوگا۔ جو حربی دار الاسلام میں آکر زمی بن گیا اس کے لئے شرط یہ ہے کہ وہ دار الحرب واپس نہ جائے۔ لیکن اگر چلا گیا تو شرط توڑنے کی وجہ سے ذمی نہیں رہا بلکہ حربی ہو گیا اور اس کا خون مباح ہو گیا۔ زمی کو دار الحرب میں گھر بنانے کی اجازت دی جائے تو وہ جاسوسی کرے گا اور ہمارے خلاف تعاون کرے گا اس لئے یا ذمی بن کر حاشیہ : (الف) حضرت عمر نے یہود، نصاری، اور مجوس کے لئے مدینے میں تین دن ٹھہرنے کا متعین کیا کہ وہ خرید و فروخت کریں۔ اور اپنی ضرورت پوری کریں۔ اور ان میں سے کوئی تین دن سے زیادہ نہ ٹھہریں (ب) زیاد بن جدیر کہتے ہیں کہ میں نے حضرت عمر کو لکھا کہ اہل حرب کے کچھ لوگ دار الاسلام میں آتے ہیں اور ٹھہرتے ہیں۔ فرمایا حضرت عمر نے ہمیں جواب دیا اگر وہ چھ مہینے ظہر میں تو ان سے دسواں حصہ لو۔ اور اگر ایک سال ٹھہر میں تو ان سے بیسواں حصہ لو جو زمی سے لیا جاتا ہے ( ج ) حضور نے جب حضرت معاذ کو یمن کی طرف روانہ کیا تو انکو حکم دیا کہ ہر بالغ ذمی سے ایک دیناریا اس کے برابر معافری کپڑا لیں جو یمن میں ہوتا ہے۔

عاد الى دار الحرب وترك وديعة عند مسلم او ذمى او دينا في ذمتهم فقد صار دمه مباحا بالعود [۳۰۵۲ (۷۳) وما في دار الاسلام من ماله على خطر فان أُسِرَ او ظهر على دار الاسلام میں ہمیشہ رہے یا دار الحرب میں رہائش پذیر ہو جائے اور حربی ہو جائے۔ پس اگر وہ حربی ہو گیا تو اس پر حربی کا حکم جاری ہوگا اور وہ یہ کہ اس کو قتل کرنا حلال ہو گا (۲) شرط کے خلاف کرنے سے مباح الدم ہو جاتا ہے حدیث میں اس کا ثبوت ہے۔ عن ابن عمر ان النبی قاتل اهل خيبر فغلب على الارض والنخل والجاهم الى قصرهم فصالحوه على ان لرسول الله الله الصفراء والبيضاء والحلقة ولهم ما حملت ركابهم على ان لا يكتموا ولا يغيبوا شيئا فان فعلوا فلا ذمة لهم ولا عهد فغيبوا مسكا لحيى بن اخطب ... فوجدوا المسک فقتل ابن ابی الحقیق وسبى نساء هم وذراريهم (الف) (ابوداؤد شریف، باب ما جاء فی حکم ارض خیبر، ص ۶۸ نمبر ۳۰۰۶) اس حدیث میں حی بن اخطب کے مشک کو چھپا کر عہد کی خلاف ورزی کی تو ابن ابی حقیق کو قتل کیا گیا اور اس کی اولاد کو قید کر لیا گیا۔ اسی طرح یہاں ذمی نے عہد کی خلاف ورزی کی تو وہ حربی بن جائے گا اور اس کا خون مباح ہو جائے گا (۳) اثر میں ہے۔ سئل عن عطاء عن الرجل من اهل الذمة يوخذ في اهل الشرك وقد اشترط عليهم ان لا يأتيهم فيقول لم اردعونهم فكره قتله الا ببينة فقال له بعض اهل العلم اذا نقض شيئا واحدا مما عليه فقد نقض الصلح (ب) (مصنف عبدالرزاق، باب المشرک یا تی المسلم بغیر عہد، ج خامس ، ص ۲۹۳، نمبر ۹۲۵۴) اس اثر سے معلوم ہوا کہ ذمی حربیوں کے درمیان چلا جائے تو عہد ٹوٹ گیا اس لئے وہ حربی ہو گیا اور اس کا خون حربیوں کی طرح مباح ہو گیا۔
اصول یہ مسئلہ اس اصول پر ہے کہ جو دار الحرب بھاگ گیا وہ حربی ہو گیا اور اس کا خون اور اس کا مال مباح ہو گیا۔
ورية : امانت
[۳۰۵۲ (۷۳) اور جو دار الاسلام میں اس کا مال ہو وہ خطرے میں ہو گیا۔ پس اگر قید کر لیا گیا یا دار الحرب پر غلبہ ہو گیا اور قتل کیا گیا تو اس کا قرض ساقط ہو جائے گا اور امانت غنیمت ہو جائے گی۔
یہ آدمی حربی ہو گیا اور جنگ کرنے بھی آیا اور وہ قید ہو گیا یا قتل کیا گیا تو اس کا جو کسی کے پاس قرض تھا وہ اس کا ہو جائے گا اور جو مال کسی کے پاس امانت تھا وہ غنیمت میں آجائے گا۔ اور جو مال دار لاسلام کے ورثہ کے پاس تھا وہ آپس میں تقسیم کرلیں گے۔ قرض کا مال قرض والے کے پاس اس لئے رہ جائے گا کہ مال مباح پر جس کا قبضہ ہو جائے وہ اسی کا ہو جاتا ہے۔ یہاں قرض والے کا پہلے
حاشیہ : (الف) آپ نے اہل خیبر سے جنگ کی اور زمین اور باغات پر قابض ہو گئے۔ اور ان کو قلعے میں بند رہنے پر مجبور کیا۔ انہوں نے حضور سے سونا، چاندی اور حلقہ پر صلح کی۔ اور یہودیوں کے لئے وہ ہو گا جو ان کی سواری لے جاسکے اس شرط پر کہ وہ کچھ نہ چھپائیں گے اور نہ کوئی چیز غائب کریں گے۔ اور اگر انہوں نے چھپایایا غائب کیا تو نہ کوئی ذمہ دار رہے گا اور نہ عہد رہے گا۔ پھر بھی جی بن اخطب کا مشک نائب کیا... چنانچہ مشک ملا تو تو ابن ابی اتحقیق کو قتل کیا ان کی بیویوں اور اولاد کو قید کیا (ب) حضرت عطاء سے پوچھا کوئی ذمی مشرکین کے درمیان ملے حالانکہ اس پر شرط لگائی گئی تھی کہ ان کے پاس نہ جائے۔ پس ذمی کہتا ہے کہ میں ان کی مدد کے لئے نہیں آیا ہوں۔ تو بغیر گواہی کے حضرت عطاء نے اس کے قتل کو مکروہ قراردیا۔ ان سے بعض اہل علم نے کہا شرائط میں سے کسی شرط کو توڑا تو صلح ٹوٹ گئی۔
[3051] (72) If he returns to dar al-harb and leaves a trust with a Muslim or a dhimmi, or a debt owed to them, then due to his return his blood becomes permissible (mubah). The condition for a harbi who comes to dar al-Islam and becomes a dhimmi is that he must not return to dar al-harb. But if he goes, due to breaking the condition he is no longer a dhimmi, but becomes a harbi, and his blood becomes mubah. If a dhimmi is permitted to build a house in dar al-harb, he will spy and cooperate against us. Therefore, either as a dhimmi... Footnote (alif): Umar determined that Jews, Christians, and Magians may stay in Medina for three nights to buy and sell and fulfill their needs, and none of them may stay more than three nights. (ba) Ziyad ibn Hudayr said: I wrote to Umar that some people of war come to dar al-Islam and stay. Umar replied: If they stay six months, take from them the tenth; and if they stay a year, take from them the twentieth which is taken from a dhimmi. (jim) The Prophet, when he sent Mu'adh to Yemen, commanded him to take from every adult dhimmi a dinar or its equivalent from Ma'afiri garments in Yemen. ... He returned to dar al-harb and left a trust with a Muslim or a dhimmi, or a debt in their liability, so due to the return his blood becomes mubah. [3052] (73) And whatever property he has in dar al-Islam is at risk. So if he is captured or becomes apparent over... In dar al-Islam he must always stay, or he takes residence in dar al-harb and becomes a harbi. So if he becomes a harbi, the ruling of harbi applies to him, i.e., killing him is halal. (2) By violating the condition he becomes mubah ad-dam. There is proof from a hadith: From Ibn Umar that the Prophet fought the people of Khaybar, conquered the land and date palms, and forced them to their fort. They made peace with him on condition that for the Messenger of Allah is the yellow, the white, and the weapons, and for them what their mounts carry, provided they do not conceal or hide anything; if they do, then there is no protection and no covenant. They hid a leather bag of Huyayy ibn Akhtab... They found the bag, so Ibn Abi al-Haqiq was killed and their women and children were taken captive. (alif) (Abu Dawud, Bab ma ja'a fi hukm ard Khaybar, p. 68, no. 3006) In this hadith, Huyayy ibn Akhtab hid the leather bag and violated the covenant, so Ibn Abi al-Haqiq was killed and his children were captured. Similarly, here the dhimmi violated the covenant, so he becomes a harbi and his blood becomes mubah. (3) There is an athar: 'Ata' was asked about a man from ahl al-dhimma who is found among the people of shirk, though it was stipulated to him that he should not go to them. He says: I did not intend to aid them. 'Ata' disliked killing him without evidence. Some scholars said to him: If he violates any one condition, he has broken the peace. (ba) (Musannaf Abd al-Razzaq, Bab al-mushrik ya'ti al-muslim bi-ghayr 'ahd, vol. 5, p. 293, no. 9254) From this athar it is known that a dhimmi who goes among the harbis breaks the covenant, so he becomes a harbi and his blood becomes mubah like that of harbis. The principle (asl) of this issue is that whoever flees to dar al-harb becomes a harbi, and his blood and property become mubah. Wariyyah: trust. [3052] (73) And whatever property he has in dar al-Islam becomes at risk. So if he is captured or dar al-harb is conquered and he is killed, then his debt lapses and the trust becomes booty. This man became a harbi and also came to fight, and he was captured or killed. Then whatever debt he had with someone becomes his (the debtor's?), and whatever property was with someone as a trust becomes booty. And whatever property was with heirs in dar al-Islam, they will divide it among themselves. The debt property remains with the debtor because property that becomes mubah and is seized becomes the property of the one who seizes it. Here, the debtor's... Footnote (alif): The Prophet fought the people of Khaybar, conquered the land and gardens, forced them to their fort. They made peace with him on condition that the gold, silver, and weapons are for the Messenger, and for them what their mounts carry, provided they do not conceal or hide anything; if they conceal or hide, then no protection and no covenant. Then Huyayy ibn Akhtab's leather bag was hidden... They found the bag, so Ibn Abi al-Haqiq was killed, and their women and children were captured. (ba) 'Ata' was asked: A dhimmi is found among the polytheists, though it was stipulated that he should not go to them. The dhimmi says: I did not come to aid them. 'Ata' disliked killing him without evidence. Some scholars said to him: If he breaks any one condition, the peace is broken.
Source pages p. 298

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof from the Book of Siyar, addressing the consequences when a dhimmi violates the dhimma contract by returning to dar al-harb. The author explains that the condition for a harbi who becomes a dhimmi is that he must not return to dar al-harb. If he does return, he breaks the condition, ceases to be a dhimmi, and becomes a harbi, making his blood permissible (mubah ad-dam). This is supported by the hadith of Khaybar: when the Jews of Khaybar concealed property, they violated the treaty, and the Prophet killed Ibn Abi al-Haqiq and took their women and children captive. Similarly, a dhimmi who goes to dar al-harb violates the covenant and becomes a harbi. Further evidence comes from an athar where 'Ata' was asked about a dhimmi found among polytheists despite a condition against it; some scholars stated that breaking any condition voids the peace. The principle is that whoever flees to dar al-harb becomes a harbi, and his blood and property become permissible. The author then discusses the fate of the dhimmi's property in dar al-Islam: if he is captured or killed, his debts become void (or are treated as the debtor's property) and any trusts he left behind become part of the spoils (ghanimah). The reasoning is that property that becomes mubah and is seized belongs to the seizer. This ruling underscores the sanctity of the dhimma contract and the severe consequences of violating it.

Key Terms
مباح الدم (mubah ad-dam): A legal status where killing a person is permissible without legal consequence, usually due to loss of protected status (e.g., becoming a harbi).
عهد (ahd): Covenant or treaty; in this context, the dhimma contract that guarantees protection in exchange for jizya and adherence to Islamic law.
غنيمت (ghanimah): Booty captured from the enemy in warfare; here, the property left behind by the dhimmi who became a harbi becomes part of the spoils.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the hadith of Khaybar, what was the specific violation that led to the nullification of the treaty?
A) The Jews refused to pay jizya.
B) The Jews concealed a leather bag (misak).
C) The Jews attacked Muslim caravans.
D) The Jews broke the treaty by leaving Khaybar.

Key Takeaway
A dhimmi who returns to dar al-harb breaks the dhimma contract and becomes a harbi, making his blood and property mubah, as established by the Khaybar hadith and the principle that fleeing to enemy territory forfeits protection.

Distinction Between Ghanimah and Fay'
Ruling on spoils taken by force vs. booty from peace

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between ghanimah and fay' and state the Hanafi ruling for each, including the treatment of khums and distribution.

Core Idea
Property taken by force is ghanimah with khums; property obtained without fighting is fay' for public welfare.

In Islamic law, not all spoils are treated equally. The Hanafi school draws a fundamental distinction between ghanimah — goods seized through combat — and fay' — assets acquired by peace or submission. This ruling has direct implications for the distribution of wealth and the role of the treasury (bayt al-mal). In this lesson, we explore the definition, evidence, and practical application of these two categories.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two categories
Recognize ghanimah vs. fay' based on the method of acquisition: fighting vs. no fighting.
Ghanimah requires force; fay' comes from peace or fear.
2
State the Hanafi ruling for each
For ghanimah: one-fifth (khums) for specified recipients, four-fifths for fighters. For fay': entire amount to public treasury for Muslim welfare.
Fay' is treated like kharaj.
3
Examine the evidence
Analyze Surah al-Hashr 59:7 and the hadith of Abu Hurairah and the peace of Najran.
The verse forbids circulation among the rich; hadith distinguishes conquered towns.
4
Apply the distinction to a scenario
Classify a given situation as ghanimah or fay' and determine the distribution.
Consider whether fighting occurred or the enemy submitted peacefully.
5
Understand the practical consequence
Recognize how this distinction affects state finances and incentives for fighters.
Misclassification can lead to unjust distribution.

(۳۰۵۳) (۷۴) مسلمانوں نے جو کچھ اہل حرب کا مال لیا بغیر قتال کے تو وہ مسلمانوں کی مصلحت میں خرچ کیا جائے گا، جیسے کہ خراج کا مال خرچ کیا جاتا ہے۔ اگر تربیوں سے قتال کر کے مال لیا تو یہ مال غنیمت ہے۔ اس میں سے پانچواں نمس نکال کر اس کومساکین، یتیم اور مسافروں پر خرچ کیا جائے گا۔ اور باقی چار حصے مجاہدین میں تقسیم کر دیئے جائیں گے۔ اس کی دلیل او پر گزرچکی۔ اور قتال کے بغیر صرف رعب سے وہ لوگ جھک گئے اور صلح کرلی تو اس مال کوئی کہتے ہیں۔ اس میں سے پانچواں حصہ نکال کر باقی چار حصے مجاہدین میں تقسیم نہیں کریں گے۔ بلکہ پورا مال بیت المال میں جمع کر دیا جائے گا اور مسلمانوں کی مصلحت میں خرچ کیا جائے گا۔ جس طرح خراج کا مال مسلمانوں کی مصلحتوں میں خرچ کیا جاتا ہے۔ مال غنیمت اور مال فی کا فرق اس اثر میں مذکور ہے۔ عن الثوري قال الفى والـغـنيـمـة مـخـتـلـفـان، اما الغنيمة فما اخذ حاشیه : (الف) اسمرا بن مضرس فرماتے ہیں کہ میں حضور کے پاس آیا اور اس سے بیعت کی تو فرمایا جہاں مسلمان نہ پہنچا ہو وہاں کوئی پہنچ جائے تو وہ چیز اس کی ہے (ب) آپ نے اہل خیبر سے جنگ کی ، پس زمین اور باغات پر قابض ہو گئے تو لوگوں نے مشک پایا اس لئے ابن ابی الحقیق کوقتل کیا ، ان کی بیویاں اور بچے قید کئے گئے۔

الشرح الثميرى الجزء الرابع
۲۹۴
كتاب السير
المسلمون من اموال اهل الحرب بغير قتال يُصرف فى مصالح المسلمين كما يُصرف الخراج .
المسلمون فصار فى ايديهم من الكفار والخمس فى ذلك الى الامير يضعه حيث ما امر الله ، والاربعة الاخماس الباقية للذين غنموا الغنيمة، والفئ ما وقع من صلح بين الامام والكفار في اعناقهم وارضهم وزرعهم وفيما صولحوا عليه مما لم يأخذه المسلمون عنوة، ولم يحوزوه ولم يقهروه عليه حتى وقع في بينهم صلح، قال فذلک الصلح الى الامام يــضــعـه حيث امر الله (الف) (مصنف عبدالرزاق، باب الغنيمتة والفی مختلفان ، ج خامس، ص ۱۳۱۰ نمبر ۹۷۱۵) اس اثر میں مال غنیمت اور مال فی کو الگ الگ بیان کیا گیا ہے اور بتایا کہ صلح کے مال کو مال فی کہتے ہیں۔ مال فی کو امور المسلمین میں خرچ کرے اس کی دلیل یہ آیت ہے۔ ما الفاء الله على رسوله من اهل القرى فلله وللرسول ولذى القربى واليتامى والمساكين وابن السبيل كي لا يكون دولة بين الاغنياء منكم (ب) ( آیت ۷ سورۃ الحشر (۵۹) اس آیت میں ہے۔ اللہ نے جوفی دیا وہ رشتہ داروں، قیموں، مسکینوں اور مسافروں کے لئے ہے۔ جس سے معلوم ہوا کہ اس میں شمس بھی نہیں ہے۔ اور مجاہدین میں بھی تقسیم نہیں کیا جائے گا، بلکہ امت کی مصلحت میں خرچ کیا جائے گا (۲) حدیث میں اس کی تائید ہے۔ عـن ابــی هــيـرة ان رسول الله الله قال ايماقرية افتتحها الله ورسوله فهى لله ولرسوله ، وايما قرية افتتحها المسلمون عنوة فخمسها لله ولرسوله وبقيتها لم قاتل عليها (ج) (سن المسبقی ، باب من رای قسمتة الاراضى المعلومة ومن لم يرها، ج تاسع ص ۲۳۴، نمبر ۱۸۳۹۳) اس حدیث میں ہے جس کو مجاہدین نے فتح کیا اس میں مجاہدین کے چار حصے ہیں، اور جس کو مجاہدین نے فتح نہیں کیا بلکہ مسلمانوں کے رعب سے دشمن نے صلح کر لی وہ سب مال نوائب السلمین کے لئے ہوگا اور اس کی مصلحتوں میں خرچ کیا جائے گا (۳) حدیث میں ہے۔ عن ابن عباس قال صالح رسول الله لا لا اله اهل نجران على الفئ حلة النصف في صفر والنصف في رجب يودونها الى المسلمين (د) (ابوداؤد شریف ، باب فی اخذ الجزية ، ج ۲ ص ۷۴، نمبر ۳۰۴۱) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ اہل نجران سے جو صلح ہوئی تھی اس مال میں شمس نہیں لیا جاتا تھا۔ اور نہ مجاہدین میں تقسیم ہوتا تھا۔ بلکہ پورا مال مسلمانوں کے کام آتا تھا۔
اوف : گھوڑا دوڑانا، یہاں مراد ہے دوڑ کر مال جمع کر لیتا۔
حاشیہ : (الف) حضرت ثوری نے فرمایا نئی اور نیمت الگ الگ مال ہیں۔ نقیمت اس کو کہتے ہیں کہ مسلمان نے کفار سے قبضے میں لیا۔ اس کا نفس امیر کو دیا جاتا ہے۔ اللہ نے اس کو جیسا حکم دیا وہاں خرچ کرے۔ اور باقی چار ٹس ان لوگوں کے لئے ہے جنہوں نے غنیمت حاصل کی۔ اور فی یہ ہے کہ امام اور کفار کے درمیان صلح کی وجہ سے کفار کی ذات پر، اس کی زمین پر اور اس کی کھیتی پر لازم ہو، جس مال پر بھی صلح ہوئی ہو جس کو مسلمانوں نے بزور طاقت نہ لی ہو اور نہ اس پر قبضہ کیا ہو۔ یہاں تک کہ آپس میں صلح ہوگئی ہو۔ یہ صلح کا مال امام کی ذمہ داری ہے کہ اللہ نے جیسا حکم دیا وہاں خرچ کرے (ب) اللہ نے اپنے رسول کو جو کچھ اہل قری کافی دیا تو وہ اللہ اور رسول کے لئے ہے۔ اور رشتہ داروں کے لئے اور قیموں، مسکینوں اور مسافروں کے لئے ہے تا کہ تمہارے مالداروں کے درمیان دولت نہ بن جائے (ج) آپ نے فرمایا کسی گاؤں کو اللہ رسول نے فتح کیا تو وہ اللہ اور رسول کے لئے ہے۔ اور کسی گاؤں को مسلمانوں نے زبر دستی فتح کیا تو اس کا شمس اللہ اور رسول کے لئے ہے اور باقی اس کے لئے ہے جس نے اس پر قتال کیا (د) آپ نے اہل نجران سے دو ہزار ملے پر صلح کی آدھا صفر مہینے میں اور آدھار جب میں مسلمان کو ادا کریں گے۔
(3053) (74) Whatever property of the people of war the Muslims take without fighting, it will be spent for the welfare of the Muslims, just as kharaj property is spent. If they take property from the enemies by fighting, then it is ghanimah. From it, one-fifth (khums) is taken and given to the poor, orphans, and travellers. The remaining four-fifths are distributed among the mujahidin. Its evidence has passed earlier. And if without fighting, only by awe they submit and make peace, then that property is called fay'. From it, one-fifth is not taken, nor are the remaining four-fifths distributed among the mujahidin. Rather, the entire property is collected in the treasury (bayt al-mal) and spent for the welfare of the Muslims, just as kharaj property is spent for the welfare of the Muslims. The difference between mal ghanimah and mal fay' is mentioned in this athar: From al-Thawri who said: Fay' and ghanimah are different: as for ghanimah, it is what the Muslims take from the property of the people of war by force, and it is spent for the welfare of the Muslims like kharaj. The Muslims came into possession of it from the disbelievers, and the khums of that goes to the commander to place where Allah commanded, and the remaining four-fifths are for those who gained the ghanimah. And fay' is what occurs from a peace treaty between the imam and the disbelievers concerning their persons, land, crops, and what they make peace upon that the Muslims did not take by force, nor did they gain possession of it, nor did they overcome it until peace occurred between them. He said: That peace is for the imam to place where Allah commanded. (a) (Musannaf 'Abd al-Razzaq, chapter on ghanimah and fay' being different, vol. 5, p. 1310, no. 9715) In this athar, mal ghanimah and mal fay' are separately explained and it is stated that the property of peace is called mal fay'. The evidence for spending mal fay' on Muslim affairs is this verse: 'What Allah has given as fay' to His Messenger from the people of the towns, it is for Allah and for the Messenger and for the near relatives and the orphans and the needy and the wayfarer, so that it may not become a circulation among the rich of you.' (Surah al-Hashr 59:7) This verse indicates that it has no khums and will not be distributed among mujahidin, but spent for the welfare of the Ummah. (2) A hadith supports this: From Abu Hurairah that the Messenger of Allah, peace be upon him, said: 'Any town that Allah and His Messenger conquer, it is for Allah and His Messenger. And any town that the Muslims conquer by force, its khums is for Allah and His Messenger, and the rest is for those who fought for it.' (c) (Sunan al-Bayhaqi, chapter on those who saw division of known lands and those who did not, vol. 9, p. 234, no. 18393) This hadith states that what the mujahidin conquer, they have four-fifths; and what they do not conquer but the enemy makes peace out of awe, all that property is for the welfare of the Muslims and spent for their benefit. (3) A hadith: From Ibn 'Abbas: The Messenger of Allah, peace be upon him, made peace with the people of Najran on a payment of two thousand garments, half in Safar and half in Rajab, to be paid to the Muslims. (d) (Sunan Abi Dawud, chapter on taking jizyah, vol. 2, p. 74, no. 3041) This hadith shows that the property from peace with Najran did not have khums taken nor was it distributed among mujahidin, but the whole property went to the Muslims' benefit. Auf: to spur a horse; here meaning to collect property by running.
Source pages p. 300

Commentary
This passage explains the crucial Hanafi distinction between ghanimah (war spoils taken by force) and fay' (booty obtained without fighting, typically by peace treaty or due to the enemy's fear). The ruling is: Ghanimah is subject to khums (one-fifth) which is distributed to the categories mentioned in the Quran (poor, orphans, etc.), and the remaining four-fifths are distributed among the mujahidin who fought. Fay', on the other hand, is not subject to khums nor distributed to mujahidin; instead, the entire amount goes to the Muslim treasury (bayt al-mal) and is spent for the general welfare of the Muslims, similar to kharaj (land tax from non-Muslims). The proof comes from several sources: (1) An athar from al-Thawri explicitly distinguishing the two, quoting that fay' is from peace treaties where Muslims did not gain possession by force. (2) The Quranic verse 59:7 which allocates fay' to specific categories (Allah, Messenger, relatives, orphans, needy, wayfarers) and indicates it is not to become a circulation among the rich, implying it goes to the public welfare. (3) A hadith from Abu Hurairah distinguishing towns conquered by force (four-fifths to fighters) from those conquered by Allah and His Messenger (full amount for public welfare). (4) The hadith of the peace treaty with Najran, where the annual payment was not treated as ghanimah. The lexical note explains 'auf' (spurring) in the context of collecting property swiftly. All rulings are presented within the Hanafi school without intra-madhhab dispute.

Key Terms
غ نی م ت (ghanimah): Spoils taken by force from enemy combatants through fighting.
ف ي ء (fay'): Property obtained from non-Muslims without fighting, such as through peace treaties or when the enemy submits out of fear.
خراج (kharaj): Land tax imposed on non-Muslim subjects of the Islamic state.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If the enemy surrenders out of fear without fighting, and the imam makes a peace treaty with them, how is the property (e.g., jizyah or tribute) treated according to Hanafi fiqh?
A) It is ghanimah, one-fifth for khums, four-fifths for fighters.
B) It is fay', not subject to khums, and all goes to public treasury for Muslim welfare.
C) It is divided equally between fighters and the treasury.
D) It is returned to the enemy.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school distinguishes ghanimah (force) from fay' (peace), with ghanimah subject to khums and fighter distribution, while fay' goes entirely to the public treasury.

All Land of Arabia is 'Ushr Land
Ruling that all Arabian land is 'ushri with hadith proofs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that all land of Arabia is 'ushr land and explain the proof from hadith that supports it.

Core Idea
Since no non-Muslim may reside in Arabia, kharaj is impossible; thus all land is 'ushri.

This passage establishes a central Hanafi position regarding land taxation in Arabia. The matn declares that all land of Arabia is 'ushr land, meaning the produce is subject to a 10% tithe rather than kharaj (land tax). The commentary explains the reasoning: kharaj is imposed on non-Muslim landowners, but non-Muslims are not permitted to reside permanently in Arabia. Therefore, the only applicable tax is 'ushr. Two hadiths are cited to support this prohibition of non-Muslim residence. This lesson unpacks the proof and the implications for land classification.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling
The matn states 'All land of Arabia is 'ushr land.' Recognize that this is a definitive classification for tax purposes.
2
Understand the key distinction
Differentiate between 'ushr land (tithe) and kharaj land (land tax). Kharaj applies when non-Muslims own land; 'ushr applies when Muslims own land. Since non-Muslims cannot reside permanently in Arabia, kharaj is inapplicable.
This is the core reasoning of the Hanafi school.
3
Examine the hadith proofs
Two hadiths are cited: (1) The command to expel polytheists from Arabia (Bukhari, Muslim). (2) The prohibition of two religions remaining in Arabia (Bayhaqi, mursal). Both indicate that non-Muslims have no permanent place in Arabia.
4
Analyze the wajh al-dalalah
The command to expel implies that no non-Muslim may reside permanently; thus, there can be no kharaj. The prohibition of two religions reinforces that only Islam may be established, precluding any non-Muslim land ownership.
The dalala is qati' (definitive) despite zanni thubut.
5
Note cross-madhhab difference
Some Shafi'i scholars consider parts of Arabia as kharaj land if conquered by force. The Hanafi school rejects this because the categorical prohibition of non-Muslim residence overrides any classification based on conquest.
This is a legitimate ikhtilaf based on different usul principles.

كتاب السير
[۳۰۵۴) (۷۵) وارض العرب كلها ارض عشر
۳۰۵۴۱ (۷۵) عرب کی زمین کل کی کل عشری ہیں۔
عشری اور خراجی زمین کے احکام کے
ی عرب میں دوسرا دین رکھنا جائز نہیں ہے۔ اور خراج اس وقت ہوتا ہے جب وہاں کا فررہائش پذیر ہوا اور عرب میں کافر کا رکھنا جائز دوسرا جائز نہیں اور ہوتاہے وہاں پذیر ہوا میں کا رھنا نہیں۔ اس لئے اس پر خراج لگانا بھی جائز نہیں۔ اس لئے وہ ساری زمینیں عشری ہیں۔
حدیث میں ہے کہ جزیرہ عرب سے تمام مشرکین کو نکال دو۔ عن ابن عباس انه قال يوم الخميس وما يوم الخميس . اخرجوا المشركين من جزيرة العرب (الف) ( بخاری شریف ، باب هل يستشفع الى اهل الذمة ومعا متهم ص ۲۲۹، نمبر ۳۰۵۳ ر مسلم شریف ، باب ترک الوصیۃ لمن لیس لہ شیء یوصی فیہ، ص ۴۲، نمبر ۱۶۳۷) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ مشرکین کو عرب سے نکال دو اس لئے وہ عشری ہے (۲) حدیث میں ہے۔ سمع عمر بن عبد العزيز يقول بلغنى انه كان آخر ماتكلم به رسول الله الله ان قال قاتل الـلـه اليهود والنصارى اتخذوا قبور انبيائهم مساجد، لايبقين دينان بارض العرب (ب) (سن للبیہقی ، باب لا یسکن ارض الحجاز مشرک ، ج تاسع ، ص ۱۳۵۰، نمبر ۱۸۷۵۰) اس حدیث مرسل سے بھی تائید ہوتی ہے کہ عرب کی زمین عشری ہے۔ یعنی اس زمین میں خراج نہیں لیا جائے گا بلکہ اس کی پیداوار میں دسواں حصہ لیا جائے گا۔
ابھی تو ساری زمین امریکی ہو گئی ہے وہ جیسا چاہتا ہے کرتا ہے۔
Book of Siyar. [3054] (75) And all the land of Arabia is 'ushr land. [3054] (75) The land of Arabia is entirely 'ushr. The rulings of 'ushr and kharaj land: It is not permissible to keep a second religion in Arabia. Kharaj occurs when a disbeliever resides there, but it is not permissible to keep a disbeliever in Arabia. Therefore, it is not permissible to impose kharaj on it. Therefore, all those lands are 'ushr. There is a hadith: Expel all polytheists from the Arabian Peninsula. From Ibn Abbas: He said on Thursday--and what is Thursday?--"Expel the polytheists from the Arabian Peninsula." (Bukhari, Muslim) This hadith indicates that polytheists are to be expelled from Arabia, so it is 'ushr. (2) Another hadith: I heard Umar ibn Abd al-Aziz say: It has reached me that the last words the Messenger of Allah spoke were: "May Allah curse the Jews and Christians; they took the graves of their prophets as places of worship. Two religions shall not remain in the land of Arabia." (Bayhaqi) This mursal hadith also supports that the land of Arabia is 'ushr, meaning that kharaj will not be taken from it, but rather one-tenth of its produce will be taken. Now all the land has become American; they do as they please.
Source pages p. 302

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof. The matn states that all land of Arabia is 'ushr land (subject to the tithe tax). The commentator explains why: since no non-Muslim may take up permanent residence in Arabia, kharaj (which is levied on non-Muslim landowners) cannot be applied. Instead, all land there is 'ushr land, meaning Muslims pay 10% of produce as tax. Two hadiths are cited: (1) The order to expel polytheists from Arabia, and (2) the prohibition of two religions coexisting in Arabia. Both support the absence of permanent kāfir residents, hence no kharaj. The final remark 'now all the land has become American' reflects the author's contemporary context, noting that the ruling may not be enforceable today.

Key Terms
ارض عشر (ard 'ushr): Land on which the produce is subject to a tithe (10%) tax, as opposed to kharaj land.
خراج (kharaj): A land tax imposed on non-Muslim owners of agricultural land under Muslim rule.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why is all land of Arabia considered 'ushr land rather than kharaj land in the Hanafi school?
A) Because the land is owned by Muslims only.
B) Because no non-Muslim may permanently reside there, so kharaj cannot be imposed.
C) Because the Prophet himself declared it so.
D) Because the land is barren and produces little.

Key Takeaway
All land of Arabia is 'ushr land because the permanent presence of non-Muslims is prohibited, making kharaj impossible.

Legal Boundaries of the Arabian Peninsula
Definition of geographical limits for legal application

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the legal boundaries of the Arabian Peninsula as defined in the Hanafi school and explain the two legal consequences that follow from this definition.

Core Idea
The Arabian Peninsula's borders are legal facts, not just geography—they determine where non-Muslims may not live and where land is 'ushr.

The Arabian Peninsula is more than a geographical region; in Hanafi fiqh, its precise boundaries carry legal weight. This lesson unpacks the definition found in the matn, derived from early narrations, and clarifies how these lines on a map translate into concrete rulings on land classification and the rights of non-Muslims. Understanding this definition is essential for correctly applying the rules of 'ushr and the prohibition of permanent non-Muslim residence.

Guided Path
1
Identify the definition phrase
Locate the exact phrase in the matn that defines the Arabian Peninsula: 'وهي ما بين العذيب إلى أقصى حجر باليمن بمهرة إلى حد الشام'. This phrase sets the skeleton of the legal territory.
The phrase is a nominal clause with 'ما بين' indicating the range.
2
Break down the two dimensions
Split the definition into width and length. Width is from al-Udhaib (al-‘Udhayb) to Hajar in Yemen. Length is from Mahrah (a region in Yemen) to the border of Syria (the eastern limits of Sham).
Width runs approximately west-to-east; length runs south-to-north.
3
Corroborate with the cited athar
Compare the matn's definition with the narrations of Sa‘id ibn ‘Abd al-‘Aziz and al-Asma‘i. Both confirm similar boundaries, though al-Asma‘i adds specific points like Jeddah and the coast.
These are not conflicting but complementary; the gist is the same.
4
State the legal consequences
Within these boundaries, two rulings apply: (1) the land is 'ushr land (subject to 'ushr tax, not kharaj), and (2) non-Muslims (including dhimmis) may not take permanent residence. This derives from the Prophet’s command to expel polytheists from Arabia.
The prohibition does not apply to temporary visits.
5
Confirm the authority level
Recognize that this definition is from the zahir al-riwayah and is agreed upon (muttafaq ‘alayh) across the Hanafi school. No significant intra-madhhab ikhtilaf exists on the boundaries themselves.
The weight is high; it is the operative definition for fatwa.

حاشیہ : (الف) آپ نے فرمایا مشرکین کو جزیرہ عرب سے نکال دو (ب) آپ کا آخری کلام یہ تھا، اللہ یہود اور نصاری کو قتل کرے انہوں نے انبیاء کی قبر کو سجدہ گاہ بنالی۔ عرب کی زمین میں دو دین باقی نہ رہے (ج) سعید بن عبد العزیز نے فرمایا جزیرہ عرب وادی سے یمن کے اخیر تک ہے اور تخوم العراق سے سمندر تک ہے (د) حضرت اصمعی نے فرمایا جزیرۂ عرب عدن کے اخیر سے ریف العراق تک لمبائی میں ، بہر حال چوڑائی میں جدہ اور اس کے اردگرد ساحل سمندر سے اطراف شام تک۔
[3055] (76) And it (Arabia) is what lies between al-Udhaib and the extreme of Hajar in Yemen, from Mahrah to the boundary of Syria. And that place is from al-Udhaib to the extreme of Hajar in Yemen, and from Mahrah to the eastern border of Syria. Details of where the Arabian Peninsula extends. They say: from al-Udhaib to a place called Hajar in Yemen—that is the width. The length is from Mahrah to the border of Syria; this is from south to north. There is an athar clarifying this: Sa'id ibn Abd al-Aziz said, 'The Arabian Peninsula is from the valley to the far end of Yemen, to the borders of Iraq, to the sea.' Another narration: al-Asma'i said, 'The Arabian Peninsula in length is from the far end of Aden Abyan to the rural area of Iraq; as for width, from Jeddah and its adjacent coastal areas to the outskirts of Syria.' (Bayhaqi) The gist of both narrations is the same: the boundary of Arabia in length is from Syria to Yemen, and in width from Bahrain to Jeddah. In this boundary, it is not permissible to give permanent residence to disbelievers, nor to keep dhimmis, and this land is 'ushr.
Footnote: (a) He said: expel the polytheists from the Arabian Peninsula. (b) His last words were: May Allah curse the Jews and Christians; they made the graves of their prophets places of worship. Two religions shall not remain in the land of Arabia. (c) Sa'id ibn Abd al-Aziz said: the Arabian Peninsula is from the valley to the far end of Yemen, to the borders of Iraq, to the sea. (d) Al-Asma'i said: the Arabian Peninsula in length is from the far end of Aden Abyan to the rural area of Iraq; in width, from Jeddah and its adjacent coastal areas to the outskirts of Syria.
Source pages p. 302

Commentary
This passage is a definition ruling. It defines the legal boundaries of the Arabian Peninsula for the purpose of applying the previous ruling (that all land there is 'ushr and non-Muslims cannot reside). The matn gives the boundaries as between al-Udhaib and Hajar in Yemen (width) and from Mahrah to Syria (length). The commentary cites two athar from early scholars (Sa'id ibn Abd al-Aziz and al-Asma'i) that give similar descriptions. The practical consequence: within these limits, no permanent non-Muslim residence is allowed, and the land is 'ushr. The footnotes repeat the hadith evidence.

Key Terms
جزيرة العرب (Jazirat al-'Arab): The Arabian Peninsula, defined here as the land between al-Udhaib and Hajar in Yemen (width) and between Mahrah and Syria (length).

All Land of Sawad (Iraq) is Kharaj Land
Ruling with definition and historical boundaries

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the historical boundaries of Sawad and explain why the Hanafi school classifies it as kharaj land.

Core Idea
The fertile Sawad of Iraq is kharaj land because it was conquered by force and left in non-Muslim hands.

This passage establishes that all of the fertile region of Sawad (Iraq) is classified as kharaj land. It defines the boundaries of Sawad and links the name to its dark, fertile soil. Understanding this classification is key to distinguishing kharaj land from 'ushr land and recognizing the basis for land tax in Islamic law.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Ruling
The matn declares that all of Sawad is kharaj land. Recognize that this is a declaratory ruling (hukm wadi'i) about the legal status of the land.
2
Trace the Boundaries
The passage provides the boundaries of Sawad: from al-Udhaib (south) to 'Aqabat Hulwan (north), and from al-Tha'laba (or al-'Alth) to 'Abbadan (east-west). These are historical landmarks.
Al-Udhaib is near Iraq; 'Aqabat Hulwan is a mountain pass; al-Tha'laba and 'Abbadan are southern borders.
3
Understand the Classification
The land is called 'Sawad' meaning black, due to its fertile soil. It was conquered by force (anwatan) and left in the hands of its non-Muslim inhabitants, who pay kharaj tax on the produce. This distinguishes it from 'ushr land (e.g., Arabia) which is owned by Muslims.
4
Note the Commentator's Expansion
The commentary adds historical context: the land was heavily cultivated and under Muslim control, reinforcing the kharaj classification. The boundaries are confirmed with minor variation (al-'Alth instead of al-Tha'laba).
This expansion clarifies that the ruling is based on actual conquest and land use.

Source Text

عذیب : یہ عراق کے پاس ہے اور عراق کے حاجی وہاں سے گزرتے تھے۔ [۳۰۵۶) (۷۷) اور سواد عراق کی کل زمین خراجی ہے جو مقام عذیب سے مقام عقبہ حلوان تک اور ثعلبہ اور بعض لوگ کہتے ہیں مقام علث سے عبادان تک۔

[3056] (77) And all of Sawad is kharaj land, and it is what is between al-Udhaib and 'Aqabat Hulwan, and from al-Tha'laba (and some say from al-'Alth) to 'Abbadan. Al-Udhaib: it is near Iraq, and the pilgrims of Iraq used to pass through it. [3056] (77) And Sawad: all the land of Iraq is kharaji, from al-Udhaib to 'Aqabat Hulwan, and from Tha'laba (some say from 'Alth) to 'Abbadan. In those times, the land of Iraq was heavily cultivated, so it was called fertile i.e. black. The boundary of Iraq was from al-Udhaib to 'Aqabat Hulwan and from 'Alth to 'Abbadan. Muslims had control over it, and it was called kharaj land. 'Lakht Sawad': black; here meaning fertile land.

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement (with definition). The matn declares that all of Sawad (the fertile region of Iraq) is kharaj land. The commentator explains the boundaries: from al-Udhaib to 'Aqabat Hulwan (in the north), and from al-Tha'laba/ al-'Alth to 'Abbadan (in the south). The note clarifies that 'Sawad' literally means 'black', referring to the fertile soil. The land is classified as kharaj because it was conquered and left in the hands of non-Muslim owners, who pay kharaj tax on it. This contrasts with the 'ushr land of Arabia.

Key Terms
سواد (Sawad): The fertile agricultural region of Iraq, from al-Udhaib to 'Aqabat Hulwan and from al-Tha'laba to 'Abbadan.

Ownership and Sale of Sawad Land
Ruling with proof about ownership of Sawad land

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on ownership of Sawad land and identify the proof from the Companions' practice.

Core Idea
Sawad land is owned by its inhabitants; kharaj does not transfer ownership.

This passage presents a foundational ruling of Hanafi fiqh regarding land conquered in Iraq. The matn declares that the land of Sawad is owned by its original inhabitants, who may sell and dispose of it. The commentator supports this with athar from Ibn Sirin and the well-known consultation of Caliph Umar with Ali (RA). Understanding this ruling clarifies the distinction between conquered land categories and the nature of kharaj as a tax, not a symbol of state ownership.

Guided Path
1
Identify the central ruling
The matn states: 'The land of Sawad is owned by its inhabitants; they may sell it and dispose of it.' This is the core hukm.
2
Examine the two categories of conquest
Ibn Sirin's athar distinguishes between sulh (peace treaty) and 'anwah (force). For sulh land, the owners retain property; for 'anwah, the land belongs to the Muslims as booty.
This distinction determines whether original owners keep ownership.
3
Analyze the Companions' consultation
The report from Umar shows he initially considered dividing the people of Sawad among Muslims, but Ali advised to leave them as a resource. This decision was implemented, and kharaj was imposed.
The precedent established that even 'anwah land may be left with owners if the imam chooses.
4
Derive the legal principle
As long as the owner pays kharaj, ownership remains, and sale is permissible. Kharaj is a tax on the land, not a transfer of ownership.
5
Apply to similar contexts
This ruling applies to any land conquered by sulh or where the imam decides not to distribute 'anwah land. It underscores the Hanafi position that the imam has discretion in disposing of fay' land.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
[۳۰۵۷] (۷۸) وارض السواد مملوكة لاهلها يجوز بيعهم لها وتصرفهم فيها.
الشرق عراق کی زمین کے بارے میں مختلف روایتیں ہیں۔ بعض سے پتا چلتا ہے کہ اس کی زمین مجاہدین کے درمیان تقسیم کی تھی۔ اور بعض سے پتا چلتا ہے کہ تقسیم نہیں کی تھی ۔ اور جو حصہ تقسیم کی تھی اس کو بھی بعد میں واپس لے لیا اور مسلمانوں کے فائدے کے لئے چھوڑ دیا۔ اور تمام زمین پر خراج مقرر کیا۔ اور قاعدہ یہ ہے کہ کوئی کسی زمین کا مالک ہو اور اس کا خراج ادا کرتا ہو تو اس زمین کو بیچ سکتا ہے اور تصرف کر سکتا ہے۔ اس کی دلیل یہ اثر ہے۔ عن ابن سیرین قال السواد منه صلح ومنه عنوة، فما كان منه عنوة فهو للمسلمين وما كان منه صلح فلهم أموالهم (الف) ( سنن بیہقی ، باب السواد، ج تاسع، ص ۲۲۵، نمبر ۱۸۳۵۸) اس اثر سے معلوم ہوا کہ عراق کا بعض حصہ للبيهقي غلبہ سے فتح ہوا تھا اور بعض حصہ صلح ہے۔ جو غلبہ سے فتح ہوا تھا اس کو مسلمانوں کے لئے تقسیم کر دیا۔ اور جو صلح سے فتح ہوا تھا وہ مالک کا مال رہا۔ اور جب مالک کا مال رہا تو اس کو بیچ بھی سکتا ہے (۲) عن عمر انه اراد ان يقسم اهل السواد بين المسلمين وامر بهم ان يحصوا فوجدوا الرجل المسلم يصيبه ثلاثة من الفلاحين يعنى العلوج فشاور اصحاب النبي عل الله في ذلك فقال على دعهم يكونون مادة للمسلمين فبعث عثمان بن حنيف فوضع عليهم ثمانية واربعين ، واربعة وعشرين واثنى عشر ( ب ) (سن للبیہقی ، باب السواد، ج تاسع ص ۲۲۶، نمبر، ۱۸۳۷) اس اثر سے معلوم ہوا کہ حضرت علی کے مشورے سے عراق کی زمین تقسیم نہیں کی گئی۔ اس لئے وہاں کے لوگ اس کے مالک رہے۔
حاشیه : (الف) حضرت ابن سیرین نے فرمایا عراق کا کچھ حصہ مصلح سے فتح ہوا ہے اور کچھ حصہ زبردستی ، پس جو ز بر دستی فتح ہو وہ مسلمانوں کی غنیمت ہے اور جو صلح سے ہو وہ صلح کرنے والے کا مال ہے (ب) حضرت عمر نے چاہا کہ عراق والوں کو مسلمانوں کے درمیان تقسیم کرے تو لوگوں کو حکم دیا کہ ان کو گئے۔ تو دیکھا کہ ایک مسلمان مرد کے حصے میں تین کا شتکار یعنی کا فرآتے ہیں۔ پس اصحاب نبی نے مشورہ کیا تو حضرت علی نے فرمایا ان کو چھوڑ دیں۔ مسلمانوں کے مادہ ثابت ہوں گے۔ پھر عثمان بن حنیف و روانہ کیا تو ان میں سے کسی پر اڑتالیس اور کسی پر چو ہیں اور کسی پر بارہ درہم مقرر کیا۔
[3057] (78) And the land of Sawad is owned by its inhabitants; they may sell it and dispose of it. Al-Sharq? There are different narrations about the land of Iraq. Some indicate that it was divided among the mujahideen, others that it was not divided. And the portion that was divided was later taken back and left for the benefit of the Muslims, and kharaj was imposed on all the land. The rule is: if someone owns land and pays its kharaj, he may sell and dispose of it. The proof is this athar: Ibn Sirin said: "Sawad: part of it is by sulh (peace treaty) and part by 'anwah (force). What was by force belongs to the Muslims; what was by sulh, their wealth belongs to them." (Bayhaqi) This athar shows that part of Iraq was conquered by force and part by peace. What was conquered by force was divided among the Muslims, and what was conquered by peace remained the property of its owners. And since it remained their property, they can sell it. (2) From Umar: he wanted to distribute the people of Sawad among the Muslims and ordered them to be counted. They found that a Muslim man would receive three peasants (i.e., disbelievers). He consulted the Companions, and Ali said: "Leave them; they will be a resource for the Muslims." So he sent Uthman ibn Hunayf and imposed on them 48, 24, and 12 [dirhams]. (Bayhaqi) This athar shows that on the advice of Ali, the land of Iraq was not divided, so its people remained its owners.
Footnote: (a) Ibn Sirin said: part of Iraq was conquered by sulh and part by force; what was by force is the booty of the Muslims, and what was by sulh is the wealth of those who made peace. (b) Umar wanted to divide the people of Sawad among the Muslims, so he ordered them to be counted. They found that one Muslim man would get three peasants (disbelievers). He consulted the Companions, and Ali said: leave them; they will be a resource for the Muslims. Then he sent Uthman ibn Hunayf and imposed on some 48, some 24, and some 12 dirhams.
Source pages p. 303

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof. The matn states that the land of Sawad is owned by its inhabitants (the original non-Muslim owners), and they may sell it and dispose of it freely. The commentator clarifies that despite being kharaj land, ownership remained with the people. He notes different narrations about whether the land was originally divided among the Muslims; the final decision, based on the advice of Ali (RA), was not to divide it but to leave it with the owners and impose kharaj. Two athar are cited: (1) Ibn Sirin explains that parts conquered by force became booty for Muslims, but parts conquered peacefully remained with the owners. (2) The story of Umar consulting the Companions about dividing the land; Ali advised leaving it with the owners to benefit the Muslims continuously. The ruling: as long as the owner pays kharaj, he retains full ownership and can sell or dispose of the land.

Key Terms
صلح (sulh): Peaceful conquest where the inhabitants surrender under terms; their property remains theirs.
عنوة ('anwah): Conquest by force; the land becomes booty for the Muslim conquerors, potentially subject to division.

Key Terms from Source Passage

D) It is owned by the conquering army.

Key Takeaway
The land of Sawad is owned by its original inhabitants, who may sell it because the kharaj is a tax, not a sign of state ownership.
