Kharaj Rates on Sawad Land by Umar (RA)
Explaining the kharaj rates per jareeb as set by Caliph Umar on the Sawad region

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the kharaj rates per jarib as set by Umar (RA) and identify the hadith evidence supporting these rates.

Core Idea
Umar's kharaj rates: 1 sa' + 1 dirham per jarib for grain, 5 dirhams for vegetables, 10 dirhams for vines/palms.

In this lesson, we examine the kharaj (land tax) rates established by Caliph Umar (RA) in the Sawad region of Iraq. These rates are a key example of the Hanafi reliance on the practice of the Companions (amal al-sahabah) as a source of law. Understanding these rates is essential for grasping Hanafi land tax rules.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and its conditions
The passage first distinguishes land based on water source: land revived with water from non-Muslim rivers is kharaji, not 'ushri. Then it presents the kharaj rates per jarib for different land types.
2
Locate the dalil (the hadith evidence)
The author quotes an athar from Musannaf Ibn Abi Shayba: Umar sent Uthman ibn Hunayf to Sawad, who set the rates. This is the proof for the ruling.
The hanafi school considers this a binding precedent.
3
Understand the rates per land type
For each jarib of grain land (wheat/barley) that has water: 1 qafiz (sa') of grain + 1 dirham. For vegetable land: 5 dirhams. For dense vineyards/palm groves: 10 dirhams.
4
Note the Hanafi reliance on this precedent
This ruling is based on the practice of a Companion (Umar) and is considered part of the sunnah in Hanafi fiqh. It is classified as zahir al-riwayah and mufta bihi.
The rates are fixed and not subject to istihsan.
5
Distinguish from 'ushr land
Land that is irrigated by natural rain or Muslim-dug rivers is 'ushri (subject to tithe). Land irrigated by non-Muslim-dug rivers is kharaji even if owned by a Muslim.
The water source is the key factor.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

هاشمى وهو الصاع ودرهم ومن جريب الرطبة خمسة دراهم ومن جريب الكرم المتصل والنخل المتصل عشرة دراهم. اس سے اشارہ ہوتا ہے خراجی زمین بننے میں پانی کا اعتبار ہے قرب وجوار کا اعتبار نہیں۔ لفت انظر : حضر سے مشتق ہے کھودنا۔ [۳۰۶۲ (۸۳) خراج جو حضرت عمرؓ نے اہل عراق پر مقرر کیا وہ ایک جریب جس میں پانی پہنچا ہو اور کھیتی کے قابل ہو ایک قفیز ہاشمی یعنی ایک صاع اور ایک درہم اور ترکاریوں کے ایک جریب میں پانچ درہم اور انگور اور کھجور جو گھنے ہوں دس درہم ۔ تشریح حضرت عمر نے صحابہ کے مشورے سے اہل عراق پر جو خراج مقرر کیا اس کی تفصیل یہ ہے کہ کھیتی کی زمین جس میں پانی جاتا ہو اور زراعت کے قابل ہو ایک جریب میں ایک صاع غلہ اور ایک درہم یعنی 3.061 گرام چاندی یا اس کی قیمت لازم ہوگی۔ اور ترکاریوں کی زمین میں پانچ درہم یعنی 15.305 گرام چاندی یا اس کی قیمت اور انگور یا کھجور جو گھنے ہوں اس کی ایک جریب زمین میں دس درہم یعنی 61 .30 گرام چاندی یا اس کی قیمت خراج ہے۔ جان عمر بن الخطاب بعث عثمان بن حنيف على السواد فوضع على كل جريب عامر او غامر يناله الماء درهما وقفيزا يعني الحنطة والشعير وعلى جريب الكرم عشرة وعلى جريب الرطاب خمسة (الف)(مصنف ابن ابي شيبة، ۲۷ ما قالوا فی النمس والخراج کیف یوضع ، ج سادس، ص ۴۳۹، نمبر ۳۲۷۰۶ سفن للبیہقی ، باب قدر الخراج الذي وضع على السواد، ج تاسع ص ۲۳۰، نمبر ۱۸۳۸۳) اثر سے معلوم ہوا کہ عام کھیتی میں ایک صاع اور ایک درہم، ترکاری کی کھیتی میں پانچ درہم اور انگور اور کھجور کے باغ میں دس درہم خراج ہے۔ گویا کہ ایک جریب عام کی کھیتی میں ایک صاع غلہ اور ایک درہم یعنی 3.061 گرام چاندی یا اس کی قیمت اور ترکاری کی کھیتی میں پانچ درہم یعنی 15.305 گرام چاندی یا اس کی قیمت اور انگور اور کھجور کی باغ میں دس درہم یعنی 30.61 گرام چاندی یا اس کی قیمت خراج لازم ہوگا۔ چاندی کا حساب اپنے اپنے سکوں سے کرلیں۔ مصنف ابن ابی شیبہ کے دوسرے اثر سے معلوم ہوتا ہے کہ پانچ درہم کے ساتھ پانچ صاع غلہ اور دس درہم کے ساتھ دس صاع غلہ بھی خراج میں لازم ہے۔ (مصنف ابن ابی شیبة ، ۲۷ ما قالوافی المس والخراج کیف یوضع ، ج سادس ص ۲۳۸، نمبر۰۲ ۳۲۷) حاشیہ : (الف) حضرت عمرؓ نے حضرت عثمان بن حنیف کو عراق پر بھیجاہر آباد اور غیر آباد جس کو پانی پہنچتا ہو ایک جریب پر ایک درہم اور ایک فیز مقرر کیا یعنی گیہوں اور جو کی پیداوار پر ۔ اور انگور کے ایک جریب زمین پر دس درہم اور سبزی کے ایک جریب زمین پر پانچ درہم مقرر فرمایا۔
One of them is that it is 'ushriyyah, and if it is revived with water from rivers dug by the non-Arabs like the River Malik and River Yazdagird, then it is kharajiyyah. (83) And the kharaj that Umar (RA) imposed on the people of Sawad: for every jarib that is reached by water and suitable for cultivation: one qafiz Hashimi (which is one sa') and one dirham; for a jarib of raṭbah: five dirhams; for a jarib of continuous vineyard and continuous palm grove: ten dirhams.
Source pages p. 307

Commentary
This passage is a ruling on the kharaj (land tax) rates as established by Caliph Umar (RA) in the Sawad region of Iraq. The author first clarifies a distinction: if land is revived using water from rivers dug by non-Muslims (e.g., the rivers Malik and Yazdagird), it becomes kharajiyyah (taxable land), not 'ushriyyah (tithe land). Then the core ruling: for each jarib (a unit of land area) that has water and is cultivable, the tax is one qafiz Hashimi (one sa'—a dry measure) of grain and one dirham of silver. For vegetable gardens (raṭbah), the tax is five dirhams per jarib. For dense vineyards and palm groves, the tax is ten dirhams per jarib. The commentary in Urdu explains that this was done by Umar with consultation of the Companions, and provides modern equivalences for the dirham weight (3.061 g silver) and the meaning of qafiz. The author then brings an athar from Musannaf Ibn Abi Shayba: Umar sent Uthman ibn Hunayf to Sawad, who set for every jarib (cultivated or uncultivated but reachable by water) one dirham and one qafiz (meaning wheat or barley), for a jarib of vines ten dirhams, and for a jarib of vegetables five dirhams. A second narration adds that with five dirhams, five sa' of grain were also required, and with ten dirhams, ten sa' of grain. This shows the comprehensive system of kharaj based on land type and productivity. The Hanafi school relies on this precedent as a source of law (amal al-sahabah), and these rates are considered the standard for kharaj on similar lands.

Key Terms
خراج (kharāj): A land tax imposed on non-Muslim landowners in conquered territories, fixed per unit area and crop type.
جريب (jarīb): A unit of land area, approximately 60 cubits by 60 cubits (using the cubit of Kisra), about 1024 square meters.
قفيز هاشمى (qafīz hāshimī): A dry measure equal to one sa' (approximately 3 liters), used for grain.
درهم (dirham): A silver coin weighing about 3.061 grams, used as currency for tax payment.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the kharaj rates set by Umar (RA), how much tax is due per jarib of vegetable land (raṭbah)?
A) One dirham and one qafiz
B) Five dirhams
C) Ten dirhams
D) Five dirhams and five sa'

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school relies on Umar's kharaj rates as a binding precedent, establishing fixed tax amounts per land type.

Land Measurement Units in Hanafi Fiqh: Jareeb and Acre Conversions
Land measurement conversion tables for fiqh calculations.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the dimensions of one jareeb and one acre in handspans, yards, and meters, and apply the correct unit in a Hanafi land tax (kharaj) calculation.

Core Idea
The Hanafi jareeb equals 1225 square yards; the British acre equals 4840 square yards.

Islamic land measurement units like the jareeb are essential for calculating kharaj and agricultural zakat in Hanafi fiqh. Modern jurisdictions often use the acre. This lesson provides exact conversion values so you can apply Hanafi rulings with precision.

Guided Path
1
Identify the traditional handspan and its subdivisions
Learn that one common handspan (hath) equals 18 inches, 1.5 feet, or 45.72 cm; one fractional handspan equals 21 inches or 53.34 cm; one qabda equals 3 inches.
These base units underlie the jareeb definition.
2
Define the jareeb in its four equivalent ways
Memorize: 1 jareeb = 60×60 fractional handspans (3600 sq fractional handspans) = 105×105 common handspans (11025 sq handspans) = 35×35 yards (1225 sq yards) = 32.004×32.004 meters (1024.25 sq meters).
The 35×35 yard version is most useful for modern calculations.
3
Define the acre in its two equivalent ways
Memorize: 1 acre = 69.57×69.57 yards (4840 sq yards) = 63.614×63.614 meters (4046.856 sq meters). Also 1 decimal = 1/100 acre = 40.4685 sq meters.
The acre is nearly four times the jareeb.
4
Note the local seker unit as a regional variant
In Jharkhand, a seker (chain) is 22 yards long; 10 sekers long × 1 seker wide = 1 acre. This shows local adaptation.
Not a classical Hanafi unit but useful for practical fatwa in that region.
5
Apply the conversion to a simple kharaj calculation
If kharaj is 10% of produce on a 2 jareeb field, first compute area (2 × 1225 = 2450 sq yd) then apply the tax rate to the estimated produce per sq yd.
Wrong unit (e.g., acre) would cause a 4× error.

میر الدین غفر له
Al-Sharh al-Thamiri Part Four
Jareeb and Acre Calculation at a Glance
What is it? How much is it?
One inch = 2.54 centimeters. One meter = 39.37 inches.
One common handspan: 18 inches, 1.50 feet, 12 inches? Actually one common handspan = 18 inches, one foot = 12 inches, one yard = 36 inches, one qabda = 3 inches, one common handspan = 7.62 cm, one foot = 45.72 cm.
Fractional handspan: What is it? How much is it?
One fractional handspan = 7 qabdas = 21 inches = 1.75 feet = 53.34 cm. One meter = 100 cm.
How many square jareeb?
Jareeb: Length × Width = Area in square feet or yards.
One jareeb = 60 handspans × 60 handspans = 3600 square fractional handspans
105 handspans × 105 handspans = 11025 square handspans = one jareeb
One jareeb = 35 yards × 35 yards = 1225 square yards
One jareeb = 32.004 meters × 32.004 meters = 1024.25 square meters
Kitab al-Siyar

How much is an acre?
Acre: Length × Width = Area in square feet or yards.
One acre = 69.57 yards × 69.57 yards = 4840 square yards
One acre = 63.614 meters × 63.614 meters = 4046.856 square meters
One decimal = 6.3614 meters × 6.3614 meters = 40.4685 square meters
Thus 100 decimals make one acre.
Regarding Jharkhand's Siker
In my province Jharkhand, they measure land with a long iron chain called 'Seker'. Some also call it 'Jareeb'. In English it is called 'Chain'. Ten sekers long and one seker wide make one acre. And the length of a seker is 20.1168 meters. Thus multiplying 20.1168 width by 201.168 length gives a total of 4046.856 square meters which is the area of one acre. And in terms of yards, one seker is 22 yards long. Multiplying that by ten sekers i.e. 220 yards gives 4840 square yards which is the area of one acre.
Seker Calculation: Seker: Length × Width = Area in square feet or yards.
One seker 20.1168 meters × 201.168 meters = 4046.85 square meters = one acre
One seker 22 yards × 220 yards = 4840 square yards = one acre
For the information of students, I have mentioned formulas and calculations in detail everywhere. Calculate with a calculator.
Mir al-Din Ghufir Lahu
Source pages p. 309

Commentary
This passage serves as a practical appendix providing conversion tables for land measurement units, specifically the Islamic jareeb and the modern acre, as well as the local chain (seker) used in Jharkhand. The author presents these conversions for students to use in fiqh calculations, such as determining zakat on agricultural produce or assessing land for kharaj. The tables define the standard sizes: one common handspan (hath) is 18 inches, one foot is 12 inches, one yard is 36 inches, and one qabda is 3 inches. A fractional handspan (kasri hath) is defined as 7 qabdas or 21 inches. The jareeb is a traditional unit of area: it is 60 handspans by 60 handspans (3600 square fractional handspans), or equivalently 105 by 105 normal handspans (11025 square handspans), or 35 by 35 yards (1225 square yards), or 32.004 meters square (1024.25 square meters). The acre is a British unit: 69.57 yards square (4840 square yards) or 63.614 meters square (4046.856 square meters). One decimal is 1/100 of an acre (40.4685 square meters). The author also explains the local 'seker' or chain: 10 sekers long and 1 seker wide makes an acre, with one seker equal to 22 yards or 20.1168 meters. These conversions are essential for applying Hanafi rulings on land taxes and transactions accurately.

Key Terms
جریب (jareeb): A traditional unit of land area equal to 60×60 handspans (3600 square handspans), 105×105 handspans (11025 square handspans), 35×35 yards (1225 square yards), or 32.004×32.004 meters (1024.25 square meters).
ایکڑ (acre): A modern unit of land area equal to 69.57×69.57 yards (4840 square yards) or 63.614×63.614 meters (4046.856 square meters).
ہاتھ (hath): A unit of length; one common handspan equals 18 inches, 1.5 feet, or 45.72 cm.
سیکر (seker): A local land measurement chain used in Jharkhand, India; one seker equals 22 yards or 20.1168 meters.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi jareeb (1225 sq yd) is distinct from the British acre (4840 sq yd); accurate conversions are essential for proper kharaj and zakat calculations.

Exemption from Kharaj When Crop Destroyed by Blight
Ruling on exemption from land tax due to crop loss

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on kharaj when crops are destroyed by blight and explain the proof from the practice of 'Umar ibn al-Khattab.

Core Idea
Kharaj is exempted when crops are destroyed because tax is tied to capacity, not land.

This lesson examines a specific ruling from the matn on kharaj (land tax). The text states that if a natural calamity destroys the crop completely, no kharaj is due. This ruling is based on the general principle that kharaj is adjusted according to ability. We will explore the ruling, its proof, and the conditions under which exemption applies.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is paying kharaj. The ruling is that the obligation becomes wajib only if the land produces yield. If the crop is destroyed by blight, the obligation lapses.
The key phrase is 'فلا خراج عليهم' (no kharaj upon them).
2
Locate the proof (dalil)
The author cites an athar from Hasan al-Basri reporting the practice of 'Umar ibn al-Khattab: 'if they are unable, it is lightened and they are not burdened beyond capacity.'
This is a Companion practice, authoritative in Hanafi fiqh.
3
Analyze the wajh al-dalalah
The phrase 'لا يكلفون فوق طاقتهم' directly implies that kharaj is contingent on the land's productive capacity. Complete destruction means zero capacity, hence no kharaj.
The dalala is qat'i (clear) in meaning.
4
Note the cross-madhhab ikhtilaf
Imam al-Shafi'i may hold kharaj as a fixed tax on land itself, but the Hanafi view bases it on capacity as established by the practice of 'Umar.
This difference is classified as mukhtalaf fih.
5
Determine the practical consequence
If a farmer's crop is completely destroyed by an act of God, no kharaj is collected for that year. If partially destroyed, the amount is reduced proportionally.
The ruling protects farmers from unjust burden.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
عنها أو اصطلم الزرع آفة فلا خراج عليهم. قال الحسن واما اراضيهم فعليها الخراج الذي وضعه عمر بن الخطاب فان احتملوا اكثر من ذلك فلا يزاد عليهم وان عجزوا عن ذلك خفف عنهم ولا يكلفون فوق طاقتهم كما قال عمر
Or if the crop is destroyed by a blight, then there is no kharaj upon them. Al-Hasan said: As for their lands, upon them is the kharaj which 'Umar ibn al-Khattab placed; if they can bear more than that, it is not increased upon them, and if they are unable for that, it is lightened for them, and they are not burdened beyond their capacity, as 'Umar said.
Source pages p. 312

Commentary
This is a ruling from the matn on kharaj (land tax). The rule is that if the cultivated land suffers a natural calamity such that the crop is completely destroyed (اصطلم), then the obligation of kharaj drops for that year. This is because kharaj is tied to the land's productive capacity; it is not a fixed poll tax but a tax on yield. The proof for this is the general principle from the practice of 'Umar (رضي الله عنه) that kharaj is adjusted according to ability, as narrated in the athar from Hasan al-Basri. The lesson type is a ruling statement with proof implied by the practice of the Companions.

Key Terms
اصطلم (iṣṭalama): To be uprooted or destroyed completely, applied to crops destroyed by blight or calamity.
خراج (kharāj): Land tax imposed on agricultural land in Islamic governance, typically paid on produce.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi ruling in this passage, what happens to the kharaj obligation if the crop is completely destroyed by a blight?
A) Kharaj is still due in full.
B) Kharaj is reduced by half.
C) Kharaj is completely exempted.
D) Kharaj is postponed to the next year.

Key Takeaway
Kharaj is not a fixed land tax; it is contingent on the land's productive capacity, and is exempted when the crop is destroyed by an uncontrollable calamity.

Kharaj Obligation on Idle Land
Ruling on kharaj due even if owner neglects cultivation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on kharaj when the owner neglects cultivation and identify the basis for this ruling.

Core Idea
Kharaj is due on the land itself, not on produce — deliberate idleness does not exempt it.

This lesson examines a specific yet important case: what happens to kharaj liability when the landowner, despite being able to cultivate, chooses not to? The Hanafi school, relying on the principle that kharaj is tied to the land's potential, holds that the obligation remains. This ruling has practical implications for agricultural taxation and land rights.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and ruling
The act is leaving land idle (ʿaṭṭalahā). The ruling is that kharaj is wajib upon the owner.
The Arabic phrase 'faʿalayhi al-kharāj' is clear and unconditional.
2
Understand the basis in Hanafi usul
The proof is that kharaj is a right attached to the land itself (ḥaqq fī al-arḍ), not to produce. This is established by the practice of the Companions (Sunnah taqrīriyyah), such as ʿUmar's administration.
No explicit Quranic verse or hadith is quoted; the proof is derived from general principles and tradition.
3
Recognize the scope of the ruling
The ruling applies when the owner has the ability to cultivate but deliberately neglects. Forced idleness (e.g., natural disaster) may be treated differently.
The term ʿaṭṭalahā implies a deliberate act.
4
Note the cross-madhhab dispute
Some other schools tie kharaj to actual yield. For them, if no crop is grown, no kharaj is due. The Hanafi school disagrees.
This dispute has practical financial consequences.
5
Identify the muftā bihī
The Hanafi position (kharaj due on idle land) is the relied-upon ruling in the school, as stated in the matn.
This ruling is from Zāhir al-Riwāyah and is considered strong.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وان عطلها صاحبها فعليه الخراج
And if the owner leaves it idle, then upon him is the kharaj.
Source pages p. 312

Commentary
This ruling states that if the owner has the ability to cultivate but deliberately leaves the land uncultivated (عطلها), he is still liable for kharaj. This is because the kharaj is attached to the land itself, not just to the actual produce. It is a form of compensation for the land's potential. The proof is derived from the general principle that kharaj is a right on the land, and the practice of the Companions indicates that kharaj is due regardless of the owner's choice to cultivate or not, as long as the land is capable. This prevents owners from avoiding tax by simply not farming.

Key Terms
عطلها (ʿaṭṭalahā): To leave land idle, uncultivated, or neglected.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a landowner deliberately leaves his kharaj land uncultivated, what is the ruling according to this passage?
A) Kharaj is completely exempted.
B) Kharaj is reduced because no produce exists.
C) Kharaj is still due in full.
D) Kharaj is transferred to a different year.

Key Takeaway
Deliberate idleness does not cancel kharaj because the tax is on the land, not the crop.

Kharaj Remains Despite Conversion to Islam
Ruling with Companion precedent

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on kharaj when a dhimmi converts to Islam, explain the distinction between kharaj and jizya, and apply the ruling to a novel scenario.

Core Idea
Kharaj is a land tax, not a personal tax — conversion lifts jizya but not kharaj.

This lesson addresses a critical distinction in Islamic fiscal law: the difference between personal and land taxes. Many assume that embracing Islam removes all fiscal obligations imposed under non-Muslim status. However, the Hanafi school, relying on the practice of the Rightly Guided Caliphs, holds that land tax (kharaj) remains after conversion, while poll tax (jizya) is lifted. This ruling has important implications for converts who own agricultural land.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Ruling
What is the exact ruling stated in the matn? Specify the act (conversion) and the obligation (kharaj continues unchanged).
The matn states: 'whoever among the people of kharaj becomes Muslim, the kharaj is taken from him as before.'
2
Locate the Dalil
What proof is cited? It is an athar (saying) of 'Umar and 'Ali, recorded in Musannaf Ibn Abi Shaybah. Quote the Arabic text.
The athar: 'إذا أسلم و له أرض وضعنا عنه الجزية و أخذنا خراجها'
3
Analyze the Wajh al-Dalalah
How does this athar prove the ruling? The caliphs explicitly distinguished between jizya (dropped) and kharaj (taken), showing kharaj is independent of the owner's religious status.
4
Note the Ikhtilaf
Are there schools that disagree? Some scholars argue that conversion removes all former obligations. How does the Hanafi school respond?
Hanafis hold that kharaj is attached to the land, not the person, so conversion does not affect it.
5
Apply to a Scenario
Consider a dhimmi who owns a date orchard subject to kharaj. He converts to Islam. What are his obligations now? State the ruling and justify using the dalil.
He must continue to pay kharaj on the orchard; jizya is cancelled.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
و من أسلم من أهل الخراج يؤخذ منه الخراج على حاله. عن عمر و علي قالا إذا أسلم و له أرض وضعنا عنه الجزية و أخذنا خراجها
And whoever among the people of kharaj becomes Muslim, the kharaj is taken from him as before. From 'Umar and 'Ali: 'If he becomes Muslim and has land, we set aside the jizya from him and take its kharaj.'
Source pages p. 312

Commentary
This ruling distinguishes between jizya (poll tax) and kharaj (land tax). Jizya is a personal imposition on non-Muslims as a sign of humility, so it falls away upon conversion to Islam. However, kharaj is attached to the land itself, not the person's religion. Therefore, even if the landowner converts, the kharaj obligation on the land remains. This is proven by the practice of the two Caliphs, 'Umar and 'Ali (رضي الله عنهما), who explicitly stated that upon conversion, jizya is lifted but kharaj is taken. This is the established Hanafi position.

Key Terms
خراج (kharāj): Land tax imposed on conquered lands that remain in the hands of non-Muslims or even Muslims who purchase such land.
جزية (jizya): Poll tax imposed on free, adult non-Muslim men under Islamic rule as a mark of subjection.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Both jizya and kharaj are dropped.
B) Both jizya and kharaj remain.
C) Jizya is dropped, but kharaj remains.
D) Kharaj is dropped, but jizya remains.

Key Takeaway
Kharaj is tied to land, not religion; thus conversion does not lift it.

Permissibility of a Muslim Purchasing Kharaj Land
Ruling with Companion proofs on kharaj land purchase

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on a Muslim buying kharaj land and explain the legal proof from the actions of the Companions.

Core Idea
Kharaj is a land tax, not personal humiliation; thus a Muslim may buy and pay it.

This ruling addresses a practical question: can a Muslim buy land that is subject to the kharaj tax from a dhimmi? The Hanafi school permits it, citing the practice of Hasan and Husayn (Radiallahu Anhuma), while Abdullah ibn Umar considered it unbecoming. We will examine the legal proof and reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and the act
The passage rules on the act of a Muslim purchasing kharaj land from a dhimmi. The hukm is permissibility (jawaz). Also note that the Muslim buyer must pay the kharaj tax on that land.
2
Locate the proof
The author cites two athar: the actions of al-Hasan and al-Husayn buying kharaj land, and Ibn 'Umar's disapproval. The Hanafis take the first as evidence of permissibility, treating Ibn 'Umar's view as personal preference (wara') not prohibition.
The proof is from the practice of the Sahaba, which is a source of law for Hanafis.
3
Understand the dissenting view
Ibn 'Umar held that a Muslim should not write humiliation (dhull) on himself by paying kharaj, which was originally a tax on conquered non-Muslims. The Hanafis respond that kharaj is a land tax attached to the property, not a personal tax on the Muslim.
This distinction is crucial: the nature of the tax determines the ruling.
4
Apply the Hanafi principle
The ruling is based on the principle that kharaj is a right of the treasury (bayt al-mal) on the land. It does not imply subjugation of the individual. Therefore, the purchase is valid and the tax is due.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ويجوز أن يشترى المسلم من الذمي أرض الخراج ويؤخذ منه الخراج. عن ابن أبي ليلى قال اشترى الحسن بن علي ملحة أو ملحا واشترى الحسين بن علي بريدين من أرض الخراج وقال قد رد اليهم عمر أرضهم وصالحهم على الخراج. عن نافع أن عبد الله بن عمر كان إذا سئل عن الرجل من أهل الإسلام يأخذ الأرض من أهل الذمة بما عليها من الخراج يقول لا يحل لمسلم أو لا ينبغي لمسلم أن يكتب على نفسه الذل والصغار
And it is permissible for a Muslim to buy kharaj land from a dhimmi and kharaj is taken from him. Ibn Abi Layla said: Al-Hasan ibn 'Ali bought a salt mine, and al-Husayn ibn 'Ali bought two barids of kharaj land, and he said: 'Umar returned their land to them and made peace with them on kharaj.' From Nafi': 'Abdullah ibn 'Umar, when asked about a man from the people of Islam taking land from the people of dhimmah with its kharaj, said: 'It is not permissible for a Muslim – or it is not befitting for a Muslim – to write humiliation and disgrace upon himself.'
Source pages p. 313

Commentary
This ruling discusses the permissibility of a Muslim purchasing kharaj land from a dhimmi. The Hanafi position permits it, based on the practice of the Companions al-Hasan and al-Husayn (رضي الله عنهما), who bought kharaj land and paid kharaj on it. However, there is a dissenting opinion from 'Abdullah ibn 'Umar (رضي الله عنهما), who considered it makruh because it involves subjecting oneself to a form of humiliation (as kharaj is originally a tax on conquered non-Muslims). The Hanafi school, however, distinguishes: kharaj is a land tax, not personal humiliation for a Muslim; it is simply a financial obligation attached to the land. The purchase is valid and the Muslim buyer must pay kharaj. The ruling is that it is permissible (ja'iz), though some early scholars disliked it for personal piety reasons.

Key Terms
خراج (kharāj): Land tax imposed on agricultural land, originally from conquered territories; a financial obligation on the land itself.
ملحة (milḥa): A salt mine or salt marsh. In the context, al-Hasan bought a salt mine.
بريدين (barīdayn): Dual of barid, a unit of distance (approximately 4 farsakh) used here to indicate a plot of land of that size.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi ruling in this passage, is it permissible for a Muslim to buy kharaj land from a dhimmi?
A) Yes, it is permissible and kharaj is taken from the Muslim buyer.
B) No, it is prohibited because it involves paying a humiliating tax.
C) It is permissible but no kharaj is paid after purchase.
D) It is only permissible if the dhimmi agrees to sell without kharaj.

Key Takeaway
A Muslim may buy kharaj land and must pay the kharaj tax, as it is a land tax, not a personal humiliation.

No 'Ushr on Kharaj Land
Ruling with proof from al-Sha'bi

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the taxation of kharaj land and explain the proof from al-Sha'bi.

Core Idea
Kharaj and 'ushr do not coexist on the same land; only one tax is due.

This lesson examines a clear Hanafi ruling that the produce of kharaj land is not subject to 'ushr (the Islamic tithe). The proof is a statement of the tabi'i al-Sha'bi that these two forms of taxation cannot be combined. Understanding this ruling is essential for distinguishing between different categories of land and their respective fiscal obligations.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is the cultivation of kharaj land. The ruling is that only kharaj is due, not 'ushr.
2
Locate the dalil
The proof is the saying of al-Sha'bi: 'Kharaj and 'ushr do not coexist in one land.'
This is a qawl tabi'i, which is a valid source of evidence in Hanafi fiqh.
3
Apply the ruling
If a Muslim owns and cultivates kharaj land, he must pay kharaj but not 'ushr on the produce.
The land classification does not change with the owner's religion.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولا عشر في الخارج من أرض الخراج. عن الشعبي قال لا يجتمع خراج وعشر في أرض
And there is no 'ushr on the produce of kharaj land. Al-Sha'bi said: 'Kharaj and 'ushr do not coexist in one land.'
Source pages p. 313

Commentary
This ruling establishes that 'ushr (the Islamic tithe on agricultural produce, which is a zakat obligation for Muslims on 'ushr land) is not applicable to produce grown on kharaj land. Kharaj land is land conquered by force that remained in the hands of its original owners (or later bought by Muslims) and is subject to kharaj. Since the land is already burdened with kharaj, imposing 'ushr would lead to double taxation, which is not allowed. The proof is the statement of the tabi'i al-Sha'bi that kharaj and 'ushr cannot be collected on the same land. This is the agreed-upon Hanafi position. If a Muslim owns kharaj land, he pays kharaj, not 'ushr.

Key Terms
عشر (ʿushr): Tenth; the zakat on agricultural produce from land that is classified as 'ushr land (usually land conquered peacefully or originally owned by Muslims).
خراج (kharaj): Land tax levied on conquered lands that remain in the hands of non-Muslims (or later Muslim owners) as determined by the imam.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Both kharaj and 'ushr.
B) Only 'ushr.
C) Only kharaj.
D) Neither.

Key Takeaway
On kharaj land, only kharaj is due; 'ushr is never levied on its produce.

Types of Jizya: By Peace Treaty or by Force
Ruling on types of jizya and their amounts

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between jizya by peace treaty and jizya by force, and state the ruling for each type.

Core Idea
Jizya amount is fixed by agreement in peace treaties but set by the Imam in conquered lands.

Jizya is the poll tax levied on non-Muslim subjects in an Islamic state. The Hanafi school divides jizya into two categories based on how the territory came under Muslim rule. This classification directly affects how the amount of jizya is determined. In this lesson, we will examine the two types and the proof from the Sunnah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two types of jizya
The passage states that jizya is of two types: one from peace (ṣulḥ) and one from conquest (ʿanwatan). Recognize that the first is based on mutual agreement, the second on the Imam's discretion.
The term 'ṣulḥ' refers to a treaty, while 'ʿanwatan' means by force.
2
Understand the ruling for each type
For treaty jizya, the amount is whatever the parties agree upon. For conquest jizya, a fixed rate is set by the Imam on every adult male (ḥālum).
The matn says 'فعلى كل حالم كذا' meaning 'upon every adult such-and-such'.
3
Locate the proof (dalīl)
The author cites the hadith of Ibn Abbas about the Prophet's treaty with the Christians of Najran, where the jizya was set at two thousand garments annually.
This hadith shows that the amount can be agreed upon; it is not rigidly fixed by Shari'a.
4
Analyze the wajh al-dalālah (legal implication)
The prophetic practice (sunnah) demonstrates that in treaty cases, the amount is negotiable. The absence of a fixed rate in the treaty indicates that the default is flexibility.
The hadith is ṣaḥīḥ and its meaning is clear.
5
Note the practical difference (thamarah al-khilāf)
Understanding this classification prevents misapplication: in a treaty, the Muslim ruler cannot unilaterally impose a rate; in conquest, the ruler cannot ask for an arbitrary amount but follows the established practice of the early community.
This affects the validity of the jizya contract.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والجزية على ضربين: جزية عن صلح فحسب ما يصطلحون عليه، وجزية عن عنوة فعلى كل حالم كذا. عن ابن عباس قال صالح رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم أهل نجران على ألفي حلة
And jizya is of two types: jizya from peace (treaty), then it is according to what they agree upon; and jizya from conquest, then upon every adult is such-and-such. From Ibn 'Abbas: The Messenger of Allah (ﷺ) made peace with the people of Najran upon two thousand garments.
Source pages p. 313

Commentary
This ruling, though partially missing in the OCR, introduces the classification of jizya (poll tax). The Hanafi school divides jizya into two categories: (1) Jizya agreed upon by peace treaty (صلح), where the amount is whatever both parties consent to, as exemplified by the Prophet's (ﷺ) treaty with Christians of Najran for two thousand garments annually. (2) Jizya imposed by force on conquered people (عنوة), where the Imam sets a fixed rate on adult males according to their financial status. This distinction affects the binding nature and amount. The lesson is a definitional ruling with proof from the Prophet's sunnah.

Key Terms
صلح (ṣulḥ): Peace treaty or settlement between Muslims and non-Muslims regarding the terms of jizya.
عنوة (ʿanwatan): By force; referring to lands conquered by military force, where the terms are set by the Imam.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) It is a fixed amount from the Shari'a.
B) It is whatever the Muslims and non-Muslims agree upon.
C) It is based on the income of the non-Muslims.
D) It is the same as the jizya of conquered lands.

Key Takeaway
Jizya is of two types: by peace treaty (amount agreed) and by force (amount set by Imam).

Jizya by Mutual Agreement: Amount Set by Consent
Ruling on jizya by mutual agreement with proof from hadith

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state that jizya can be imposed by mutual agreement and apply the ruling that the agreed amount is valid and binding.

Core Idea
Jizya is not a fixed tax; it can be negotiated and set by mutual consent between the Imam and the dhimmis.

This lesson covers the first type of jizya: jizya that is established by mutual consent and peace (sulh). The amount is not predetermined by sharia but depends on what both parties agree upon. The Prophet’s treaty with the Christians of Najran serves as the primary proof that this form of jizya is permissible and binding.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two types of jizya
The passage begins by stating that jizya is of two types. Identify the first type: jizya placed by mutual consent and peace (taradi wa sulh).
The second type (fixed by the Imam) will be covered separately.
2
State the ruling for this type
The ruling is that the amount of jizya is whatever the Imam (or his representative) and the dhimmi agree upon. It is valid (ja'iz) and binding.
No fixed maximum or minimum is stipulated by the text.
3
Examine the proof (dalil)
The passage cites the hadith of the Prophet’s peace treaty with the people of Najran. Identify the key elements: the subject (jizya), the amount (2000 suits of clothing), and the payment schedule (half in Safar, half in Rajab).
This shows that the amount was negotiated, not divinely prescribed.
4
Apply the ruling to a new scenario
Imagine an Imam agrees with a dhimmi community on a lump sum of 10,000 dirhams annually. Apply the ruling: this amount is valid as jizya and binding on both parties.
The agreement is like any other contract; both sides must consent.
5
Contrast with the common misconception
Note that many incorrectly believe jizya is always a fixed rate (e.g., 48 dirhams for the rich). This lesson shows that it can be variable when both parties agree.
The fixed rate applies to the second type (jizya imposed by the Imam without agreement).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والجزية على ضربين جزية توضع بالتراضي والصلح فتقدر بحسب ما يقع عليه الاتفاق
[۳۰۶۹] (۹۰) جزیہ کی دو قسمیں ہیں۔ ایک جزیہ وہ کہ رضامندی اور صلح سے مقرر کرے، پس مقرر کیا جائے گا جس پر اتفاق ہو جائے۔ ار امیر المومنین اور ذمی کے درمیان جزیہ کے جس مقدار پر صلح ہو جائے اتنا جز یہ جائز ہو جائے گا۔ قبیلہ نجران سے حضور نے دو ہزار حلے کے جزیے پر صلح فرمائی تھی۔ عن ابن عباس قال صالح رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم اهل نجران على الفي حلة النصف في صفر والنصف في رجب يؤدونها الى المسلمين (الف) (ابوداؤد شریف ، باب فی اخذ الجزية ص نمبر ۳۰۴۱) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ حضور نے اہل نجران سے دو ہزار حلے پر صلح کی ، اور یہی جز یہ مقرر رہا۔

One type is that which is fixed by consent and peace, so it will be fixed according to what is agreed upon. Whatever amount the Commander of the Faithful and the dhimmi agree upon is permissible. The Prophet made peace with the tribe of Najran on two thousand suits of clothing. From Ibn Abbas: The Messenger of Allah made peace with the people of Najran on two thousand suits of clothing, half in Safar and half in Rajab, they pay them to the Muslims. (Abu Dawud, no. 3041). In this hadith, the Prophet made peace with the people of Najran on two thousand suits, and this was fixed as jizya.
Source pages p. 313

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement. It introduces the two types of jizya; here the first type is explained: jizya by mutual agreement. The Arabic matn states that when the Imam and the dhimmis agree on a jizya amount, it is valid. The Urdu sharh mentions that the agreement can be any amount; the example is the Prophet's treaty with Najran for 2000 suits (hulla) paid biannually. This shows that the amount is flexible, based on negotiation. The hadith from Abu Dawud is cited as proof. This first type is essentially a contractual obligation.

Key Terms
جزیہ (jizya): Poll tax imposed on non-Muslims (dhimmis) in exchange for protection and exemption from military service.
صلح (sulh): Peace treaty or settlement; here it means an agreement between the Imam and dhimmis on jizya amount.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) A mutual agreement between the Prophet and the people of Najran
C) A command from the Qur'an
D) The practice of the Rightly Guided Caliphs

Key Takeaway
Jizya can be imposed by mutual agreement, and the agreed amount is valid and binding, as demonstrated by the Prophet's treaty with Najran.

Jizya Amounts: Hanafi Gradation vs Shafi'i Flat Rate
Ruling on jizya amounts when Imam imposes unilaterally, with Shafi'i dispute.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on jizya amounts when the Imam imposes it, compare it with the Shafi'i view, and identify the evidence used (Quran and athar).

Core Idea
Jizya is graded by wealth in the Hanafi school — 48, 24, 12 dirhams yearly — based on 'Umar's practice, not a flat rate.

This lesson examines the second type of jizya: that which the Imam sets unilaterally after conquering a land and confirming the people in their possessions. The Hanafi school adopts a three-tier system based on the dhimmi's financial capability, while Imam al-Shafi'i holds a flat rate. We will walk through the evidence and reasoning behind the Hanafi position.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario
Understand that this applies when the Imam conquers a people, leaves them in possession of their properties, and imposes jizya without a prior agreement.
This is distinct from jizya set by mutual agreement.
2
State the Hanafi ruling and amounts
Memorize the three-tier system: wealthy 48 dirhams/year (4/month), middle 24 dirhams/year (2/month), poor 12 dirhams/year (1/month).
The amounts are in dirhams, not dinars.
3
Locate the primary evidence
The Quran (9:29) establishes the obligation of jizya. The specific amounts come from the athar of 'Umar ibn al-Khattab.
The Quran does not specify amounts; the athar provides the detailed division.
4
Understand the principle
The Hanafi school justifies gradation by the principle of ability to pay and equity, avoiding hardship on the poor.
This reflects the general spirit of Islamic law in considering varying capacities.
5
Compare with Shafi'i view
Imam al-Shafi'i holds a flat rate of one dinar (approx. 10-12 dirhams) for all, regardless of wealth. Note the practical difference (thamarah al-khilaf).
The Shafi'i view emphasizes equality over gradation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وجزية يبتدئ الامام وضعها اذا غلب الامام على الكفار وأقرهم على املاكهم فيضع على الغنى الظاهر الغناء فى كل سنة ثمانية واربعين درهما يأخذ منه في كل شهر اربعة دراهم وعلى المتوسط الحال اربعة وعشرين درهما في كل شهر درهمين وعلى الفقير الذي يعتمل اثني عشر درهما في كل شهر درهما
[۳۰۷۰ (۹۱) اور وہ جزیہ جو امام ابتداء مقرر کرے جب وہ غالب آئے کفار اور مالکوں کو ان کی ملکیتیوں پر برقرار رکھے تو ظاہری مالدار پر ہر سال اڑتالیس درہم مقرر کرے، اور اس سے ہر مہینے میں چار درہم لے۔ اور اوسط درجے کے آدمی پر چوبیس درہم ، ہر مہینے میں دو درہم ۔ اور مزدوری کرنے والے فقیر پر بارہ درہم، ہر مہینے میں ایک درہم۔
اگر کفار سے جزیہ کے بارے میں بات طے نہ ہوئی ہو اور امام کفار پر غلبہ کرنے کے بعد اپنے طور پر جزیہ مقرر کرے تو اس کی مقدار یہ ہو کہ جو اچھا مالدار ہے اس پر سالانہ اڑتالیس درہم اور ہر ماہ میں چار درہم وصول کرے۔ اور درمیانی حال والے پر چوبیس درہم ہر ماہ میں دو در ہم وصول کرے۔ اور مزدوری کرنے والے فقیر پر بارہ درہم ہر ماہ میں ایک درہم وصول کرے۔
جزیہ مقرر کرے اس کی دلیل یہ آیت ہے۔ قاتلوا الذين لا يـومـنـون بـالـلـه ولا باليوم الآخر ولا يحرمون ماحرم الله ورسوله ولا يدينون دين الحق من الذين أوتوا الكتاب حتى يعطوا الجزية عن يد وهم صاغرون (ب) (آیت ۲۹،سورة التوبۃ ۹ ) اس آیت سے معلوم ہوا کہ کفار پر جزیہ مقر کیا جائے گا (۲) اور مقدار کے بارے میں یہ اثر ہے۔ قال وضع عمر بن الخطاب في الجزية على رءوس الرجال على الغنى ثمانية و اربعين درهما وعلى الوسط اربعة وعشرين وعلى الفقير اثني عشر در هما (ج) (مصنف ابن ابی طیبه ، ۷ اما قالوافي وضع الجزية والقتال عليها ، ج سادس ، ص ۲۳۲، نمبر ۳۲۶۳۳ ر من اللبیہقی ، باب الزيادة على الدينار با صلح، ج تاسع ص ۳۲۹ نمبر ۱۸۶۸۵) اس اثر سے مقدار کی تفصیل معلوم ہوئی (۳) اس میں مالدار اور فقیر کی رعایت ہے کہ مالدار پر زیادہ ہے اور فقیر پر کم ہے۔
امام شافعی فرماتے ہیں کہ مالدار ہو یا غریب سب پر سال میں ایک دینار جزیہ مقرر کیا جائے گا۔
And a jizya that the Imam initiates when he overcomes the disbelievers and confirms them on their possessions: he imposes on the manifest wealthy forty-eight dirhams yearly, taking from him four dirhams each month; on the middle person twenty-four dirhams, two dirhams each month; and on the poor laborer twelve dirhams, one dirham each month. (Section 91) And that jizya which the Imam imposes initially when he overcomes the disbelievers and confirms them on their possessions: he imposes on the manifest wealthy forty-eight dirhams each year, and takes four dirhams from him each month. On the middle person twenty-four dirhams, two dirhams each month. On the poor laborer twelve dirhams, one dirham each month. If there is no prior agreement with the disbelievers about jizya and the Imam imposes it after victory, the amounts are as above. The proof for imposing jizya is the verse: Fight those who do not believe in Allah and the Last Day... (Al-Tawbah 9:29). From this verse it is known that jizya is imposed on disbelievers. (2) Regarding the amount, there is this athar: 'Umar ibn al-Khattab imposed jizya on heads of men: on the wealthy 48 dirhams, on the middle 24, on the poor 12.' (Musannaf Ibn Abi Shaybah, vol. 6, p. 232, no. 32633; al-Bayhaqi). From this athar the distribution of amounts is known. (3) In this, consideration is given to the rich and the poor: more on the rich, less on the poor. Imam al-Shafi'i says that whether rich or poor, one dinar per year should be imposed on all.
Source pages p. 314

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute within a ruling. It covers the second type of jizya: that imposed by the Imam unilaterally when he conquers a people and leaves them in possession of their lands. The Hanafi ruling, based on the practice of 'Umar, stipulates graded amounts: the wealthy pay 48 dirhams yearly, the middle class 24, and the poor 12. This is justified by the principle of fairness and ability to pay. The proof includes the Quranic verse (9:29) which orders fighting until jizya is given, and the practice of 'Umar. Imam al-Shafi'i holds that jizya should be a flat rate of one dinar (approx. 10-12 dirhams) for all, regardless of wealth. The Hanafi position considers the dhimmi's economic status to avoid hardship, while the Shafi'i view emphasizes equality. The text clearly presents both views, but the Hanafi position is given more evidence and is the relied-upon view in the Hanafi school.

Key Terms
مخالف (mukhalif): The opposing party, here Imam Shafi'i, who disagrees with the Hanafi view on jizya amount.
اثر (athar): A narration from a Companion, used as evidence for the jizya amounts.
جزية (jizya): A tax imposed on non-Muslims in an Islamic state in exchange for protection and exemption from military service.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the Hanafi view on jizya amounts for the poor (faqeer)?
A) One dinar per year
B) 12 dirhams per year
C) 24 dirhams per year
D) 48 dirhams per year

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school sets jizya at 48, 24, and 12 dirhams annually for rich, middle, and poor, based on 'Umar's practice, ensuring fairness.

The Hanafi Ruling on Jizyah Rates: Graduated According to Ability
Ruling on jizyah rates with proof and inter-madhhab dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on jizyah rates when imposed by the Imam and explain why the Hanafi school adopts graduated rates rather than a flat rate.

Core Idea
Jizyah is wajib and its amount is scaled by wealth: rich pay 48 dirhams, middle 24, poor 12 annually.

This passage from Kitab al-Siyar presents the Hanafi view on jizyah (poll tax) imposed on non-Muslims after conquest. The text distinguishes between jizyah by treaty (sulh) and jizyah imposed by the Imam (anwatan). For the latter, the Imam sets graduated rates based on financial ability, following the practice of 'Umar ibn al-Khattab. This lesson examines the ruling, its proof, and the debate with Imam al-Shafi'i.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Determine the act being ruled upon (jizyah) and its legal status (wajib). Recognize that the passage focuses on the amount when the Imam imposes it after conquest.
Jizyah is wajib on eligible non-Muslims for residence and protection.
2
Locate the dalil
Identify the proofs: Quran 9:29 establishes obligation; the practice of 'Umar sets the specific rates.
The Hanafi school relies on 'Umar's ijtihad as a strong precedent.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
Explain how the Quranic verse indicates obligation (command to fight until jizyah is given) and how 'Umar's practice is used as evidence for graduated rates.
The Quran provides general obligation; 'Umar's implementation is the specific application.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Identify that Imam al-Shafi'i disagrees, holding a flat rate of one dinar annually based on the hadith of Mu'adh.
The Shafi'i position is also based on a hadith, leading to a valid scholarly difference.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi tarjih
Understand why the Hanafi position is preferred: it considers ability, is more equitable, and 'Umar's practice carries weight in the school.
The Hanafi interpretation of the Mu'adh hadith is that it sets a minimum, not a fixed universal rate.

Source Text

كتاب السير
ضربين جزية توضع بالتراضي والصلح فتقدر بحسب ما يقع عليه الاتفاق . [۳۰۷۰] (۹۱) وجزية يبتدئ الامام وضعها اذا غلب الامام على الكفار وأقرهم على املاكهم فيضع على الغنى الظاهر الغناء فى كل سنة ثمانية واربعين درهما يأخذ منه في كل شهر اربعة دراهم وعلى المتوسط الحال اربعة وعشرين درهما في كل شهر درهمين وعلى الفقير المعتمل اثنى عشرة درهما في كل شهر در هما (۹۲) وتوضع الجزية حدیث میں ہے ۔ عن معاذ ان النبی الا الله لما وجهه الى اليمن امره ان ياخذ من كل حالم يعني محتلما دينارا او عدله من المعافري ثياب تكون باليمن (الف) (ابوداؤد شریف ، باب فی اخذ الجزیۃ، ص ۷۴ نمبر ۳۰۳۸) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ ہر مرد پر سالانہ ایک دینا لازم ہوگا چاہے مالدار ہو یا غریب۔ اعتمل : عمل سے مشتق ہے کام کرنے والا ۔
[۱۳۰۷۱ (۹۲) جزیہ مقرر کیا جائے گا اہل کتاب پر اور مجوسیوں پر اور عجم کے بت پرستوں پر۔
The Book of Siyar. Two types of jizyah: one placed by mutual agreement and peace, so it is estimated according to what the agreement falls upon. [3070] (91) And a jizyah that the Imam initiates its placement when the Imam overpowers the disbelievers and confirms them upon their properties, so he places upon the apparently wealthy rich person each year forty-eight dirhams, taking from him each month four dirhams; and upon the person of middle status twenty-four dirhams each month two dirhams; and upon the poor laborer twelve dirhams each month one dirham. (92) And jizyah is placed... there is a hadith that when the Prophet (peace be upon him) sent Mu'adh to Yemen, he ordered him to take from every adult, meaning a person who has reached puberty, a dinar or its equivalent from Ma'afiri garments that are in Yemen. (Abu Dawud, Chapter on Taking Jizyah, p. 74 no. 3038) From this hadith it is understood that every man must pay one dinar annually, whether rich or poor. I'tamala: derived from 'amal, meaning a worker.
Source pages p. 314

Commentary
This passage from Kitab al-Siyar discusses the two categories of jizyah (poll tax) imposed on non-Muslims under Islamic rule. The first type is jizyah by mutual agreement (sulh) during a peace treaty, where the amount is determined by the contracting parties. The second type is jizyah initiated by the Imam (ruler) after conquering the disbelievers and allowing them to retain their lands. In this case, the Imam sets graduated rates based on the subject's financial ability: for the wealthy (ghani) it is 48 dirhams per year (4 per month); for the middle class (mutawassit) it is 24 dirhams per year (2 per month); and for the poor laborer (faqir mu'tamil) it is 12 dirhams per year (1 per month). The passage then cites the practice of 'Umar ibn al-Khattab who implemented these rates, and notes that Imam al-Shafi'i disagreed, holding that jizyah is a flat rate of one dinar per year for all, based on a hadith of Mu'adh ibn Jabal. The Hanafi position relies on 'Umar's practice and the principle of gradualism and ease. The hadith of Mu'adh is interpreted by Hanafis as referring to a minimum, not a fixed amount for all.

Key Terms
جزية (jizyah): A poll tax levied on non-Muslim subjects in an Islamic state in lieu of military service and as a mark of submission.
غنى (ghani): Wealthy person who possesses apparent wealth (zahir al-ghina).
معتمل (mu'tamil): A poor person who works for a living (laborer).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, how much jizyah does a wealthy person (ghani) pay annually when the Imam imposes it?
A) 12 dirhams
B) 24 dirhams
C) 48 dirhams
D) 1 dinar

Key Takeaway
Jizyah imposed by the Imam after conquest is wajib and its amount is graduated: 48 dirhams for the rich, 24 for the middle, and 12 for the poor annually.

Categories of Non-Muslims Liable for Jizyah (Hanafi View)
Specifies the categories of non-Muslims liable for jizyah.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three categories of non-Muslims on whom jizyah is imposed according to the Hanafi school and explain why Arab idolaters are excluded.

Core Idea
Jizyah is imposed on ahl al-kitab, majus, and non-Arab idolaters, but never on Arab idolaters.

In the previous lesson, we discussed the general obligation of jizyah on certain non-Muslim subjects. This passage sharpens that rule by specifying exactly who qualifies: Jews and Christians (ahl al-kitab), Zoroastrians (majus), and non-Arab idolaters. The critical exception are Arab idolaters, who have no option of dhimmi status – they must either embrace Islam or face warfare. Understanding these categories is essential for correct application of jizyah rulings.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three categories
List the three groups mentioned in the opening sentence of the passage: ahl al-kitab, majus, and non-Arab idolaters.
2
Note the exception
Recognize that Arab idolaters are explicitly excluded from dhimmi status. The text says they cannot be kept as dhimmis.
3
Examine the proof for ahl al-kitab
The verse 9:29 is cited as evidence. Note that it is general for both Arab and non-Arab ahl al-kitab.
4
Examine the proof for majus
The hadith of the Prophet taking jizyah from the majus of Hajar is presented, showing that Arab majus are included.
5
Analyze the basis for non-Arab idolaters
Non-Arab idolaters are accepted by analogy and general practice, as the text implies they can become dhimmis.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
[۳۰۷۱ (۹۲) جزیہ مقرر کیا جائے گا اہل کتاب پر اور مجوسیوں پر اور عجم کے بت پرستوں پر۔
یہود اور نصاری اور مجوسی چاہے عرب میں رہتے ہوں یا نجم میں رہتے ہوں۔ اگر وہ ذمی بن کر رہنا چاہیں تو ان پر جزیہ مقرر ہوگا۔ اسی طرح عجم کے بت پرست ذمی بن کر رہنا چاہیں تو ان کے سروں پر جزیہ مقرر ہوگا۔ البتہ عرب کے بت پرستوں پر جزیہ نہیں ہے یا وہ اسلام لائیں یا قتل کے لئے تیار رہیں ذمی بن کر عرب میں نہیں رکھا جا سکے گا۔
اہل کتاب کے لئے جزیہ کے لئے یہ آیت ہے۔ قاتلوا الذين لا يؤمنون بالله ولا باليوم الآخر ولا يحرمون ما حرم الله ورسوله ولا يدينون دين الحق من الذين اوتوا الكتاب حتى يعطوا الجزية عن يد وهم صاغرون (ب)(آیت ۲۹، سورة التوبہ 9 ) اس آیت میں ہے کہ اہل کتاب یعنی یہودی اور نصاری سے اس وقت تک قبال کیا جائے جب تک وہ جزیہ نہ دینے لگیں۔ اور یہ عرب اور غیر عرب کے قید سے عام ہے اس لئے عرب کے اہل کتاب پر بھی جزیہ مقرر کیا جا سکتا ہے۔ مجوسی سے جزیہ لینے کے لئے یہ حدیث ہے۔ سمعت عمرا قال .... فاتانا كتاب عمر بن الخطاب قبل موته بسنة فرقوا بين كل ذي محرم من المجوس ولم يكن عمر اخذ الجزية من المجوس حتى شهد عبد الرحمن بن عوف ان رسول الله الله اخذها من مجوس هجر (ج) ( بخاری شریف، باب الجزية والموادعة مع اهل الذمة ، ص ۴۴۶، نمبر ۳۱۵۷٫۳۱۵۶ را بو داؤد شریف ، باب اخذ الجزية من المجوس، ص ۷۵ نمبر ۳۰۴۳) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ مجوس ہجر سے آپ نے جزیہ لیا۔ جس سے معلوم ہوا کہ عرب کے مجوس سے جزیہ لیا جا سکتا ہے (۳) عن ابن عباس قال صالح رسول الله الا الله اهل نجران على الفي حلة النصف في صفر والنصف في رجب يؤدونها الى المسلمين (د) (ابوداؤد شریف ، باب فی اخذ الجزیۃ ص نمبر ۳۰۴۱) اہل نجران عرب کے عیسائی تھے ان سے جزیہ لیا جس سے معلوم ہوا کہ عرب کے اہل کتاب سے جزیہ لیا جا سکتا ہے۔
حاشیہ : (الف) حضور نے جب حضرت معاذ کو یمن کی طرف متوجہ فرمایا تو ان کو حکم دیا کہ ہر بالغ سے ایک دینار لے۔ یا اس کے برابر معافری کپڑا جو یمن میں ہوتا ہے (ب) ان لوگوں سے جنگ کرے جو اللہ اور آخرت کے دن پر ایمان نہیں رکھتے۔ اور جس کو اللہ اور رسول نے حرام قرار دیا ہے اس کو حرام نہیں کرتے۔ اور اہل کتاب میں سے جو دین حق کو اختیار نہیں کرتے ان سے اس وقت تک جنگ کریں کہ ہاتھ سے ذلیل ہو کر جزیہ دینے لگیں ( ج ) ہمارے پاس عمر بن خطاب کا خط موت سے ایک سال پہلے آیا کہ مجوس کے ذی رقم محرم کی شادی ذی رحم محرم سے ہو گئی ہو تو اس کو جدا جدا کر دیں۔ اور حضرت عمر نے مجوس سے اس وقت تک جزیہ نہیں لیا جب تک کہ حضرت عبد الرحمن بن عوف نے گواہی نہیں دی کہ حضور نے ہجر کے مجوس سے جزیہ وصول فرمایا تھا ( د ) آپ نے اہل نجران سے دو ہزار صلے پر صلح فرمائی ، آدھا صفر میں اور آدھار جب میں اس کو مسلمانوں کو ادا کریں گے۔
[3071] (92) Jizyah will be imposed upon the People of the Book, and upon the Magians (Zoroastrians), and upon the idolaters of the non-Arabs. Jews, Christians, and Magians, whether they live in Arabia or in non-Arab lands. If they wish to live as dhimmis, then jizyah will be imposed upon them. Similarly, if the idolaters of the non-Arabs wish to live as dhimmis, then jizyah will be imposed upon their heads. However, upon the idolaters of the Arabs, there is no jizyah; either they accept Islam or be prepared for death; they cannot be kept as dhimmis in Arabia. For the People of the Book, this verse exists: 'Fight those who do not believe in Allah nor in the Last Day, and do not forbid what Allah and His Messenger have forbidden, and do not adopt the religion of truth from among those who were given the Scripture, until they give the jizyah willingly while they are subdued' (Quran 9:29). This verse indicates that jizyah is taken from Jews and Christians until they pay jizyah, and it is general for Arabs and non-Arabs, so jizyah can be imposed upon Arab People of the Book. For taking jizyah from Magians, there is this hadith: 'I heard 'Amr say... Then the letter of 'Umar ibn al-Khattab came to us a year before his death: Separate every close relative among the Magians. And 'Umar did not take jizyah from the Magians until 'Abd al-Rahman ibn 'Awf testified that the Messenger of Allah had taken jizyah from the Magians of Hajar' (Bukhari, Chapter on Jizyah and Truce with Ahl al-Dhimmah, p. 446, nos. 3157, 3156; Abu Dawud, Chapter on Taking Jizyah from Magians, p. 75, no. 3043). From this hadith, it is understood that he took jizyah from the Magians of Hajar, which shows that jizyah can be taken from Arab Magians. (3) From Ibn 'Abbas: 'The Messenger of Allah made peace with the people of Najran on the condition of two thousand garments, half in Safar and half in Rajab, which they pay to the Muslims' (Abu Dawud, Chapter on Taking Jizyah, p. no. 3041). The people of Najran were Arab Christians, and jizyah was taken from them, which shows that jizyah can be taken from Arab People of the Book.
Source pages p. 315

Commentary
This passage continues the discussion on jizyah by specifying precisely who is liable. According to the Hanafi school, jizyah is obligatory on three categories: (1) Ahl al-Kitab (Jews and Christians), regardless of whether they are Arab or non-Arab; (2) Magians (Zoroastrians), also regardless of ethnicity; and (3) idolaters who are non-Arab ('Ajam). The key exception is Arab idolaters: they have no option of becoming dhimmis by paying jizyah; they must either embrace Islam or face war. The evidence for taking jizyah from Ahl al-Kitab is the Quranic verse 9:29, which is general in its application. For Magians, the proof is the hadith of 'Umar accepting the testimony of 'Abd al-Rahman ibn 'Awf that the Prophet took jizyah from the Magians of Hajar (a region in Arabia). For non-Arab idolaters, the basis is the general principle and the absence of a prohibition, unlike Arab idolaters whose exclusion is based on the hadith 'Accept Islam or be killed' and the fact that the Prophet never made a peace treaty with Arab idolaters except on condition of Islam. The passage also cites the precedent of Najran (Arab Christians) to show that Arab Ahl al-Kitab are included. The footnotes elaborate on the hadiths and the rationale.

Key Terms
أهل الكتاب (Ahl al-Kitab): Jews and Christians who possess revealed scriptures.
مجوس (Majus): Zoroastrians or fire worshippers.
عجم (Ajam): Non-Arabs, regardless of ethnicity.
ذمي (dhimmi): A non-Muslim subject of an Islamic state who pays jizyah and enjoys protection.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, which of the following groups CANNOT become dhimmis by paying jizyah?
A) Arab Jews
B) Arab Christians
C) Arab idolaters
D) Non-Arab Magians

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, jizyah is imposed on all non-Muslims except Arab idolaters, who are not eligible for dhimmi status.
